thus whyles romaynes ſente theyr ambaſſadours fro hanniball ceaſſed whan weary ſouldiours releued ſelfes theyr peines trauayle encourage men againſt ennemies ſometyme hope victory ſometyme hope ryche townes countreys ¶ howe anniball paſſed riuer rhodanus put frenchman flight refuſed fyght conſul rome wordes couraged ſouldiours paſſe mountaynes cap viii thus annibal either feare money wynnynge countreys wente brought hoſte fielde volcanes ſtronge kynde people inhabyted ſydes water rhodanus doubtyng power carthaginenſes myſtruſtynge theyr owne ſtrengthe conueyed hadde ouer ryuer formoſte nyght withdrue hym campe reſted ſo ſoone wyſt mountayne men thoſe watched paſſage gone reſt made many great fyres leauyng cariage ſtuffe horſemen moſte part fotemen cāpe hym ſelfe great numbre lyght valiant men quikly paſſed ſtraites gate ſame hylles kepte nexte day hoſte ſtuffe beganne come mornyng mountayne men aſſembled go place wont doo whan ſawe enemy gotten caſtels place aboue heades feared harme theyr neyghbours wolde rather haue frendſhyp amitie prouoke wrathe carthaginenſes offeryng obey commaundementes ayde vytailes conducte hym people theyr way aſſuraunce thereof offered delyuer hym ¶ howe army rome carthage approched oration p c scipio conſul made • ncourage men fyght capit x anniballes commynge thoſe party found moch purpoſe taurine inſubres warryng one agaynſte coulde arme hoſte helpe one parte body ſo wery labour theyr clothes ſo foule fylthy ſome deſyred reſt theyr trauaile ſome ſought vitayles theyr hunger ſome taried chaunge apparayle make cleane theyr garmentes ſo ſoore handled paſſynge mountaynes thyng p cornelius scipio conſull perceyued well cauſed hym make ſpede army ryuer padus myght fight er refreſhed theyr great labour could haue time furniſhe army thoſe legion folowed fugitiue ennemye nowe bycauſe hoſte ſent ſenate rome spayne make warre vnder brother cneius scipio intent ſhulde haue bothe conſull capitayne agaynſte anniball carthaginenſes wyllyngly toke vpon warre newe capitayn new ſouldiours ſhuld vſe fewe wordes notwithſtandyng leſt ye ſhulde ignorant kind warre knowe whome ye ſhall fyght ye ſhall vnderſtand theſe ye ſhall haue laſte warres ye ſubdued bothe lande ſea ye toke truage perforce ſpace twenty yeres alſo wonne sardinia sicilia prey warre therfore battayle ye muſt haue ſame harte myndes wont conquerours ennemies muſte mountaynes whyche loſte two partes bothe horſemen footemen paſſynge ouer ſame mountaynes ſhulde haue nowe hope truſt thoſe fewe left haue loſte harte ſtrength ſo nowe ymages yea rather ſhadowes men men dede beinge clonged together hunger colde feynte febled emonge rocky hylles beſydes theyr ſynewes veynes ſhronke togyther colde ſnowe theyr membres wythered froſte yſe theyr harnies ſhaken ruſty brokē theyr horſes feble lame theſe enemy muſt fyght ye ar leuynges ennemies ennemies feare nothynge ſhall fyght foos ſhalbe thought mountayns haue fyrſt ouercome thē taken honour v ſo perchance neceſſary mete goddis without man helpe without battayle ſhulde ouercome truce breaker violated diſceyued ſhulde next goddis theyr myniſters bryng vtter confuſyon peraduenture many wyl ſuppoſe ſpeake theſe wordes proudly hyghly onely exhortation comfort ſhulde thynke otherwiſe ſelfe therfore ye ſhall vnderſtand ſent spayn myne owne prouince whether nowe going myne hoſt ſhulde haue vſed bothe felowſhyp counſayle brother peryls ieopardies ſhoulde haue fought rather haſdrubal leſſe power hanniball ſo ſhuld haue leſſe withſtandyng whan arriued ſhyppes beyonde coſteo fraunce landyng hearde anniball exhorted ſouldiours fight valiantly cap xi whyles scipio conſulle maner exhorted romaine anniball thynkyng fyrſt encourage men dedes wolde exhort theym wordes diſpoſed army compaſſe beholde fyght thanne brought middes mountayne men •• nnde whome taken priſoners layde alſo ſame place armour frenchemen whyche hadde ouercome cauſed one coulde ſpeake language inquere thoſe pryſoners whyche yf loſed theyr bondes wold take hors armour fight theyr line whan hadde deſyred armour battayle cauſed lotte caſte accordyng lotte loſed great number leapyng ſkypping theyr maner euery ſhortely toke armour beinge ioyfull glad dye honour lyue ſhame capti • itie incontinent called ſouldiours aboute hym made oration maner forme folowynge ¶ ye haue mynde remembrance example ſtrangers fortune longe paſſed ye ſhuld haue ſame euen nowe wayinge owne fortune chaunce haue ouercome battayle thoſe captiues wherfore ye muſt thynke theſe priſoners nowe ſhewed ſhewed ſpectakle beholde certayn reſemblance owne chaunce condition caſe ye nowe ouercome taken tell whether fortune hath gyuen greatter bandes vrgent neceſſitie hath gyuen heretofore theſe captiues two ſeas doo compaſſe bothe ryght hande lefte ſhyppes haue none eſcape awaye withall water padus aboute v violent ryuer rhodanus backes hygh mountayns ye paſſed ſo great peyn peryll wherfore louing ſouldiours ye muſt eyther ouer come ennemies valiantnes recouer agayne onely sicilia sardinia whiche wonne forefather might thought ſufficient reward caſe ſpede wel ſo euer romains haue goten ſo many victory triumphes dominion nowe poſſeſſe thus whan two conſuls met together al power rome aſſembled ageinſt anniball withſtanding one conſul beinge ab • ted fyrſt battayle ſore wounde wold rather prolong matter fight freſhe luſty therfore fierce wold haue delay thinking great honour vnto might recouer agayn conſul loſt wherfore ſayd man wold deferre battaile weaker harte body remēbrance wound refrain fighte alſo tyme ought prolonged inbuſſhement horſemen ſayde brother mago place ſhalt thou kepe thou ſhalte ſayde choſe vnto one thouſande horſemen oone thouſande fotemen beſt myn army lye theſe couert place whan tyme ſhal requyre cauſe al men dyne refreſhe ſelfes redynes againſt ſhuld called battaile sempronius bearyng rumour numidies brought army beinge deſyrous battayle ryuer whervnto reculed backe appointed anniball weather extremely colde ſhowed faſt ſouldiours hadde taken ſuſtenance made prouiſion ſtrength kepe theyr body warme colde froſt ſnowe haſte folowyng numidian theyr crafty ennemyes fledde theym entred ryuer nowe water ryſen nyghte reaſon ſnowe high theyr breſtis whan cam water theyr body ſo ſtark benommed colde ſcarſely could holde theyr armour vpon alſo towarde myddes daye beganne faynt hunger meane ſeaſon anniball cauſed great fyres made ſouldiours tentes euery man might warme alſo put oyle gloues whyche ſhoulde ſouple ioyntes membres whan hearde theyr ennemies paſſed ryuer beinge luſty bothe body harte euery man toke weapon went battayle anniball ordred battayles circumſpectly fyrſt ſette forthe thrower dartes whyche yles called baleares light harneyſed fotemen numbre viii footemen alſo abrode battayle footemen maynteyned ſeaſon • none reaſon horſmen elephantes alſo ſodayne commynge mago numidian fierſely aſſayled romaynes theyr backes ſtryken ſuche feare fledde partes ieoparded take water ageyne eſcaped theyr tentes fewe either drowned depe water el ſlayne theyr ennemies chaſe water ſyde many toke ryght way placentia therby ſaued ſyde carthaginenſes ſoo beaten rayne myxte ſnowe ouer ryuer trebia ſo placentia vnware carthaginenſes reaſon vehement ſtorme rayne felle nyght coulde remouyng elles peyne theyr woundes werynes labour dyſſembled matter toke hede ther thus roman conueyed peaſibly placentia then paſſed ouer padus cremona whan chance therof knowen rome aroſe ſuche ſo dayn feare among though theyr ennemies ben come alredy baners diſplayde gate rome neyther hope fierſe cruell ioy pride newe office onely lyttell feared lawe dignitie father ſenate alſo wanted feare immortall goddis fortune alſo nouryſhed foolyſhe hardynes proſperous ſucceſſe wel ciuile buſynes affayres home certain foreyn batayles ſo appered wente aboute thynges cruelly ouer haſtily nother counſaylynge goddis men howe moche redye folowe owne foly ſo moche buſyer anniball prouoke ſtere hym ſame wherfore leauing ennemies left hande went towarde feſſula intendyng diſtroy fieldes hetruria ſhewed conſull great waſte deſtruction ſpoylynge frendes myght bothe robbynge ſlaughter burnyng thintent ſhulde therby rather prouoked battayle flamminius owne nature gyuen buſy although ennemy wolde haue ben quiete reſt whan ſawe goodes frendes caryed awaye neyghbours bourned face thynkynge diſhonour vnto hym ſee anniball wander throughe myddes italy taking pleaſure without reſiſtence determyned incontinent gyue battayle although many men perſwaded hym ſhuld tary commynge felowe conſul ſo ſhulde counſayles hooſtes togyther procede vnto theyr enterpryſe agaynſte annibal meane tyme horſemen lyght harneyſed footemen lette hym frome robbynge deſtroyinge countrey contrary aduertiſement gyuen hym beinge angrye ruſhed forth counſel howſe quikly cauſed baners ſtanderdes dyſplayde lepte hym ſelfe vpon horſe incontinent hors ſodainly fell caſt conſull earthe whyche vnlucky begynnynge cauſed thoſe preſent greatly feare ſucceſſe therof ¶ battayle traſimenus deathe conſul flamminius many romayns cap xvi anniball whyle diſtroyed waſted cruell warre fieldes betwene citie cortona lake ſoo ſhoulde incloſed hemmed partes hauynge waye eſcape reaſon hylles greatte lake ¶ flamminius folowynge ennemies come aboute ſettyng ſonne lake next day early mornynge whan ſcarcely day lyght hoſte one ſyde whyche deſyred alſo compaſſed army ſide gaue ſigne men ſodeinly inuade ennemies commandement anon diligence executed rū nyng downe hylle aſſaylyng romanes partes one thyng moche amaſed romaynes ſodayne ſtraunge chaunge thereof aroſe frome brode lake myſte thycker darker hylles apparence whyche letted theym ſyght true knowledge maner theyr ennemies inuaſyon noyſe ſodayne affraye aroſe amonge theym perceyued theym ſelues betrayde hemmed battayle begonne bothe bothe ſydes coulde put good aray take theyr armor drawe theyr ſwerdes ¶ conſull flamminius whan people thus oppreſſed feare hym ſelfe man great courage lyttell affrayde ordered troubled company ſette order well tyme place wolde ſerue ſtyll exhortyng meanes myghte abyde fyghte ſhewynge theym booted theym praye call theyr goddis make vowes theym theyr delyuerance nowe waye theym eſcape ſtrengthe hardyneſſe way made ſwerd leſſe feare dydde take leſſe ieopardye perylle ſhoulde noyſe ſoo greatte wordes counſaylle capitayne coulde hearde ſo diſmayde ſkarſely knewe theyr ſtanderdes place repayre vnto hadde ſcante harte drawe theyr weapon theyr harneis rather burthen defence myght heare moche noyſe clamour thoſe wounded lyttell coulde ſee fled fleing hapned fall company romanes fought earneſtly ſtayed fleinge commynge towarde battayle diſcomfyture ſuche mette whyche fledde away diſcouraged fledde alſo laſte whan perceyued way eſcape felle earneſtly fyghtyng kepyng order oraray companyes happed theym falle togyther beganne battayle fyerce partes endured almoſte thre howres euery cruell moſte daungerous conſull ſtrengthe hoſte folowed hym ſo euer parte ſawe men daunger quyckly diligently reſcued beinge valiant bothe myghtyly aſſayled ennemies defended citezens vntyll one inſubria called ducarius violently thyckeſt ennemyes route ſleinge ſquyre whyche mette hym vnhappyly way afterwarde ſpeare ranne conſull body hadde ſpoyled hym ſtronge company romayne knyghtes withſtande hym deathe beganne roman flee al partes nother hylles lake coulde lette theym wandred blynd men ſtraites ouer rockes ſome fallyng one ouer whan coulde fynde none waye toke next way fennes runnynge water ouer head adioynyng apulia ſtyll robbynge ſpoylynge countreys abrode way went ¶ whan fabius romanes choſen hygh officer ſet thynge ſtay rome takyng army seruilius conſull alſo ii newe romayn legion encreaſyng army went mayſter horſemen minutius mete anniball ſtay hym deſtruction countrey fabius committing nothyng raſhely fortune eaſy iourneis good eſpies came feldes arpos pytchyng campe farre ennemies anniball ſoone cōminge brought people fieldes good aray redy fyght fabius al day kepte men campe whervpon anniball rebuking feble courage roman withdrew people tentes fearyng mynde ſobrenes fabius whiche capitayne choſen farre vnlyke sempronius flā minius neuertheleſſe proue faſcion conduicte fabius anniball oftentymes remoued campe euer ſpoyled countreys frendes romanes went sometyme wolde ſodeynly conuey army ſecretely tourne way lye awayte yf chaunce myght take ennemies auantage fabius euer ledde hoſte high place countreis ſtyll kepynge ennemies ſyghte ſo wolde farre theym yet intended giue battayle men went neuer theyr campe prouiſyon thynges neceſſary whan lacked vytailes forage woode ſent great numbre togyther myght walke ſurely alſo thoſe wente therfore ſuffered ſtray farre hoſte hadde euer horſemen lyght harneyſed footemen redyneſſe aray feare ſodayne inuaſions enemy alſo thintent ſhulde redy oppreſſe foe tyme ſhulde roue abrode ſpoyle vitailes mynded neuer ieoparde hole eſtate empire open battayl remayned ſtyl ſtay weary enemy whiche ſobrenes leſſe diſpleaſant anniball thā minutius maiſter horſemen beinge raſhe deſyrous put auenture fyrſt pryuily openly dyſprayſed ſlacknes fabius callynge hym bothe ſlowe fearefull anniball often remouing cam arpos samnium waſtyng fieldes beneuentanes toke towne tileſia truſtyng ſhewe ſoo moche diſpleaſure malice bourne ſpoile plentyfull countrey ryuer vulturnus ¶ tyme fabius come hilles toppe maſſicus mountayn romayns myght beholde carthaginenſis lodged fayre playnes vnder ceaſſed ſpoyle fieldes falernus burne houſes simeſſa diſpleaſure entred erneſtly hart minutius aboue maligned cowardiſe dictatour fabius oration full great inuectiues ſet hartis moſt part hoſt agaynſt hym theyr murmurynge fabius lyttell eſtemyng contynued reſte ſommer olde faſcion euer kepyng anniball battaile thyng moſt deſyred whan wynter began draw nere fabius perceiuyng countrey able ſuſteyne hoſt ennemies long ſeaſon none way paſſe fieldes falernus ſame ſtrayte wayes whych entred ſendyng ſufficient power roman hyll callicula towne caſilinus hym ſelfe mayſter horſemen kept narowe way whyche anniball muſt nedes paſſe anniball wylling proue maner kepyng ſtrayt came thyther made ſkirmiſhe romanes ſomewhat loſſe fayne recule backe perceyuynge roman haue samnite campanes frendes theyr backes redy ſuccour neceſſaries hoſte ſo encloſed like winter among ſtones formiana ſandes linterni forgatte renewe accuſtomed ſubtiltie craft inuented deceyte mockery fearefull men ſyght wherby myght paſſe ſtraites ſtelthe nyght cauſed rotten ſtyckes drye piece woode gathered togither fieldes fagottes yong roddes bowes made whych cauſed tyed horne ox kyne whiche taken pray countrey ſome wylde ſome tame ii thouſande beaſtis ſhuld thus ordred charge committed haſdruball ſhuld beginnyng darknes nyght ſette faggottes fyre horne beaſtes dryue theym hylles ſtraytes ſpecially aboue way roman kept begynnyng nyght ſecretely cauſed men remoue campe driuing ox lytel ſtanderdes whan came fote hyll narowe way commanded fagotes beaſtes horne ſet fyre whiche done feare flamyng fyre aboute theyr heades heate commyng quicke lower parte horne beaſtes cauſed runne though bene mad whyche ſodeyne running yong roddes toke burnyng euen though woddes hylles ben fire mouing heades cauſing flame ſprede abrode ſhewed like ben men rūning abrode fyre whan thoſe ſet entryng paſſage ſawe fyre hygh hylles aboue ſuppoſyng ben betrayde lefte place aſſigned theym kepe fiedde theyr ſuccours ſekyng theyr beſt way toppe hylles whiche great flame blaſe dyd ſhyne chaunced vpon certayne ox ſtrayed theyr flocke whan fyrſt ſawe liuing thinges breathynge fyre flame ſtode aſtonyed ſyght perceyuynge crafte made conueyd men ſuppoſing treaſon great noyſe rumour toke flyght fabius alſo ſeinge mockery fearynge deceyte kepte people within campe tyll day thus nyghte whyle aſtonyed ſtrange • yght anniball paſſed ſtraite carthaginenſes capitu xviii hard eſcape daunger anniball ledde army though wolde haue gone towarde rome fieldes samnite robbing burning vnto pelignes then returned towarde apulia fabius ſet tentys betwene citie rome ennemies nother goyng theym gyuinge battayle tyll ſhort ſpace called rome bycauſe ſacrifice ſhulde doone goddis departyng exhorted minutius mayſter horſemen lefte army alſo spanyarde treaſon conueyde pledg •• spayne fro carthaginenſes dely ••• ed roman ca xix sagunt noble ſpanyard called acedux tyme ben faythfull carthaginenſes facion many common ſort men whan fortune fayled faith lykewyſe chaunged imagined hym ſelfe way myght beſt attayne frendſhyp roman many ſundry imagination thought ſooneſt brynge might finde meanes delyuer thoſe noble men child whiche left sagunt pledge ſuerties meanes thought roman myght beſte wynne hartis pricis spain enterpriſe thought coulde compaſſe onleſſe myght obteyne fauour one boſtar lay encamped without citie vpon ſhoore ryuer good numbre spaniardes ſure kepyng citie ſtoppe romanes entre way hauen without whoſe cōmandement knewe well kepers pledge wolde nothyng acedux thought crafte aſſay boſtar went campe lay deſyryng ſecretely ſpeake hym fyrſt beganne ſhew hym daunger countrey conſyderyng ſtronge armye roman whiche hande ſhewed hym alſo spaniardes ſo longe continued frendeſhyp carthaginenſes feare loue cauſe romane army ſo farre theym nowe ſyns come ouer iberus feared leſte wolde yelde ſelues vnto scipio wherfore deſyred hym worke wyſely therin ¶ whan boſtar demaunded wold haue remedy therof anſwered wold aduyſe ſende child noble mē ye haue pledge towne parentes frendes city ſo ſhal ye get theyr harte loues kyndnes ſhewyng whiche ye neuer get feare whan fynde ye put truſt ye ſhall bynde faithful ſelfe wyll gladly take peyne delyuer agayne pledge theyr frendes ſo worke wyll get theyr harte moche ye nowe haue boſtar meanynge truthe playnnes anone perſwaded ſame purpoſe graunted hym conduite ſureties went acedux priuyly scipio tentes declared vnto hym good wyll bare towarde hym romanes appoynted hym tyme place delyuere pledge went acedux agayn boſtar receyued ſpeciall cōmandementes token kepers pledge go takyng pledge whan wold requyre theym ſhewed kepers chyldren wolde depart citie nyght thintente better eſcape danger watch roman hoſte wherfore wylled theym redy ryde hym whan called theym howre certayne night folowinge innocentes matter made thynges redye departe howre appoynted whyche howre fayled come thus departed cytie chyldren alſo kepers • ware ledde ayde roman whan ſo euer scipio commaunded theſe thynges doone spayne ſeconde yere battayl betwene carthaginenſes romaynes ¶ fabius rome diſpleſure minutius maiſter horſmen fighteth annibal putteth worſe therfore made halfe rular hooſte fabius fyghteth put flight reſcued fabiꝰ ca xx nowe let v returne fabius wyſe abſteining battayl ſaued many roman death neuer leſſe thought rome many hart failed trifled forth tyme onely thintent empire rule myghte longer contynue cared coſte citie infyndyng ſo great army ſo myght reſt honour thus gotten many enemy rome encreaſe malice towarde anniball wrought meruaylous ſubtyltie ſente numbre men ſpoyle cuntrey commaunded wyſe hurt landes fabius whiche gate knowledge certayne fledde hym roman army intent ſhuld thought ſom ſecret bargayn conſpiracy made betweene hym fabius whyche crafty act anniball cauſed fabius ſuſpect tothe ſenate rome take awaye ſuſpection hym fabius ſent ſonne ſolde grounde feldes whiche violated anniballes ſubtiltie nowe fortuned alſo encreaſe fabius euyll wyll rome departing hoſte minutius mayſter horſemen beinge lefte guyde armye cauſed campe tentes whiche fabius ſette ſafe hyghe hylles broughte downe pytched lowe valeys diſpoſed diſcretion capteyn thynkyng eyther make ſkyrmiſhe went abrode robbe el inuade thē left behind tētis ¶ anniball knowing ſhuld kepe warre captein moche vnlyke ennemies wolde order buſynes quyckly wyſely perceyuyng enemy draw nere vnto ſent thyrd part ſouldiors robbe waſt cuntreys ii partes kept within theyr tentes remoued campe nere romās abode vpō certain hyll roman hoſt might pceiue redy ſuccour robber aſſaut made thē purpoſe entiſe roman batail could minutius lōger forbere ſent good nūber horſmen aſſaile robber diſtroid many ſparkled abrode ſeking theyr pray cam annibal reſcue men fortune ſo ſerued romanes wer • moſt buſy fighting one numerius decimus capytain samnite cam ſuccour roman viii fotemen ii c horſmen whoſe help bet anniball cāpe ſlew vi men glad tydinges minutiꝰ although loſt ſame batell v owne men ſent boſting letter rome wherwith citie moch cōforted withſtanding fabius whan citie mery wold nother beleue newes letter laſt ſaid al trewe rather feared proſperous aduenture reioyſed therin whyche ſaying cauſed greatly hated citezens marcus metellus openly rebuked fabius therfore ſayinge kept men theyr campes lyke captiues priſoners men warre specially ſuffred preſent wold ſuffer nothing done valyantly agaynſt enemy alſo abſent held againſt thing well done maſter horſmē fabius anſwered fewe wordes thought ſhuld euyll harde ſayd ii yeres paſt citie ſuſteined great harmes loſſe foliſhe hardyneſſe gouernours douted yf myght beare rule haue mynde wolde make euident men fortune coulde lyttell worke againſt good captain wiſdom reaſon ſhuld haue dominion ouer al chance ſaid ſaued hoſt cruel enmy al perillous time without harme ſhame thought ought praiſed thā kyl great nūbre enmies concluſion determination ſenate attilius regulus ſhuld conſull plabe flāminius minutius maiſter horſemen ſo nobly gouerned army ſhuld halfe ruler hoſte fabiꝰ gouernāce therof parted betwene thē ¶ theſe diſpleſant actes ſenate fabius returned army truſtyng although minutius ſhoulde haue halfe rule hym yet ſhuld want policy maner ordryng part army cōmitted whiche policy exercyſe great tranayle obteyned minutius perceyuyng hym ſelfe ſuche eſtymation rome wel ſenators common lyttell proude beganne take moch hym boſtyng hym ſelfe theyr great calamitie alone founde captayne able matche anniball began diuiſe parting empyre rule wold haue ſo parted one day one weke ſhulde haue ruled one day weke fabius rule al ſo take hole gouernance tourne wolde fabius none wolde haue army parted betwene ordynances neceſſaries sayyng caſe coulde counſayle ſaue hole hoſte yet wold aſſay ſaue halfe therof wel myght poynt agreed thervpon deuyded theyr company legion alſo theyr campes debate order romayn capytayns knowen anniball eſpyes thinges done tentes ennemies whyche tydynges brought hym double ioye one thought vanquiſhe foolyſſhe hardynes minutius euen wolde hymſelfe halfe ſtrengthe fabius dymynyſſhed reaſone partynge hoſte thanne hylle betweene hooſte anniball hoſt minutius hyll ſo euer goten ſhuld able moche diſpleaſure enemy annibal deſyred ſo moche take without batayle although occupation therof ſhuld hym neceſſary make occaſion batail minutius wiſt wel wold euer run withſtande enterpriſe attaining therof fielde myddell betwene hym ſayd hyll whyche fielde playne fayre appeered moche vnmete treaſon hyde embuſhement bycauſe nother couered woode ſhrubbes buſſhes ſemed therfore place rather mete deſcry treſon hyde plaine bare valey ſuche deceyte myght feared anniball eſpied bottome ſayd hyll diuers caues holowe cowardyſe ſluggyſſhenes alſo theyr hardynes vertue el wold publius sempronius preſent yf folowed ſaue garde romane tentes captiues theyr ennemyes whan theyr enemyes weery fyghtynge alſoo reioycynge theyr vyctory mooſte parte theym retourned theyr tentes myght haue hadde nyghte free without interruption haue eſcaped veryly vii thouſande armed men myght haue eſcaped theyr ennemyes takyng ſo lytell hede truely nother wolde enterpriſe thynge theym ſelues folowe wolde take aduenture nyght longe almoſte sempronius ceaſſed admonyſhe exhorte ſhould folowe hym theyr capytayne whyles fewe ennemyes vtterly alienate frome ryght cytezens ye nowe made ſeruauntes vnto carthaginenſes wylle ye redemed ſrome thenſe whither wyllyngly went cowardyſe ſlowenes wyckednes wolde sempronius citezen whiche yf done father conſcript ye ſhoulde haue nowe xx ſtronge hardy ſouldiours cannuſiū nowe howe theſe accompted good faythful citezens bolde wyll call ſelfes whyche rather lye lurkyng theyr redemed thynke worthy yelded anniball whiche eſcaped theyr tentes myddell theyr ennemies theyr great hardines reſtored ſelues theyr countrey whan manlius fynyſhed oration al though many theym kynrede anniball entred italye many v alyue doo remembre yet howe varyable vyctorye fyrſte warres betwyxt carthage rome warres buſynes bothe ſea lande thought neuer proſperous thanne caius luctatius appius poſthumius conſuls yet theyr tyme ouercomme iles egates lykewyſe nowe yf fortune tourne ſhe always varyable whiche praye vnto goddis maye happen wolde ye hope haue peace whan ouercome whiche nowe hym marcus junius beyng dictatour beſydes legyons whyche appoynted bondemenne cytie ſuccours ſuche coulde gather togyther dyuerſe countreyes adioynynge fournyſſhe armye lepte beſydes horſe ſayinge ſuche haue commytted maner cryme worthye deathe condempned pryſon money yf wolde ſowldyours hym go warre wold pay theyr dettes loſe theyr handes punyſhement thus hadde ſort vi ſouldyours armed armor c flamminius toke frenchemen went citie xxv harneyſt men ¶ battayle betwene marcellus anniball citie nola annibals wyntryng capua delycate pleaſures wherby withdrewe harte courage men warrelyke faſcion cap xxviii anniball taken capua aſſayed many dyuers way haue gotten naples whiche whan coulde brynge paſſe went then fieldes nolans aſſayeng many way wyn towne nola ſenate namely chiefe ſtacke ſurely olde frendes romaynes cōmunes wont deſyrous newes inclyned anniball wherfore ſenate fearyng ſtryue common openly agaynſte whoſe power yfnede requyred able reſyſt priuyly diſſemblyng founde meanes prolong time ſaying cōtent yelded anniball knew maner condition ſhuld yelde whiche tyme delay ſent ambaſſadours marcellus pretor rome cannuſium ſhewyng hym circumſtance matter wylling come yf intended ſhuld kepe towne perceiuyng theyr ſtedfaſtnes greately prayſed ſenate nola deſyrynge perſeuere theyr purpoſe vſe ſuche ſubtiltie prolonging tyme done vntill commyng whych ſhuld ſhortly meane ſeaſon willed aknowen ſuccour commynge ſtreyght made hym redy army toke way calacia ouer riuer vulturnus ſo nola ¶ anniball pretor comming went nola naples deſyrous wynne ſome towne laye ſea coſtes whyche ſhyppes myght haue free ſafe paſſage affrica whan vnderſtode naples defended romane capytayne neapolitan gotten thyther iunius syllanus ſhulde well kept nola went layde ſiege nuceria whyche laſt vſynge many wayes cauſed famyne yelde marcellus tyme towne nola ſurer owne ſouldyours thanne pryncis nola feared common aboue dradde yonge man hardye noble lygnage whoſe name lucius bantius moche deſyrous yelde towne anniball beynge founde amonge heape dead body ſoore wounded battayle canna anniball cauſed hym healed ſent home large gyftes gentyll dede wold fayne nola ſhuld yelded anniball marcellus perceyued bantius troubled mynde ſuche ſtudy ſo muſt eyther punyſhement refrained orels benefit reconciled ſent hym ſo beninglye wordes promyſes gyftes entertayned hym none citie ſo ſure roman ¶ whan anniball come nuceria late taken gate nola marcellus entred citie fearyng kepe campe abrode leſt taryinge without ſhulde occaſyon betraying yeldyng vp citie beganne ſmall ſkyrmyſhyng betwene citie carthaginenſes whiche time pryncis nola ſhewed marcellus common people hadde ſecrete metynges communication nyghte carthaginenſes whiche purpoſed whanne roman gone fyght wolde take theyr ſtuffe cariage ſhutte gate ſo whan gotten bothe theyr ſtuffe goodes wold receyue carthaginenſes town ſtede roman whā ſhewed theſe conſpiracies marcellus praiſed theyr fidelitie greatly thought aſſaye myght battayle ſuche trouble ſhoulde within citie firſt ordered hoſte diuided thre partes iii gate whyche opened agaynſte ennemyes commaunded ſtuffe baggage folowe prety ſpace middel gate ſet ſtrēgth roman legion newe ſouldiours cam ſuccours ſette two gate ſtraightly commaundyng nolans wyſe ſhulde come walles nere gate ſent alſo certayn ſouldiours awaite cariage ſtuffe leſt whan buſy battaile nolanes myghte ſpoyle take whan thynges thus put good order ſtode ſtyll within walles without makyng ſhewe ¶ anniball ſtanding aray fieldes longe ſpace wont meruailed ſawe nother hooſte come fieldes man armed walles ſuppoſed theyr counſayle knowen feare cōmons towne conſtrayned forſake promyſe wherfore ſent part ſouldiours tentes fetche ordynaunce thynges neceſſary aſſault walles thynkyng went while abode ſtay common people citie wolde make ſome rumour walles incontynent whyles euery man cōmandement ranne buſines touchinge aſſault hoſt wente walles gate ſodeinly opened marcellus cōmanded ſpreade baners trumpettes blowe footemen fyrſt horſemen runne theyr ennemies author ſaye ſlayne ſkirmyſſhe ii iii c carthaginenſes one man roman whetherthe victory ſo great whether leſſe acte great conduicte noble anniball hauynge hope opteynyng towne went acerras marcellus ſtreyght cauſed gate nola ſhutte leſt manne ſhulde paſſe furthe made anon ſtrayght dilygent examination wolde haue betrayed towne beheaded lxxx cauſed goodes dyſtributed amonge common committed charge kepyng towne ſenate remoued hole hoſt beyonde sueſſala ¶ anniball hadde wonne acerras came caſſilinum ſo valyantlye defended theym ſelfes anniball beinge halfe aſhamed left ſiege wente wynter capua kepte hooſte houſes moſt part wynter long tyme endured agaynſt kyndes peynes trauayle hauynge ſmalle knowlege pleaſure eaſe could ouercome kynde miſery peyne loſte vnmeaſurable pleaſures wherein wholly drowned ſo gredy therof theyr accuſtomed peynes thus toke al theyr delite ſlepe wyne bankettes hauntynge harlottes bathe dayly reſte ydelnes whiche delycate faſhion withdrewe bothe theyr courage alſo theyr ſtrength theyr body myndes ſo afterwarde theyr ioye comfort ſtrength remembrance victory whiche opteyned theyr preſent ſtrength ſo moche lette ſouldiours thus folow theyr luſtes thought amonge expert warriours greater hynderance vnto hym lead hoſt rome ſtreight battayle canna tarienge doubting thought prolongyng victorye faute made theym vnable afterwarde ouercome soo whan remoued capua winter ſemed ledde furthe ſtraunge army brought thyther obſerued none theyr accuſtomed ſort warre ſomme retourned theyr harlottes many ſoone beganne feele peyne trauayle hardeneſſe warre fayne couered ſkynnes ſo werye warre ſemed ſo tediouſe wanted bothe theyr ſtrength bodye hardyneſſe mynde whyche hadde greatte parte hoſte without theyr wage ſtole theyr capytaynes nother hadde denne receptable capua ¶ longe ſiege wynnynge caſſilinum deathe diſtruction conſull poſthumius hoſt woode lytana craft frenchemen cap xxix vvhan drewe towarde ſommer anniball remoued agayne caſſilinum without aſſaute gyuynge contynuall ſiege kepynge broughte inhabita • te therof almoſte extreme ponertie famyne dictatour ſeaſon gone rome ſerche diuinations fortune ſhulde happen titus sempronius left ruler army marcellus nola wolde haue ſuccoured caſſilinum ſaue citezens nola wolde caſe ſuffer hym go theym fearynge leſte departure inhabitantes capua wolde haue inuaded theym ryuer alſoo vulturnus ryſen ſo hygh coulde well paſſe ouer great ieopardy gracchus lefte certayne men warre lye caſſilinum moued brought ſuccour bycauſe hadde commandement dictatour ſhulde moue battayle abſence yet hearde ſuche newes caſſilinum whyche wolde haue moued man haue broken commandement ſhewed hym ſome able ſuſteyne greatte hungre famine without aduyſement diſtroid ſelfes ſome deſyryng death wold ſtand walles without armour intent myght ſlayn ſhotte theyr ennemies gracchus ſeyng durſte helpe theym battayle bycauſe contrary cōmaundement dictatour remedy brynge ſuſtynance caſe coulde done without battayle gathered fieldes many kyndes corne could therwith fylled great numbre veſſels barelles ſent meſſanger rulars citie certifying wolde next nyght ſende veſſels grayne downe water warning redy receiue theym cōmyng tyde nyght folowyng euery man went ryuer tary cōmyng grayn accordyng promyſe gracchus laſte myght ſee tounnes come ſwymmynge downe myddell ſtreame whiche receyued gladly diuyded equally among thus continued ſpace iii iiii nyghtes ſo longe diſceyued watchemen theyr ennemies laſte water aroſe moche hygher wont reaſon continuall rayne fell ſo ſtreame ſwyft wont whereby veſſels dryuen lande part hoſt anniball lay many founde ſtyckyng amonge wyllowes grew bankes ryuer ſhewed vnto anniball afterwarde greatter dilygence watched ryuer vulturnus leſt ſhuld ſuch meanes eftſones deceyued yet ſuche lyke deuyſe made ſendyng nuttes downe ſtreame barels tyll alſo eſpyed length brought ſuche pouertie conſtrayned take ſkynnes ſtrynges couerynges ſhieldes whiche made ſofte warme water ſo eate nother refrayned eate myſe ſuche kynde vermyn kynde herbes rootes whiche grewe without fielde adioyning walles thus alſo perceyued anniball wherfore cauſed grounde plowed vp ſuche herbes rootes dyd growe ennemies ſuccour without wall whiche newe plowed groundes men towne ſowed paſnepſede wherat anniball cried shall tary caſſilinum whyle theſe ſedes growen vp able theyr foode ſuſtynance whervpon wolde cōmunication truce contented couenant theyr redemption price redemption vii ounce golde euery theym whan couenantes made yelded ſelues kepte pryſon vntylle money payde ſent good leaue cumas came preneſte garyſon caſſilinū v c ſeuenty ſouldiors whiche moſte part ſlayne famyſhed reſidue went preneſte capitayne manicius caſſilinum giuen citezens capua kept vii c anniballes ſouldiours leſte whan departed then roman ſhulde take agayn ſenate rome appoynted double ſtypende ſouldiours preneſte alſo gaue fiue yeres licence abſent warres theyr great fidelitie roman buſy choſyng newe ſouldiours ſupply theyr place ſlayne batayle lucius poſthumius titus sempronius choſen conſulles dictatour whan offycers choſen went theanū army wyntred left maiſter horſemen rome anone receyued office counſayled father choſing ordeyning army yere whan mooſte diligent aboute theyr bulines tydynges brought citie newe ſlaughter loſſe happed vnto theym oone euylle chaunce yere commynge truth lucius poſthumius armye dyſtroyed france meane great wyde woode called frenchemen litana ſhuld leade hoſte whiche woode frenchman ſo cutte tree bothe ſydes waye yf moued wolde ſtande ſtylle beinge thynge moued wolde anon fall poſthumius hoſte fyue twenty thouſande men frenchemen hadde beſtowed companye rounde aboute compaſſe woode whan armye romaynes welle entred woode caſt downe fartheſt part tree growynge border woode whan moued fell one vpon woode hauyng ſtay throwyng downe ſleing roman paſſed bothe men horſes ſo ſcarſely tenne men eſcaped moſte part almoſte paſte breathe deade hurtes tree fallynge reſidue eſcaped wolde haue fledde beinge amaſed ſodeyne chaunce ſlayne frenchemen beinge armed beſet tho woode rounde taken ſought goo ouer brydge whiche frenchemen kepte anone compaſſed beſet frenchemen conſull poſthumius wyſe wolde taken ennemyes manfully nobly dyed brought ornamentes bodye heade beinge cut body chiefe temple countrey ſyngyng moche myrthe pourged clenſed ſkull within without couered brayne panne ouer golde vſynge drynke therin whan dyd ſacryfice ſolemne feaſt alſo ſerued prieſtes biſhoppes temple cuppe ſacrifice praye leſſe frenchemen thanne victorye although moſt parte cattall ſlayne fallyng tree yet loſt nothyng ſubſtance ¶whan ſlaughter knowen rome citezens ſuche ſorowe trouble great ſpace ſhutte wyndowes ſhoppes though ben nyght within ſhort ſpace ſenatours charged officer go citie cauſe ſhoppes doores opened cauſe citezens leaue ſorow ¶than titus sempronius called ſenate courte exhorted counſailed father conſcript whoſe harte ouer come great diſtruction loſſe battayle canna ſhulde nowe ſuffer ſelues vanquyſhed moche leſſe ſorow calamitie admonyſſhynge theym concernynge carthaginenſes anniball truſted ſhuld well warres frenchman myght deferred ſeaſon tymes reuengynge theyr harmes power goddis romayns furthermore ſhewed theym ought chiefly counſayle worke agaynſt anniball circū ſpectly preparyng numbre men might reſiſted fyrſte reaſoned numbre footemen horſemen citezens theyr frendes italy hoſt dictatour marcellus declared nūbre army charge thus ymagyned decreed numbre ſhulde ſatiſfye two conſuls hoſtes agreed warre agaynſt frenchemenne ſhoulde omytted vntyll tyme ¶of victory scipions spayne cap xxx vvhyles theſe thinges done prepared italy romayne capytaynes spayne ydell vpperhande ennemies p scipio c scipio brother parted army betwixt theym ſo cneius ſhoulde haue lande publius ſea great warre spayn betwene scipions haſdruball whan knowen spayne haſdruball ſhuld go hoſt italy great numbre turned theyr harte roman wherfore haſdrubal ſente letter carthage certifieng senate howe dangerous departyng spayne ſhuld paſſed ryuer iherus part spain wold tourne roman whiche letter although fyrſt moued ſenate moche withſtandyng bycauſe theyr hole myndes gyuen toward charge buſines affaire italy chāged purpoſe conferryng ſendyng haſdruball italye place ſent himilco hoſte fournyſſhed kepe ſeas lande alſo countrey spayne whan thynge neceſſary prouyded hym great ſpede myght paſſed countrey spayne vntyll came haſdruball ſoone ſhewed hym commaundement ſenate haſdruball likewyſe informed hym howe ſhulde demeane hym ſelfe warres spayne retourned agayne tentes ſpede haſdrubal er euer remoued campe cauſed tax money rayſed cuntreys vnder obeyſance knowyng well anniball bought certayne paſſages frenchemen withoute theyr helpe entre alpes hyghe mountaynes harde optained whan gathered greate ſummes money went downe ſpede riuer iberus ¶ whan purpoſe carthaginenſes haſdrubals iourney knowen ſhewed scipions ſettyng buſynes aparte bothe theyr hoſtes togyther ſet forwarde mete hym prepared lette enterpryſe ſuppoſynge yf haſdruball capitayn great newe hoſte carthaginenſes ioyned anniball alone italy ſcarſely able withſtande empyre rome ſhoulde ſoone ende thus beinge troubled care buſynes brought theyr hooſte iberus whan paſſed ryuer conſultynge longe whether ſhoulde pytche theyr campe neere theyr ennemies elles ouerrunne ſubdue ſome carthaginenſes frendes therby ſtaye prolonge theyr ennemies purpoſed iourney laſt determyned beſiege citie called ibera water whiche nere rycheſt countrey tyme whiche thyng whan haſdruball knewe ſtede bryngyng ſuccour frendes wente beſiege citie lately yelded roman ſo roman left liege turned battayle wholly haſdruball betwixt two hoſtes ſpace certayn dayes ſpace fyue myles duryng whiche tyme without ſmall ſkyrmyſhyng length pretended bothe partes one tyme bothe hole hoſtes diſcended playne redy gyue battaile roman hoſt diuided thre partes part footemen ſette ſtanderdes part behynd horſemen kept ſydes wynges part haſdruball ſette myddell battayle spaniardes right wyng carthaginenſes left winge affricans hyred ſtraunge ſowldiours put numidian footemen carthage reſidue affricanes ſette wynges nother dyd ſette numydians ryght wyng thoſe whoſe quality ſuche lyghtnes nymblenes rydyng vpon one horſe leadyng ſpare horſe theyr handes whan one wery wold among thickeſt enemyes leape armed freſhe horſe theyr agilitie quycknes ſo great horſes kind ſo gentil wel taught thus ſtode aray litel difference numbre kyndes ſouldiours eyther hoſte withſtandyng ſouldiours harte like romane capitayns although fought farre home yet myght eaſyly perſuade ſouldiours ſhuld fyght theyr cuntrey citie rome wherfore doubtfull battaile purpoſed ouercome dye truſting therby haue ſhort returne home cuntrey hooſte hadde ſo ſterne valiaunt hardy men parte theym spanyardes whiche rather ouercome spayne wynnynge victory conducted italy therfore fyrſte metynge whan dartes ſcarſly throwen middell warde fledde gaue place romanes came vpon great violence withſtanding battailes nothynge leſſe wynges one ſyde carthaginenſes ſyde affricans came boldly fought egerly whan romane hoſte gotten myddell togyther ſtronge ynough put away wynges theyr ennemies wherefore numbre ſtrength beſt ſhortly put worſe great numbre men ſlayne vnleſſe spaniardes fledde away ſo thicke battayle begunne hadde ſcarſely theym remayned vnſlayne bataile betwene horſe men ſoone mauritaynes numidian ſawe myddell warde ouercome putte flyghte dryuynge elephantes theym ſodaynly departed fledde leauynge bothe wynges bare haſdruball remainyng tyll laſt ende battaile fledde fewe hym battayle cauſed harte spanyardes whiche doubted frendſhyp romanes wholly gyuen dyd take hope haſdrubal leading hoſte italy alſo ſcarſe tarieng hym spayne thinges certified ſenate rome scipions letter ſo gladde victory haſdrubal hoſt prohibited entre italy ¶ oration samnite hirpines anniball deſyrynge helpe againſt romaine order marcellus anniball nola cap xxxi vvhyles theſe thynges done spayn romanes ordered theyr buſines wyſely italy titus sempronius quintus fabius maximus choſen conſuls marcellus laye nola made dyuers runnynges armye fieldes hirpines samnite ſo dyſtroyed ſwerde fyre renued memorye olde diſtruction samnium ſtrayght wayes bothe nation ſente theyr meſſangers anniball one ſpake hym maner ¶ anniball ennemies romayns ſelues longe weapon harneys ſtrengthe able maynteyne v afterwarde whan ſmalle hope truſte theym fell amitie pyrrhus whome forſaken beinge able defende v toke truce peace neceſſary vnable withſtande romaynes haue endured ſame peace ſpace fyfty yeres vnto thy commyng italy sen whyche tyme thy onely gentylnes towarde cytezens whiche beynge taken thou ſendeſt v agayne well thy vertue fortune ſo hathe wonne v vnto yf thou frende ſafe good helth wolde feare roman alſo yf laufull ſpoken wold feare goddis verily thou ſafe ſounde alſo preſent thou mayſt alſo beholde houſes burnynge waylyng wyues chyldren ſo ſpoyled goodes waſted dyſtroyed may thoughte marcus marcellus hath ouercome canna anniball alſo romaynes may reioyce thou onely one battayle art ſtronge valyant next wethered faynt kepte warre romaynes ſpace one hundred yeres beyng ſuccoured man ſauyng pyrrhus ſpace ii yeres increaſe ſtrengthe power men rather defende v power wylle reioyſe proſperitie whan ſubdued ii conſulles theyr hoſtes one time brought ſubiection omytting ſuche proſperous chaunces myghte ſhewe thoſe thynges happed infortunately v tyme yf leſſe ſhame maye nowe declare thoſe chaunced v dydde inuade coſtes countreys tyme ii noble dictatours mayſters horſemen two conſulles two conſulles hooſtes hauynge thynge prouyded theym neceſſaryly wolde aduenture robbe dyſtroy countrey nowe almoſte praye one lyttell hoſte beynge lefte ſuccours nola nowe beynge ſmalle noumbre maner robber ouercome countreye leſſe feare thanne yf romayne fieldes cauſe nother thou doeſte defende v alſo luſtye yonge valyaunt menne whiche without doubt yf home wolde defende v vnder thy baner neyther knowen thyne hoſte hadde happed thy myght ſoo many roman ſlayne put flyght whome may ſuppoſe lyght thyng ſuppreſſe robber ronyng abrode fieldes without order runnyng whyther foolyſſhe vayne hope pray dothe leade theym whome fewe thy numidian wolde vtterly confounde doubte thou wylte ſende v ſome ſure helpe ſuccour excepte thou iudge v vnworthy defended holpen whan heretofore thou thoughteſt v vnworthy taken thy frendes companyons receyuyng v thy amitie frendſhyppe ¶ theyr lamentable oration anniball anſwered hirpines samnite dyd ſhewe ruine loſſe requyryng helpe therein alſo dyd complayne lefte withoute ſuccour vnholpen one ſhulde fyrſt haue ſhewed theyr cauſe aſkynge ſuccour theyr myſchiefe afterwarde yf coulde haue healpe complayne theyr ſuite vayne neuer leſſe promiſed ſuccours helpe army ſhuld come theyr groundes wolde inuade theyr neyghbours whiche frendes romaine wherby ſhulde drawe roman vexyng makyng gladde defende theyr frendes concernyng warre betwene romaynes yf battayle traſimenus nobler trebia battayle canna noble traſimenus wolde make fame memorye victory canna obſcure nothyng eſtemed compariſon noble triumphant victorye truſted haue anſwere great rewardes ſent home leauyng lyttell company tiſatis toke iourney nola ſame tyme hanno came hym bruſians ſtuffe ſent carthage elephantes ¶ whan anniball pytched tentes farre frome nola founde thynges otherwyſe ſhewed hym legate samnite marcellus ſo ruled hym ſelfe euer men cōmitted nothinge fortune nother left thyng raſſhely daunger ennemyes whan went ſpoyle countrey gette pray dyd prouidently though ſhuld haue done anniball beinge preſent whan perceiued anniball become kept hoſte within citie whervpon hanno approched nygh vnto wall callynge furthe herennius baſſus herius petreius lycence marcellus went furthe talke hym vnto interpretour beganne extoll vertue fortune anniball diſpiſed nobilitie roman ſayd decayed togyther theyr power ſtrength whyche nobilitie power yf lyke olde tyme withſtandyng knowynge harde cruell empire gouernance roman great gentylnes anniball towardes captiues italy frendſhip amitie carthaginēſes preferred amitie roman yf conſuls theyr hooſtes nola cōpared anniball battell canna moche leſſe one pretor fewe new vnſkilled ſouldiours able defende nola rather anniball oughte care maner nola ſhuld come anniballes poſſeſſion taken violēce yelded remedy haue wold capua nuceria ſayd wolde diuine ſhuld happen citie taken durſte rather promyſe vndertake wold yelde marcellus citie anniball man theym ſelues ſhulde preſcribe bandes lawes frendeſhyp ſhulde betwene ¶ whervnto herennius baſſus aunſwered amitie betwene romanes nolanes continued many yeres whiche nother dyd forthynke ſaid furthermore ſhuld haue changed broken faithes whan theyr fortune fayled chaunged nowe late chaunge chaunged long time agone ben foly haue ſought ſuccour romaynes bene mynded haue yelded towne anniball wherfore theyr myndes thoſe whiche came theyr ſuccours thynges ioyned ſurely knitte togither deth ſhulde whiche anſwere toke anniball hope optayuynge citie without battayle wherfore beſette citie rounde intendynge gyue aſſaulte thervnto partes ¶ ſoone marcellus ſawe hys ennemies approched walles ordered hooſte wyſely within walles ſodeynly iſſued batayle makyng great noyſe fyrſte encountrynge dryuen backe ſlayne whan army ioyned togyther battayle beganne fierſe bothe partes faile bena ſoore ſyght huge tempeſt raine departed theym wherby hauynge bothe egre myndes one dryuen towne campe tentes lyttell hurt done beynge bothe deſyrous battayle abode next daye ſo great violence ſtorme thyrde day anniball ſent parte ſouldiours robbe ſpoyle fieldes whan marcellus knewe ſtreight way brought hoſte furth battayle anniball ſyde nothinge behynde almoſte myle betwene towne campe two hoſtes mette togyther crye rayſed bothe partes cauſed companye returne battayle ſent ſpoyling nolans power ready increaſe romanes hoſte whome marcellus greatly prayſynge theyr good wylles courage commaunded ſtande aray redy theyr ſuccour conuey wounded battayle ſhoulde wyſe fyghte vntylle commaunded theym battayle ſtronge ſowldiours fought theyr myghtes lykewyſe capytaynes prouoked theym ſame marcellus badde boldely withſtande thoſe ouercomme thre dayes longe agone fledde cuma vacabundes yere dryuen nola beynge capytayne comforte theym ſayde theyr enemyes battayle ſome rouynge fieldes thoſe fought battayle wethered pleaſure capua wyne hauntynge harlottes ſtrengthes courage myghte theyr bodyes harte whyche paſſed greatte mountaynes called alpes hylles pyrene cleane goone ſayde alſoo thoſe leauynges foreſayde ſowldyoures ſcarſe able beare ſuſteyne theyr owne membres harneys ſhewynge capua hurtfull diſpleaſaunt vnto anniball menne canna romaones ſayde haue lefte theyr ſtrongthe vertue good feates warre yea haue lefte onely theyr glorye fame tyme paſt alſo hoope victorye tyme come ¶ exhortation anniball ſowldiours batayle betweene hym marcellus victory scipions spayne capitulo xxxii whan marcellus ſuche wordes ennemies reproche incouraged ſowldiours anniball lykewyſe leſſe rebuke blame romanes called men ſayinge knewe theym haue ſame armour ſtanderdes whyche hadde trebia traſymenus canna meaneth nowe ſaythe ye ſcarſely able withſtande one legate romayne battayle one legyon wynge two conſulles hooſtes neuer able withſtande shall marcellus newe vntaught ſouldyours ſuccours nola yet agayne prouoke v reuenged vpon ſouldyours drewe flamminius horſe ſtrake heade ſlewe lucius paulus canna ſwerdes blunte youre ryghte handes aſtonyed wearye monſtrouſe thynge whyche wonte whanne ye verye fewe noumbre ſhorte ſpace ouercome great meyny nowe beinge many ſuffer fewe ſtycke handes boſted bolde men tongue wold wynne rome yf man wold bryng thyther behold nowe buſines moch leſſe wolde ye wolde proue ſtrength hardyneſſe wynnyng nola citie countrey ſet playne fieldes beinge compaſſed nother fludde ſea ſhall leade folowe beyng laden ſo ryche pray place ſo euer wyll ¶ notwithſtandyng neyther theſe reproches entiſynges coulde preuayle ſtrength theyr harte beaten backe ſydes harte romanes dyd encreaſe onely theyr capytaynes exhortinges alſo nolanes ſteryng kyndlyng theyr courage batayle length carthaginenſes fledde dryuen backe tentes marcellus brought ſouldiours nola great ioye thankes people whoſe harte moſt inclined carthaginenſes ſlayne day aboue theyr ennemies one thouſande vi c taken ſtanderdes baners xx iiii elephantes ſlayne battayle romanes ſlayne nexte daye truce taken whyche ſpente buryinge deade bodyes marcellus made oblation vulcan ſpoyle ennemies within thre dayes eyther diſpleaſure hope wage ii c lxxii numidian horſmen spanyardes fledde anniball marcellus whoſe faithfull ſtronge helpe aide romanes vſed bataile often tymes anniball ſent hanno agayne bruſians hoſte brought hym then went hym ſelfe wynter apulia lay arpos ¶ ſoone quintus fabius harde anniball gone apulia brought corne moche thought neceſſary ſerue winter nola naples campe sueſſula leauyng ſufficiente garry ſon moued campe nygh vnto capua burnyng ſpoylyng theyr fieldes ſo capua conſtrayned truſtyng lyttel theyr owne ſtrength come citie encampe ſelues walles fortifyeng munimentes without gate vi ſouldiours armed coulde better ſkylle horſebacke foote wherfore horſemen euer prouoked theyr enemy ſkyrmyſhyng soone quintus fabius conſull remoued tentes backe campanes myght tyll ſowe theyr grounde nother dyd come thyther agayne diſtroye fieldes campanes new corne come vp good height able fother theyr cattall came thyther agayne cauſed gathered broughte claudius tentes aboue sucſſula prouided wynter cōmaundynge marcus claudius leauynge neceſſary garriſon nola defence therof ſhuld ſend reſidue ſowldyours rome leſte ſhuld bothe charge theyr frendes coſte common wealthe ¶ ende ſommer whan theſe thinges done came letter scipions great proſperous actes done spayne theyr money grayne clothynge theyr ſouldiours ſea men ſpente whiche beinge pondered senate thynges neceſſarye ordeyned ſente whan theſe ſtipendes neceſſaries come spayn towne illiturgus beſieged haſdruball mago amilcar ſonne bomilcar angre changed harte yelded roman neuertheleſſe thorough theſe thre hoſtes scipions valiantly entred towne theyr frendes without greate fyght ſlaughter bryngynge theym grayne good plentye wherof great nede exhorting citezens ſo valiantly kepe defende theyr towne perceiued romaynes fyght sone iſſued aſſayle great campe wherof haſdruball capitayn thyther came ſuccours two capitaynes carthaginenſes theyr determynation ſpake olde q fabius ſayinge oughte conſyder peryllous tyme warre ſo procede loſe none theyr faythfull frendes occaſyon example dyd ſhewe meanes poſſible yf frendes fallen fynde meane part towne ſowne horne gyue hym knowlege wherby reſte hooſte might approche theyr ſuccour deuiſe ſpede executed chaunce ſuche one thynge whiche thought wolde greate let theyr purpoſe beſt holpe
