gate theyr entre diſcried anniballes men towne v ſouldiours towne alſo armed iii thouſande men whyche townes men carthaginenſes cauſed go front battaile myſtruſtynge haue behynde backes littell ſkyrmyſhyng ſtretes dyuers townes men arpos certayne romanes whyche acquayntaunce beganne common talke togyther fyrſt ſpake roman ſayd ye men arpos ye meane take part theſe barbarous nation againſt cuntrey men wherin haue roman offended haue carthaginenſes deſerued vnto ye ſhuld thus trauail make italy ſubiect tributary affrica arpins excuſed ſelues ſaying betrayed ſold captain carthaginēſis almoſt vtterly diſtroyed theyr communication ſtayed fyghtyng certayn ſpace pretor gouernour towne brought men conſull ſo well agreed incontinente arpines toke part roman againſt carthaginenſes alſo towne thouſande spanyardes lykewyſe tourned romanes fyrſt opteyned conſul garriſon carthaginenſes might freely depart towne go liberty whiche truely performed departed salapia annibal towne incontinent deliuered romanes without loſſe theyr army ¶ scipions ſpace broughte theyr buſyneſſe proſperouſly paſſe spayne bothe conſeruyng theyr olde frendes gettynge newe beſydes ſodeynly comforte good affrica reaſone one syphax kyng numidia thā become ennemy carthaginenſes kynge ſent iii legate ſhuld bring amitie roman alſo cauſe make warre vpon carthaginenſes meſſage alſo acceptable syphax whervpon reaſoned legate expert men warre perceyued many thynges wherin men ignorant wherfore whan wolde haue departed intreated two wold retourne home theyr capitaynes deſyre ſure aliaunce betwene hym romanes aſcertayne full mynde thyrde myght remayne ſtyll hym gouernour army ſaying men good horſe men nothynge ſkylfull fyght foote requeſt agreed departed takyng kynges othe promyſe caſe theyr capitayns wold agree therto incontinent theyr felowe whiche left behynd ſhuld ſent home agayn name hym remayned kyng syphax statorius anon choſe greate numbre yonge actyue men whome taught folowe theyr baners kepe theyr aray romayne facion ſhorte ſpace syphax thought hym ſelfe able bothe horſebacke foote gyue battayle carthaginenſes thus ſafe bande peace amytie betweene romaynes syphax ¶ whan carthaginenſes ware therof ſent incontinent meſſangers one gala kyng part numidia gala ſonne xvii yeres age noble wyſe yongman called maſſaniſſa imbaſſadours ſhewed king better theyr helpe ouercome syphax betyme meanes roman ſhuld haue entre affrica ¶ ſuche wordes perſwaded gala warre moche ſooner maſſaniſſa ſonne deſyred gouernour army whervppon army carthaginenſes ioyned maſſaniſſa army fyrſte battayle syphax ouercome xxx men ſlayne ſo fewe horſemen fledde mauritaynes inhabyted nygh gades pyllars hercules gathered newe army men thinkyng ſayle ouer spayne er euer could take water maſſaniſſa armye camme agayne hym without helpe carthaginenſes fought noble batayle hym ouercame hym ¶ anniball treaſon nico philomenes wynneth citie tarent cap xxxvi anniball ſeaſon euer hauing hope citie tarent ſhuld one meane wōne ſayd made abode farre citie bring opinion purpoſe happed fortunate chāce meanes oone phileas tarentine longe tyme taryed rome meſſanger tarentines rome dyuers pledge noble bludde tarent kept gentyl kepyng theſe pledge phileas foūd mean haue often recours length ſo corrupted kepers ſuffered depart citie begynning nyghti phileas went guide ſecrete way morning yarly fame pledge departing ſprede abrode citie great numbre purſued thē ſpede ſo far trauailed ouertoke brought backe agayn citie theyr offence iudgement gyuen ſhuld firſt ſcourged roddes naked brought hygh rocke toppe wherof ſhulde throwen downe grounde ¶ cruell ende thoſe noble offended moch mindes dyuers city italy grece ſpecially thoſe kynne amitie alyed theym ſlayne among whiche ſort xiii noble tarent conſpired agaynſt roman captayns chief nico philomenes great hunter vſed moche iſſue citie nyght go huntyng wherfore colour goinge huntynge went towarde army anniball intendyng ſpeke declare vnto theyr intentes whā came nere campe two leauyng theyr company wodde nere adioynyng wente campe anone taken watchemen brought anniball theyr requeſt declared theyr purpoſe good wylle gaue theym greate thankes ſente theym hoome agayne looded fayre promyſes couer better theyr deuyſe wylled dryue certayn cattalle carthaginenſes ſayinge hadde gotten praye theyr ennemyes whyche ſuffered doo without reſyſtence brought home tarent ioye vſed oftentymes ſo thoughte meruayle ſoo often enterpryſed ſuche feates euer eſcaped vnſlayne thus often vſed euer whan kylled venyſon brought praye carthaginenſes whyche ſuffered tymes theyr pleaſures eyther gaue capytayne citie romayne elles porter gate ſoo brought porter ſuche cuſtome whan ſoo euer philomenes dyd whiſtell tymes nyghte gate opened vnto hym ¶ whan brought thynges good caſe purpoſe wente anniball agreed hym couenaunt tarentines ſhulde lyue euer vnder owne lawes cuſtomes alſo ſhoulde paye hym noo trybute haue anye armye appoynted anniball kepe citie owne pleſure ſhulde enioy goodes onely ſouldiours romanes whiche citie theyr goodes ſhulde pleaſure wyl anniball lay anniball iii dayes iourney tarent bycauſe wolde haue longe abode ſuſpecte fayned hym ſelfe ſycke cauſed bruted abrode ſycknes cauſe longe lyinge one place agaynſte tyme wolde haue towne choſe x thouſand horſemen lighteſt footemen army remoued campe nyght makyng ſpede tyll came within xv mile tarent ſecretely abode chargyng men wiſe breake aray order ſhuld beredy capitaynes dyd cōmaunde none fyrſte er ſette furth couer better remouing thintent none countrey ſhulde deſcrye armye ſent iiii ſcore numidian lyght horſemen go hym chargyng ouerrunne cuntrey whiche army ſhuld paſſe yf ouertoke men bring backe met ſhuld ſlea intent ſhulde thought inhabitantes went robber theues menne warre fame theyr robbyng came eares romayne capitayne tarent toke ſmalle regarde therto thynkyng ſyth anniball hym ſelfe ſycke army ſo farre wolde next day ſende furth certayne men armes dryue away thoſe robber ſaue corne cattall frendes ſame nyght deade parte therof remoued anniball toward tarent hauynge philomenes hym guyde whan came nigh towne appoynted philomenes ſhulde entre towne numbre men harneys gate wonte entre bryngynge praye huntynge whan came thither awaked porter ſaying brought great bore ſlayn fyrſt call porter opened gate fyrſte let two yong men company entred ſeruantes pluckyng great boore whoſe greatneſſe whyle keper daryng muſynge philomenes ſodeynly ſlew hym boore ſpeare huntyng ſtaffe incontinent let xxx men harneis ſlewe watchemen ſaid gate without noiſe let reſt army ſecretely brought theym market place abode ſpace without makyng noyſe while done one gate annibal great nū bre hym came priuily towarde gate farre made great fyre ſigne token made betwene hym nico abode complices redy within towne loking commyng whiche fyre whan nico perceyued anſweryng ſame made fyre whan eyther perceyued incontinent theyr fyres ſodeinly put anniball beganne approche army gate nico alſo within citie cam porter ward found open fyndyng watche ſlepe ſlewe kepers therof openyng gate lette anniball company footemen entre horſemen cōmaunded abyde playnes without neede requyred thus entred towne makyng noyſe came market place mette philomenes company thā company ii french men whyche deuyded thre partes ſent dyuers partes citie affricanes tarentynes cauſed kepe moſte accuſtomed ſtretes towne commaundynge theym ſlea romaynes wyſe ſpare tarentine citezens pourpoſe appoynted ſayde yonge gentylmenne tarent helper frendes company ſouldyours whan ſawe citezens ſhulde comfort byddyng affrayde ſhulde haue hurt beganne great rumour noyſe rayſed towne euer ſoo ſodeyne chaunce happeth capytayne fyrſte noyſe doubtyng treaſon fledde hauen frome then ſmalle bote paſſed ouer caſtell ¶ whanne day appeered harneys armes carthaginenſes perceyued alſo frenchemen deathe ſoo many romaynes manyfeſt anniball wonne towne whervpon romanes might eſcape fledde ſayd caſtell cauſed anniball citezens aſſemble togither without armure pleaſure obeyed dyd declare vnto loue great affection hath euer borne vnto gentylnes ſhewed vnto battaile traſymenus battaile canna whan ſent vnto theym ſuche theyr frendes taken captiues without hurt impediment raunſome expreſſed great inuectiues cruel proude dominion roman euer hadde ouer whiche come delyuer wyllinge euery one citie retourne home houſe ſpede wryte name doore owne houſe incontinent wold ſende ſouldiours ſpoyle diſtroy ſuche houſes name entitled doores chargynge theym peyne deathe none theym ſhoulde write name vppon doore roman mark wherby men myghte knowe houſes frendes thoſe ennemies ¶ exhortation lycenſed euery man departe home within certayn ſpace gaue ſygne ſouldiours ſpoyle houſes romanes whiche done good ſpoyle therof taken morowe determined aſſault caſtell whan ſawe ſtronge naturall ſite therof beyng halfe compaſſed ſea beatyng great hygh rockes halfe hauing great dyches hyghe walles towarde towne lothe ſpende tyme aſſaultyng therof leaue great thynges folowed neuertheleſſe loth leaue frendes tarentines open inuaſyons men armes caſtell towne myght tymes haue acceſſe pleaſure thought make walle dyche towne ſyde betwene caſtelle hadde opinyon whan dyche caſtynge romaynes wolde aduenture make excurſion labourer lette worke purpoſe intended yf ſo fierſely wold ſo diſpoſe men pryuily imbuſhmentes ſuch ſlaughter ſhulde made ſhoulde able hurte towne euen thoughte ſoo camme paſſe ſo ſoone worke begunne anone gate caſtell ſette open romaynes came workemen carthaginenſes ſuche violence anone gaue backe ſommewhat purpoſely enhaunce theyr harte courage allure theym frome theyr holde anone certayne token gyuen imbuſſhemente brake ſuche force inuaded romaynes fledde backe moche ſpeede towarde caſtelle ſtrete ſoo narowe whyche muſte paſſe ſoo troubled baggage labourer laye waye many ſlayne fleinge fyghtynge thus power caſtell lefte ſo ſmall afterwarde theyr workes neuer lette depe dyche walle made ſuche wyſe neded leaue garryſon towne neuer leſſe theyr ſauegarde lefte certayn ſouldiours reſte army remoued fyue myles thenſe ryuer galeſus pitched tentes soone retourned viewe ſtrength caſtell thought myght wonne ſaute whervppon cauſed maner engyns made ſette vp agaynſte walles greatte feare theym caſtell ſodeynly nyghte came certayne ſhyppes menne warre frome metapontus whyche holden roman entred hauen whoſe healpe caſtell threwe downe burned ingynes munymentes carthaginenſes wherby anniball loſte hope wynnynge caſtelle aſſaulte ymagyned contynuall ſiege famyſſhe theym whyche purpoſe alſo ſerued hym nothynge caſtelle hadde ſea free oone ſyde receyued vytayles theyr pleſure romaynes beynge mayſters hauen kepte prouyſyon frome cytie wonte comme water soo moche lyke endure famyne thanne caſtelle whome beſieged wherfore anniball myſtruſting ſtrength place called ruler tarent hym ſayde ¶ beholde nature ſite ſtrengthe caſtell ſee aſſault preuayle ſo long ennemies lordes ſea haue liberty may ſaid haue ſhippes may reſtrain vitailes brought either wil depart then yeld vnto v tarentines agreed well ſaid muſt helpe ſome nauy carthage sicilia might cauſed comme thither kepe ſaid port ſayde anniball haue ſhyppes owne yes truely ſayde lye littell creke ſo longe ennemies haue dominion mouthe hauen howe euer eſcape brode ſeas yes ſaid anniball feare many thinges naturally letted witte policy may brought paſſe citie ſituate playne euen grounde ſtretes way brode paſſe partes ſhippes wyll conuey high way leadeth middell citie vpon waines wheles vnto hauen ſmalle charge ſea ſhall nowe enemy lordes ſea lande wyll compaſſe ſo ſhortely ſhall dryuen forſake caſtell el ſhall take bothe alſo ¶ wyſe diuiſe made men haue wonder admiration hym alſo hoope good ſucceſſe purpoſe furth withal wayne carte gathered tyed togither engins made raiſe drawe vp ſhippes way made hard euen leuell myght eaſily drawen thus ſtrength beaſtes men ſhyppes broughte hauen fewe day garniſhed men thinges neceſſary brought rounde caſtell caſtyng ankers mouthe hauen ¶ fuluius flaccus romane conſull wynneth campe hanno ſleeth taketh great number men ryche pray mago ſleeth titus gracchus many romaynes treaſon flauius lucan capitu xxxvi vvhyles anniball thus occupied aboute buſyneſſe tarent quintus fuluius flaccus appius claudius choſen conſuls yere com bothe armyes party samnite ruler capua feared greatly leſt dyd intende ſhortly beſiege citie alſo plentye corne beganne faile legion roman hadde ſo inuaded countrey campanes durſt neither tyll ſow groundes wherfore ſent legate vnto annibal deſiring hym cauſe plenty wheate brought capua countrey adioynyng conſuls dydde enter countrey theyr army whervpon anniball ſent meſſangers hanno ſhuld come bruſians army cāpania make prouiſion campanes might haue good plenty corne ſent ¶ hanno commaunded leauynge samnite conſuls paſſed tyll came within iii myles beneuentum mountayne pitched campe townes frendes adioyning great plentie wheate ſommer bene caryed made goodly prouiſion campanes ſent worde ſecretely capua day ſhuld wayne carte coulde aſſemble countrey reſorte ſayd place fette away ſaid wheate campanes lyghtly ſklenderly foreſeing buſines welth day aſſigned came thither bringyng iiii hundred carte theyr ſlouth hanno greatly rebuked maruaylyng wolde hedily auoyde hunger whiche brute beaſtes labour eſchue wherfore ſente home laden appoynted nother day retourne againe moche greatter quantitie ¶ appoyntment came eares beneuentanes whervpon incontynent ſente tenne meſſangers conſulles certifyenge theym campanes purpoſe furthwith agreed fuluius armye ſhoulde goo beneuentum enter towne nyghte kepynge cloſe therin tyll ſawe tyme apte purpoſe ſoone fuluius entred beneuentum ſhewed hym hanno parte army gone furth wheate ii wayns come campe great rude ſort people vnarmed lay myngled amonge ſouldiours kepyng order vſe men warre knowen conſul cōmanded men redy theyr baners armure next night wold aſſayle campanes tentes carthaginenſes executyng commandement made redy iiii clocke ſet furthe towne came hannos campe lyttell dawnyng day theyr fyrſt commynge ſodain noiſe carthaginenſes becam ſo feareful campe pitched plain ground wonne ſmall reſiſtence height hyll defēſes made therabout ſuch could way get vp vnto great ſteppes climming daunyng day bataile began waxe ſtronge carthaginenſes onely defended campe alſo kept hyll without euer throwing doune romās ſtroue wonderſly clymme place neuertheleſſe length great pein trauaile alſo great loſſe hurt men gat diches campe conſull aduiſyng well miſchief ſhulde fall company winning place callid tribune vnto ſaying wold time purſue foliſhe enterpriſe wold returne day beneuentū morow wold ioyne campe campe enmies ſo campanes ſhuld iſſue hanno haue recours thē whan returned bring better ſurely paſſe wolde ſende felowe claudius conſull army aſſiſt therin whan tribune cauſed retreate ſowned ſouldiours earneſtly buſy aboute enterpriſe wolde gyue none care therto among one vibius capitain cōpany pelignes ſtreight toke baner hande force threwe ouer diche campe carthaginenſes ſayd euyl might fare company myn enemy ſhall enioy baner great force lightly went ouer diche clame vp entred campe enemy company boldly folowed thus fought within cāpe carthaginenſes part cried valerius flaccus ſluggiſhe cowardes nowe waxen ſhall pelignes wynne honour taking campe ennemies v roman whervpon titus pedanius capitayn hūdred men toke ſtanderd hande ſtanderde bearer ſaying ſtanderde wyll beare fielde myne enemy folowe ſyrs many wolde lothe loſſe therof anone companye goten part cāpe conſul perceyuing hardynes changed mynd calling away began comfort exhorting reſt helpe felowes ſo valiantly fought campe theyr enmies whoſe harty wordis euery man inforced ſelfe enter regarding dartes weapon enemy people fearyng peryll people cared deth ſo might dye campe enemy thus within ſhort ſpace ſtrong place wōne aboue vi ſlayn vii taken men campania came corne al carte riche pray hā gotten fieldes frendes roman whiche pray conſuls ſolde tyme claudius alſo come thither therwith rewarded men ſpecially vibius pedanius whan hanno hearde loſſe people fledde backe againe brutianes fewe men whiche taken hym get wheate campanes ¶ cāpanes heryng loſſe men frendes ſent annibal ſhewing cōſuls beneuentū within day iorney capua intending lay ſiege city feared leſt ſhortly ſuccour roman wold wynne diſtroy citie ſaid nother caſtell tarent town alſo ought ſo moch eſtemed capua noblenes wherof knew well ſelfe ſo moch wont compare vnto carthage wherfore truſted wold leaue vndefended haue ſpoiled diſtroyed romayns ¶ annibal hering meſſage ſhewed ambaſſadours loue bare vnto citie promiſing euer defender therof theſe gentyll wordes ſent home ſent alſo ii horſmen whoſe helpe might defend fieldes robbing waſtyng ¶ meane whyle p cornelius pretor certain ſhippes laden wheate came hauen tarent hole power carthaginenſes cauſed alſo ſuche ſouldiours metapontus garriſon come caſtell tarent remaine defence therof whoſe cōminge caſtell ſure hurt ennemies ſo ſoone inhabitantes metapontus deliuered romayne garriſon incontinent fell leage amitie anniball whervpon thurines alſo hauynge grudge roman ſleing diuers frendes aforſaid deuyſed meane bringe citie amitie anniball kynſmen ſlayne ſente meſſangers hanno mago among bruſians willing come army lay ſiege towne doubtyng one marcus attinius ruler ſmalle company romaynes left defence towne wolde anon brought iſſue gyue battaylle vppon truſt yong men armes towne armed inſtructed feates warre roman facion douted ſort wold doo hym ſmall pleaſure whan ſhuld haue moſt nede theym two capitains hearing glad tidinges ſpede entred fieldes thurines diuydyng company betwene theym hanno footemen baners diſplayed good aray went towarde towne mago horſmen abode valey vnder certayn hylles nigh towne attinius knowing company fotemē put men good aray great courage iſſued towne nothing myſtruſtyng myſchiefe wrought agaynſt hym within towne battaile quicke part roman thurines ſtode men gaue lokynge enemy hanno men pourpoſe gaue backe drawe romanes daunger horſmen whan came nere hilles fierſly aſſayled romayns ſyde mago horſemen came ſodainly egrely vpon fyrſt encountring thurines fledde towne faſt coulde roman ſeaſon mainteyned battaile laſt conſtrained thereto alſo fledde towarde towne traytours cauſers al miſchief gotten gate power againſt commyng backe thurines fledde kept open gate receyued towne whan romanes came fleyng alſo thinkyng haue entred cried tyme nowe ſhutte gate el ſhall lette carthaginenſes towne among owne men ſo loſe whervpon ſhut theyr gate ſuffred roman ſlayne ennemies without ſuccour attinius capitayn gentilly dered ruler ſuffered enter fewe incontinent gaue ſhippe hauen badde hym ſaue ſelfe ſea whoſe departynge opened gate receyued carthaginenſes ¶ nowe conſuls departed beneuentū aſſaute capua thinkyng ſhuld make yere happy honourable yf might wynne capua ſo noble riche reuenge iniuries done neuertheleſſe intent beneuentanes ſhulde lefte withoute ſuccours theyr abſence ſent titus gracchus cuntrey lucans commandyng hym horſemen lyght footemen come beneuentum leauynge lucanes reſte men vnder ſome capitayn myght truſte ¶ lucans diuided diuers townes rendred vp anniball certaine abode vnder romaynes iurisdiction ſort chiefe rular yere one flauius lucan flauius ſodeynly tourned mynde anniball obteyne fauour ſente mago among brutians come ſpeke hym whan mette compoſition made betwene coulde delyuer gracchus capitayn romain army lucanes ſhulde frendly receiued amitie carthaginēſes lyue lawes thā brought mago great couert willed great numbre men armes hyde hym appoyntyng hym tyme whiche wolde bring thither romaine capitayne appoyntment departed went gracchus ſhewed begunne ſecretely great enterpryſe whyche brynge effecte muſte haue healpe aſſyſtence haue ſayde moued perſwaded pryncis lucans gone amitie anniball nowe retourne agayne obedience rome haue declared vnto increaſe romanes power whiche dayly may perceiue decreaſe ſtrength carthaginenſes bad myſtruſt gentylnes romains whoſe nature haue euer tryed meke gentyll ſuche haue rebelled agaynſt vpon hū ble ſubmiſſiō made theſe perſuaſions contented reconciled ſo may ſpeake ſame laying right hand pledge faithe whervnto may truſt haue ſayde vndertaken ſhall doo haue appoynted compoſition ſecrete place wel way company feare eſpies yet far campe fewe wordes may go matter meane bryng lucanes wholly vnder iurisdiction ¶ gracchus nothyng ſtruſtynge diſceite treaſon wordes toke officer horſemen al vnarmed ſo rode place appointed hauynge flauius hym guyde ſoone come thyther mago army inuaded theym ſodaynly make treaſon euident flauius incontinent ioyned carthaginenſes plenty dartes caſte gracchus horſemen whan ſawe noo remedy alyght horſe bad company doo ſame exhortynge ſyns fewe number vnarmed ſuche place coulde noo waye eſcape wolde dye lyke beaſtes vnreuenged noble harte ſhoulde aſſaile theyr ennemyes dye bathed beſprynkled bloudde theyr ennemies whereby ſhulde ende moſte honour ſpecially aboue thyng ſayde lette euery v ſeeke ſlea lucane traytour flauius doubtynge ſo euer ſhall ſende traytours ſoule helle dye hym ſelfe ſhall fynd oblation therof todoo hym moche comforte ſolace ſoone hadde thus ſpoken threwe clooke aboute lefte arme ſtede ſhielde ranne vppon ennemies dartes weapon ſlewe moſt part romaine whan ſawe gracchus without helpe intended take hym lyue ſo ſoone perceiued flauius amonge ennemies ranne thickeſt ſuche force haue ſlayne conſtrained ſlea hym elles done greate hurte whoſe body mago cauſed brought anniball cauſed buried moche honour ¶ centenius penula cneius fuluius theyr two army diſcomfyted ſlayne anniball ſeuerall battayles cap xxxviii meane ſeaſon conſulles entred fieldes campanes theyr menne ouerſpreading countrey robbynge ſpoylynge waſtynge dyuers place whiche beinge perceyued mago horſemen healpe townes men iſſued oute ſodaynely theym euer coulde gather togyther order battaile ſlewe one thouſand fyue hundred loſſe cauſed conſuls circumſpectly worke theyr procedynges afterwarde ¶ anniball heryng proſperous bataile campanes abſence drew nere vnto capua army thinkyng romanes ſhulde moche leſſe able indure power ioyned campanes wherfore third day comming diſplayde baners ſet company order goodly aray redy fight romayns likewiſe made theym redy horſemen bothe ſydes fought ſtrongly ſeaſon tyll bothe partes perceiued ſtrange army comming toward wherof nother priuie truthe therof c cornelius bearing office queſtor rome taken legiōs whyche yere vnder sempronius commyng ayde conſuls commynge vnknowen made well conſuls affraide anniball ſo agreement partes withdrue campes roman hauing ſomwhat loſſe thā cartha ginēſes conſuls wylling draw annibal away frō capua deuiſed night folowing depart awaye fuluius hoſt went diſtroy fieldes cumans appius hoſt went lucanes anniball morning hauing knowlege ſundry departing diuers wais while dout whether might folow laſt determined folowe appius wherin moche deceiued leadinge hym great compaſſe aboute countreys pleaſure retourned againe way capua fortune whyle ſmylyng anniball ſent hym ſuche chance ſeaſon ſtayed thoſe party one foliſhe hardy enterpriſe one centenius penula gentylman goodly ſtature body noble courage mynde correſpondent ſame ¶ centenius broughte ſenate houſe p cornelius sulla deſyred ſenatours might haue deliuered v ſouldiours whoſe helpe doubted knowlege countreys alſo crafty feates ennemy wold ſame ſubtiltie policy deceiue anniball whiche deceiued romaynes vnwiſe promiſe vnto vnwiſely beleued demaunded v gaue viii men countreys went gathered togyther almoſte many mo ſuche willyngly went hauing hope courage promiſe noumbre men came fieldes lucanes anniball reſted hym company wery chaſe appius claudius whan either ſawe others army incontinēt put folke aray matche equall nother capitaines ſouldiours neuertheleſſe bataile indured two howres centenius perceiuinge part ſuffre worſe fearing leſte ſhulde lyue men ſlayne ſhulde ſuffer great ſhame infamy lyfe loſſe ſuche numbre men foliſhe enterpriſe laſt willingly entred thickeſt preaſe enemy ſhortly ſlayne men fledde partes ſo harde chaſed horſemen great company eſcaped ſcant one thouſand ¶ one happy chāce fortune ſent annibal farewel leue takyng ſhe thought depart roman occaſion therof one cneiꝰ fuluius bearing office pretor lay apulia hoſt beſiegyng ſuche townes come amitie carthaginenſis buſynes ſoo well ſped become ſo welthy riche bothe men prayes whiche taken leauyng good order warre peynfull purſuite thereof growen ſlouthe ſluggyſſhe ydelnes theyr vndiſcrete order appulians ſente woorde anniball meſſangers knowing experience wolde folowe gouernance army vnwiſe capitane wherof late triall centenius ſpede remoued coſtis apulia whan romains knowlege enemy approched ouen hande mynded haue diſplayde baners haue runne batail without cōmandement capitain night folowing annibal perceiuing great haſt battaile cōmanded iii light men warre lye priuily hyd woodes buſhes couertes next adioyning gyuing ſigne token tyme ſhulde iſſue aſſaile enmies cauſed mago ii horſemen lye priuily wayes demed roman wolde flee theyr diſcomfiture theſe thynges nyght tyme wyſely diſpoſed yarly morning came hoſt fieldes putting reſt men goodly aray ¶ ſide fuluius pretor made tarying moche inforced therto haſty wilfulnes ſouldiours wherfore ſuche aduyſement came fielde ſuche lyke aduyſement batayles ordred euery man went place ſemed beſt choſe cōpany wold ſomtyme changed place pleaſure forward left wing fyrſt ordered length ſmall thykneſſe tribune cried ſet ſtrength men myddell battailes el enemy myght eaſyly go ſmall force theyr pleaſure ſo wylfull haſty gaue noo eare theyr wordes tyme carthaginenſes come good order redy ioyne whoſe fyrſt cominge great noiſe bruite romains put wors whervpon capitayn ſeing lyke go miſchiefe toke hors two hundred horſemen fled reſte abode almooſte ſlayne xviii company eſcaped paſt ii alyue tentes ſtuffe alſo taken carthaginenſes whiche good pray tydinges theſe great ſodayn loſſes brought rome whiche cauſed citie great feare mournyng neuertheleſſe cauſe bothe conſulles army ſafe ſomwhat proſper affayres toke comforte theym incontynent ſent meſſangers conſuls wylling ſerch ſuch eſcaped theſe two battailes ſhuld gathered togither called vnto leſt either feare diſpaire wold yeld enmies whiche thyng diligence dyd execute ¶ citie capua beſeged two conſuls anniball cō meth ſuccour citezēs giueth cōſuls battel then goth rome ward hoſt thintent therby draw cōſuls ſiege capua ca xxxix meane ſeaſon capua compaſſed beſieged conſuls great prouiſion corne made ſame laid garner caſtel caſſelinꝰ ſent sueſſula claudius nero pretor leauyng ſmall garriſon came hym ſelfe theym capua power thus capua compaſſed thre greatte armyes three partes encloſe citezens ſurely prepared compaſſe hole city great diche thervpon made many caſtels good diſtance thone frō cāpanes thinkynge let work iſſued many time fought romās fortune euer ſuch loſt ſtill mē laſt conſtrained kepe within walles citie warkes ſiege ſo ſtraite ſtrong ſent ambaſſadours anniball complaynyng forſaken theym citie capua yf dyd ſhortly ſuccour muſt yeld roman anniball anſwered late reſ • ued rayſed ſiege one ſhortly wolde come helpe againe doubting romayns ſhuld vnable reſiſt power cōmyng comfortable meſſage retourned citie whyche founde ſo compaſſed double dyche peyne coulde fynde meane enter neither coulde haue entred letter p cornelius pretor bene wherin aduyſed conſuls dyche ſhuld fully finyſſhed proclaime many campanes wolde iſſue baggage bagges day lymitted ſhulde go free wold haue goodes owne day ſoo many remained wolde take vſe enemy proclamation ſo diſdainfully taken campanes beſyde wold none iſſue city alſo ſpake proude opprobrious wordes diſpite romaynes whervppon workes dyche ended citie fully encloſed ¶ anniball deſyrous ſuccour great frendes capua left al heuy cariage among brucians great numbre choſen horſemen light fotemen haſted thither faſte might hooſte came xxxiii elephantes army came valey vnder mountayn adioynyng capua called tifata er roman knowlege cōming ſent ſpies romayns hoſte capua commaundynge ſoo ſoone ſhulde gyue battaile parte boſtar mago horſemen garriſon carthaginenſes aſſemblynge alſo power citizen ſhoulde ſodaynely iſſue oute citie force aſſayle ennemies diuiſe anniball executed ſoo ſodayne crye clamoure romaynes greate feare daunger neuertheles great ſpede coulde prepared battayles dyuyded people appius claudius wente withſtande campanes fuluius wente agaynſte anniball claudius ſtronge inough ennemies fuluius hardly handled carthaginenſes spaniardes one cō pany legion men driuen backe great companye spanyardes thre elephantes broken myddell warde romaynes come trench campe redy enter tentes campe enmies whan fuluius ſawe daunger people campe cried q nanius pety capitaines exhorting aſſaile company spaniardes fought diche ſhewyng danger onleſſe might ſone confounded eaſy inough done ſens greatter number nanius ſtrong man huge ſtature whan hearde conſulles exhortation anone toke ſtanderde hym bare commaundyng company boldly take parte hym ſette furthe towarde spanyardes great courage ſone spaniardes ſawe hym drawe nere threwe plentye dartes hym beganne violently aſſayle nother beynge ſtayde multitude ennemies dartes caſte great force went ſtylle forwarde tyl helpe marcus attilius portius lucius ſlain elephantes made great ſlaughter alſo spaniardes ¶ part campanes dryuen back garriſon alſoo numidian carthaginenſes ſoo battaile ſtronge euen gate capua towarde ryuer vulturnus gate garniſhed croſſebowes dartes ſuche ingyns wherby many romayns wounded ſhot towre gate amonge conſul appius claudius ſoore hurt breaſt vnder left ſhulder neuertheleſſe citizen helper driuen citie great ſlaughter loſſe theyr company anniball ſeing ſlaughter spaniardes romaynes ſo manfully defended theyr campes cauſed people withdrawe made horſemen abyde hyndermoſte defence footemen yf ennemies happed chaſe romaine egre wolde haue folowed chaſe flaccus cauſed ſounde retreate ¶ batayle anniball wrought one crafty poynt ſent dyuers men forth coulde ſpeake latine tunge dyuers partes hooſte romaynes whyche ſhulde conſuls name behalfe declare romayne campes taken ſpoyled wherfore wylled euery man ſaue hym ſelfe fleing next mountayns ſens lenger tarying greater ſhuld theyr loſſe crafty deceite made many amaſed laſte eſpied great ſlaughter ennemies ¶ battaile romaynes kept campes ſo ſtraightly beſieged citie anniball ſeinge could drawe furth bataile nother campes romaine haue way enter capua fearyng leſte vitayles ſhuld cut hym hoſte determined depart then ymagyned wolde go towarde rome doubtynge whan romayn capitaynes dyd perceyue rome theyr head citie daunger either one wolde leaue capua come defence therof theyr power diuided bothe partes ſhoulde weaker truſted either campanes ſhulde haue fayre day ſome one thynge troubled hym ſoore leſt campana ſeing departyng wolde incontinent yelde citie romayns wherfore fayre wordes great giftes gotten one numidia go letter campes romains one runne away carthaginenſes army whan ſhuld come part hoſt towarde citie ſecretly enter capua deliuer letter full comfort declaring departyng theyr profite thintent onely withdrawe ennemies capua defende owne citie bydding diſpayre take pacience ſeaſon truſtyng ſhortly loſe daunger sone departed hoſte paſſed ryuer vulturnus taking way towarde rome commynge cauſed great heuynes citie ſenatours conſulted beſte done daungerous caſe length agreed q fuluius ſhulde come capua certayn legion leauing felowe ſiege numbre ſufficient purpoſe q fuluius hauing cōmandement toke xv fotemen one thouſand horſe men folowed anniball ſpedily could anniball come within iii mile rome pitched tentes made campe riuer ſide ſoone came quintus fuluius flaccus rome army conſulted ſenators affaire done touching enmies toke annibal ii horſemen hym camme walles gate rome riding gate called porta collina temple hercules viewynge ſituation citie ſtrength walles bolde hygh mynde anniball ſo fuluius flaccus coulde ſuffer incontinent ſent furth greate numbre horſemen force droue enemy campe next day anniball came fielde hoſt good aray redy gyue battaile flaccus hauinge hym two newe conſuls late choſen power made hym redy alſo battaile thus whan bothe partes redy go togither abidynge chaunce fortune whether ſhulde maiſter noble citie rome came ſodainly ſo vehement ſtorme raine haile togither partes faine withdrawe campes nexte daye lykewiſe redye ioyne battaile whan like ſtorme alſo departed theym agayne theyr departure incontynente wether waxed verye bryght fayre wyndes ceaſſed whiche euyl chance toke away harte courage anniball companye euer enioye citie rome wherfore hauynge hope therof returned backe haſt brucians conſul quintus fuluius returned capua felowe ¶ oration vibius virius concerning yeldyng capua romaine receyue towne ſlea ſenatours conuerte groundes therof profit city rome cap xl campanes perceyuing returne quintus fuluius annibal iuged ſelfes vtterly forſaken wherfore wepyng mourning noble men kept houſes loking dayly owne deathes diſtruction citie hole charge keping therof boſtar hanno captain garriſon carthaginenſes fering eſtate ſent priuily letter anniball ſomewhat ſharply written wherin blamed hym onely leauyng citie capua handes romaine alſo • e committing capitaynes ſure frendes ſouldiours retinue handes enemy ſuffre tourmentes intollerable hym ſelfe gone brucians bycauſe wolde ſee hym takynge capua wherfore ſaide caſe wolde come agayn returne hole power thither hole power capua wold redy breake forthe theyr ennemyes truſting wynne therby moche honour ſayde alſo commyng ouer mountaines warre rhegines tarentines romaynes romain legion ſhuld army carthaginenſes alſo ſo doinge moſte part euer good ſpede canna traſymenus diuers place giuing bataile valiantly ¶ theſe letter ſent one numidia eſpye counterfaited ſelf run carthaginenſes army hūger daily oppreſſed citie letter alſo ſame effect ſent dyuers numidian chaunced woman whome one meſſangers kepte harlotte feelyng greate hunger cytie ranne towne tentes romain conſull flaccus declared vnto hym ſuche eſpy campe whiche letter conueye anniball man founde oute whan came hedenyed parte accuſation trewe denied alſo made aboue lxx theym taken beaten fyrſt roddes hadde theyr handes ſtriken ſent citie captain ¶ whan capitayns ſawe extreme punyſhement ſhewed theyr meſſangers theyr harte began fayle whervpon leſius yererular citie called generall counſayle whyche many ſenatours moued ambaſſadours ſhulde ſent romayn conſuls vibius virius chiefe cauſer yeldyng capua anniball beynge demaunded opinyon therin aunſwered ſpake peace takyng yeldyng capua ought remembre bothe wolde haue done yf romayns theyr power lyke caſe alſo campanes lyke ſuffer whan ſubmitted wholly theyr pleaſure ¶ lette v ſayde remembre howe leauing theyr frendſhyp ſubmytted v anniball contented therwith ſlewe romaynes lefte garriſon v haue certayne knowlege theyr harte enuy towarde v lette v call v theyr actes done late agaynſt v therby ye ſhall perceyue kyndnes lyke haue theyr handes anniball ſtraunger theyr vtter enemy italy cuntrey partes fulfylled warre yet leauyng anniball theyr buſyneſſe ſente bothe conſulles theyr whole armyes beſiege capua longe contynuall kepyng ſame ſiege almoſt famiſhed hunger profe theyr ••• yee towarde v let v conſyder although anniball commyng ſuccours almoſte wonne theyr campes ſayne many theyr men put great ieopardy loſing yet ieoperdous peryll loſſe neuer coulde moue theym remoue theyr ſiege afterward whan paſſed riuer vulturnus bournynge fieldes calenus theyr fath full frendes yet coulde hurtes call capitaynes myſerable ſiege ye cauſed baners diſplayd walles citie rome ſaying onles wold leaue capua wold take high citie rome yet wolde leaue ſiege capua beares wulues wyld beaſtes neuer ſo great rage fury man goo caues theyr yong whelpes lye anone wyll leaue al aboute runne ſtreighte defence theyr yonge furyous romaynes whan rome compaſſed theyr enemy nother theyr wyues chyldren whoſe lamentable wepinges myght heard almoſte hither nother houſes temple goddis feare violating sepulture theyr auncetours coulde withdrawen ſiege capua ſo deſyrous execute v greuous punyſhement ſo ſore thyrſt drynke bludde reaſon happily ſhulde haue done lykewyſe yf fortune deſerued v wherfore ſens pleaſure goddis nedes muſte dye yet wylle chuſe deathe bothe honeſt gentyll wherby wyll eſcape tormentes diſpites myne ennemies truſte put vnto whan fuluius claudius ſhall ſolempnely triumph enter rome wyl bounden drawen ſpectacle wondryng ſtocke put pryſon tyed poſte ſuffer body ſcourged laſt haue head ſtryken body axe rome nother lyue ſe cuntrey diſtroied bourned ſee noble matron maiden capua rauiſhed defouled beginnyng flouriſhynge citie rome romains diſtroyed citie alba threwe downe grounde yet theyr originall ſame citie trowe ye wyl capua whiche hate doo carthage therfore frendes ſo many deſyrous dye ye ſe theſe ſo many ſo ſpiteful miſeries come day dyner meate alredy dreſſed whā well filled wyne good meates cup drynke wyll fyrſt drinke ſelfe ſhall borne euery one drynke ſhall delyuer body tormentes mynde rebuke eies eares frō ſyght hearyng cruell diſpites capua ¶ vibius virius went home houſe dyner whome xxvii ſenatours folowed dyned drunke plē ty wyne intent might haue leſſe feelinge laſt dredefull drynke whan came laſt receiued poyſon went table taking eyther handes louingly enbraſyng one lamented owne deathes diſtruction cuntrey remained died bourned fyres made intent ſome went home houſes made ende ſo towne deliuered romaine none left lyue ¶ next day gate opened romaine ſuffered enter gate kepte romains man ſhuld go furth firſt armour wepons brought romain capitain carthaginenſes garriſon taken put priſon ſenatours cōmanded go conſuls tentes whens ſuch moſt conſenting receiuīg annibal ſent ſūdry priſons xxv cales xxviii theanus vntil agreed puniſhment ſhuld haue golde ſyluer brought deliuered officer called queſtores claudius cō ſull moch inclined take ſenators mercy fuluius ſide wold haue ſuffer example rebelles traytours wherefore claudius remitted thing iugement ſenate rome ſent thither knowe pleaſure therin whervpon fuluius fearing leſt ſhuld ſtayed purpoſe cōmanded tribune ii horſemen redy ride third blaſt trumpet cōpany horſmen night departed army day light came theanus cauſyng ſenatours capua priſoners brought incontinent cauſed violently ſcourged roddes haue heades ſtriken then faſt might hied cales likewiſe ſat vpon iugement ſenatours capua while going execution one came ſenate rome riding great haſt letter willing ſtay iudgement execution puniſhment cāpane ſenators fuluius iudging letter writen intent neuer diſcloſed put boſom ſaying officer ſhuld procede quickly execution accordinge lawe alſo whipped heades ſtryken conſull drewe furth letter redde ſaying came late let thynge alredy done cales returned capua put diuers priſon beſide many citie ſold thā great debate ſenate rome whether citie capua ſhuld burned vtterly dyſtroyed exaumple rebelles moch moued theym ſoo doo greate ſtronge citie nere neyghbour vnto whych ſhuld ennemy agayne rome late ſhould greatlye dyſquiete romaynes spain ſtronge inough therfore hyred xxx thouſand men warre celtiberia power carthage diuided iii army gouerned thre capitaines aſdruball ſonne gyſgon mago theſe two capitaines lay v dayes iourney romaine legion thyrd whiche aſdruball ſonne amilcar auncient capitayne carthaginenſes countreye laye anniturgium neerevnto romaine hadde pourpoſe ſommer folowynge paſſe mountaynes conueye armye anniball pourpoſe lette two scipio thought fyrſte aſſayle hym aloone company doubtyng ſtronge inough ſo doo greatteſt feare leſt whan ouercome haſdruball mago hearyng therof wolde flee mountaynes ſtraytes power ſo prolonge warres spayn wherfore make ende theyr trouble one concluded part army twayne p cornelius two partes ſhulde goo agaynſt two capitaines lay togither cn scipio thyrde part theyr olde army celtiberians ſhulde aſſaile aſdruball ſonne amilcar theſe mindes ſet furth togither toward ennemies cn scipio whan came aniturgium reſted company ſyght enemy hauyng riuer betwene hym brother went furthe agreed betwene aſdruball perceiuing numbre romayns ſmall ſtrengthe ſtrangers late hyred knowing faccion people vntrue vnſtable meane spaniardes coulde ſpeake language great ſummes money corrupted princis rulars ſo agreed departe home theyr hole power deſyred hyred vndertake warres aſdrubal againſt romaine onely depart without fighting whervnto ſone intreated partly large wage though ſhuld haue foughten agayne gladde retourne home theyr cuntreys frendes auoyding danger warre therfore ſodaynely baners caryage departed romaine meruayling ſodaine chaunge ment enquired cauſe departure anſwered ſent home defende theyr owne cuntrey whiche oppreſſed alſo warre anſwere could none gette nother romaynes able kepe force scipio knowyng without theym nothynge able encounter aſdruball alſo ſeynge waye howe myghte recouer companye brother ennemies beinge ſoo nere commynge hym meruaylouſly aſtonied yet thought beſte wyſe meete hym euen grounde ſoo farre ouermatched wherfore lyttell lyttell drewe backe ſekyng ſome place ſtrength myghte ſuccour hym ſelfe ſmall company perceiuing haſdruball paſſed ryuer hooſte folowed moche ſpeede could ¶ nowe p scipio brother moche troubled parte reaſon maſſaniſſa yong luſty prince numidia beinge frende carthaginenſes comme good power numidian ſuccour mago haſdruball ſonne gyſgon fiers greatte courage romaynes coulde nother goo abrode vitayles woode ſuche neceſſaries numidian euer redy oppreſſe dyuers tymes nyght wolde aſſayle theym theyr campe people beſieged alſo tydinges brought scipio one indibilis ſeuen thouſande fyue hundred sueſſanes hande commynge healpe carthaginenſes whoſe army beinge ioyned knewe ſhulde ſtraightly encloſed wherfore compelled neceſſitie ſerche compaſſe wytte determyned ſecretely take greatter part armye meete indibilis nyghte intendynge ſoo euer mette hym gyue hym battaylle lefte titus fonteius certayne hym keepe campe goynge waye aboute mydnyght met indibilis ſodaynly aſſayled hym fyerſe conflycte ſeaſon ſodayne ſettynge theym romaynes hadde putte theym flyghte greatte ſlaughter hadde numidian horſemenne alwayes awayted romaynes ſoo euer wente bothe partes ſodeynly aſſayled theym yet scipio ſoo pryuily nyght departed hadde thought therby haue begiled numidian watchemen battail renued agayn mago aſdruball hoſtes folowing theyr backes ſo romaynes knew whiche beſt tourne scipio ſtille comforted exhorted men euer battaile moſte ſtronge thyther went lyke noble valiant gouernour tyll laſt hym ſelfe thyrſt ryght ſyde ſpeare ſo fell dead hors whan carthaginenſes ſawe romayne capitayne falle incontinent ranne abrode partes fielde ioyfully cryinge scipio capitayne romaine ſlayne fame wherof gaue hart carthaginenſes cauſed romaynes flee flyght mo ſlayne batail numidian horſmen ſo fierſe chaſe footemen hauyng lyght harneis almoſt ſwyft horſes yf nyght come theym fewe none eſcaped carthaginenſes victory ſlept ſtayde folowe theyr good occaſyon offered incontinent toke theyr horſes went haſdruball ſonne amilcar doutyng good ſpede alſo theyr power mette togyther great ioye made betweene capiteynes bothe theyr metynge alſo newes theyr late victory ¶ ſyde romayns ſtryken feareful penſifenes knowlege loſſe company ſuch ſpede made theyrennemies worde thereof coulde ſo ſoone broughte feare inwarde ſecrete iudgement theyr harte ſomme euyll chaunce happed vnto theym agayne cn scipio ſeing hoſte ennemyes encreaſed commynge mago aſdruball meruailed howe ſhulde conuey theyr armye thyther ſo ſoone without battayle onleſſe brother ſlayne meruayled alſoo brother nother dydde lette commynge thyther nother yet dydde appere folowynge theym knewe yf lyne wolde make haſte come ioyne army vnto great trouble mynde thoughte withdrawe hym moche myght wherefore nyght gone good ſpace grounde dawnyng daye numidian ware departing folowed horſes ſo long nyght ouertoke theym aſſayling one ſide ſomtyme behynde euer scipio cauſed theym keepe good aray go euer forewarde fightynge daunger footemen enemy folowed horſemen ſo vexed partes could go farre wherfore scipio gathered ſmall company vp lytell hyll beſt coulde eſpy aduātage toke order theyr ſtuffe cariage brought myddell hoſt horſemen ſette ſame without foote men ſaued inuaſion numidian horſemen tyl reſt carthaginenſes come scipio ſeing hym ſelfe ſo vnable reſiſt iii capitaynes great hoſtes began diuiſe howe might meanes caſt trenche campe make ſome hedge defende inuaſions theyr enemy thā hyll ſo bare grounde ſo ſtony buſhes thornes coulde gathered turues dygged trenche made hyll ſelfe ſo flatte coulde maner way let commyng vp enemy scipio make ſome ſhewe defence aboute campe deuiſed lay packes groſſe cariage cō paſſe campe one vpon thervppon cauſed packſaddels fardel tyed wherby rayſed walles campe good height ¶ whan hoſtes carthaginenſes come aſcended ſmall hyll lyttel peyne ſeing ſtraunge kynde fortifieng campe neuer ſene amaſed ſtayde ſeaſon capitaynes perceiuyng theyr ſodayne ſtoppe wondryng cried al partes ſaying great ſhame ſo longe coulde plucke downe deface ſuche fond deuiſe mockery wherwith child woman wold ſo long haue ben ſtayed go therfore courage ſayd ennemies lye lurkyng behynde thoſe packes theſe rebuke capitaines aſſayed enter partes though greate whyle lette troubled therabout laſt diuers partis entred ſo numbre could longer endure againſt ſo many campe wonne many ſlain wherof cn scipio noble capitayne one good number ſledde woodes next vnto ſo eſcaped came tentes publius scipio whyche kept fonteius thus bothe bretherne capytaynes romaynes spayne ſlayne within ſpace xxx dayes whoſe death greatly lamented rome alſo spain thought death hole army romaine spayn vtterly brought confuſyon countrey thereby brought romaynes handes ¶ l martius choſen capitaine romaine army maketh oration ſouldiours one nyghte day vanquiſheth ii hoſtes carthaginenſes winneth campes greate praye capit xlii peryll ieoperdous eſtate one man founde army whoſe witte courage fortune honour welthe romaynes ſaued reſtored lucius martius ſonne septinius freſhe yonge man actiue martius hadde longe ben warres vnder c scipio hym learned moche experience policy gouernance army nowe ſeing thinges almoſte deſperate gathered togither ſuch ſouldiours fleing eſcaped laſt bataile alſo aſſembled good numbre men warre dyuers townes fortreſſes whiche vnder obedience rome theſe came tentes fonteius ioynyng romaine power togither ſhort ſpace name honour ſo exalted whole conſent ſouldyours army choſen capitayne guyde whervpon incontinent applied himſelfe buſyly make ſure theyr campe alſo make good prouiſyon vitayles ſortes whoſe pleaſure commaundement men hoſte gladly obeyed neuertheleſſe whan hearde haſdruball ſonne gyſgon hande army myndynge dyſtroye vtterly romaynes lefte alſo whan ſawe theyr newe capitayne makynge redy people auauncyng ſtanderdes remembryng theyr olde noble capytaines great power wherwith wont go batayles coulde forbeare wepe lament theyr myſhappe ſuche wyſe nother theyr pety capitaynes yet martius hym ſelfe myght appeaſe yet dyd ſometime rebuke theyr feminine vnprofitable wepinges ſometyme ſtyrre defende ſelues countrey alſo reuenge deathe theyr olde noble capitaynes late ſlayne whyle thus ſpendyng tyme vnprofytably theyr ennemies hande redye aſſaile enter campes romaine tournyng teares furious rage haſte toke armure weapon defended entry campe alſo iſſued fierſely ranne ennemies whiche kepte good aray ſo littell myſtruſted ſuch reſiſtence ſodayne iſſuing cauſed carthaginenſes ſtriken feare alſo meruaile howe romaine hoſte ſo ſhortly encreaſed whiche ſo late almooſte wholly ſlayn put vtterance muſed alſo ſodayne courage hardyneſſe newe capytaine myght haue truſte two scipio beinge ſlaine feare dout beganne ſomwhat giue backe romaine folowed vppon ſoo conſtrayned flee flyght many hadde bene ſlayne elles folowers hadde bene putte greatte hurte dyſpleaſure theyr faſte purſuite hadde martius hym ſelfe ſounde retreate halfe agaynſte theyr wylles ſtayed theym frome chaſe broughte theym backe theyr tentes beynge ſtyll hotte fyerſe deſyrous ſlaughter reuenge theym enenmies carthaginenſes fledde faſte ſeaſon laſte ſeynge noo manne folowe thought feare durſte noo longer purſue theym wherefore made noo ſuche haſte wente ſoftely theyr campe whanne come thither alſo regarded greatly good watche kepynge therof lefte thinges negligently vnſurely nothynge myſtruſting ennemies hande demed remenaunt leauynges two hoſtes lately beaten nowe beynge gathered togyther neglygence carthaginenſes knowen martius eſpies wherefore fyrſte apparance ſemed rather raſſhely boldly enterpryſe night folowinge inuade theym theyr tentes fielde thinking eaſye wynne campe haſdruball alone beinge ſodainly taken vnprouided ſhoulde able defende owne campe fielde taried tyll iii capitaines carthaginenſes theyr arinies ioyned togither agayne neuertheleſſe wold ſodainly night time enterpriſe ſo high feate thought fyrſt make companye priuie therof alſo make vnto oration whiche began wiſe ¶ greatte loue haue euer borne vnto oure good capytaynes louynge ſouldiours welle whan onlyue alſo nowe deade preſente fortune tyme ſufficient perſwade man greatte authoritie rule goodnes ye haue gyuen weighty full care trouble although mynde ſore troubled diſquieted almoſte tyme fynde comfort conſolation onely whan feare dryueth away ſorowes thereof yet dolour onely conſtrayned comforte relieue ſorowes neyther whan deuyſynge meanes may ſaue preſerue leauynges two romaine hoſtes wealthe countrey tyme quitte ridde ſorowes euen thanne two scipio bothe daye nyghte doo vexe trouble ſommetyme dreames appeere vnto many tymes awake ſlepes cōmanding leaue yet noble ſouldiours cōpanions cōmon welth vnreuenged intent folow rule diſcipline haue taught while lyuing man obedient commandement thā ſo lykewyſe ar departed ſhall always glad thyng ſuppoſe wold haue done yf werehere v lyuing wold ye ſhuld thynke beſt worthy warriours mourne weepe theym though cleane deade ſens lyue perpetually noble fame honorable actes whan ſo euer ye ſhall going battayle remembre wolde haue ſo vahantly fight though ye ſawe ſetting furthe baners diſplayde exhortyng wyn honour imagination cauſed yeſterday ſo manfully vanquyſſhe put flyght youre enemy wherfore moche deſyrous proue whether ſo hardy owne pleaſure dare vndertake moche deſyre exhortation youre capitayne yeſterday whan called backe chaſe enmies dyd plucke downe ſtomakes quench noble courage deferre ſame greatter honour alſo better oportunitie intente beinge prepared therfore may aſſayle theym vnpurueyde ſame armed may take vnarmed ſlepe enemy thinke nothyng leſſe beinuaded v campe whome accompt people beſieged within owne campe let v nowe therfore enterpryſe whiche man thinke dare enterpryſe ſhall founde moſte eaſy ſemed moſte harde compaſſed ſelfe wyll guide dead night leade ſo ſecretly ſuche ſilence wyll within theyr campe er ſhalbe ware comming aſcertained kepe watche order campe ſhall wyn fyrſt brunt let ſee make ſlaughter amonge intended yeſterday haue made whā againſt wylles called back frō purſuit thē wherwith ye angry enterpriſe know great hardy ſuche neceſſitie ſuche coū ſels beſt whan occaſion offred oportunitie ſerueth muſte taken el wyll flee away without recouerie one theyr army hande two farre henſe nowe yf aſſayle one hoſte may fynde oportunitie haue ſome equall matche ye haue alredy yeſterday aſſayed bothe owne ſtrength theyrs caſe delay beinge contented yeſterdays honour ieoperdy leſt capitayns power come togither howe ſhall able ſuſtein power thre army gouernours cn scipio army able withſtand diuyding hoſtes two noble capitaynes ſlayne lykewyſe enemy beinge diuided ſeuered may v oppreſſed way none v take nowe loke oportunitie next night wherfore name goddis go ye reſtes cheriſhe body whan call ſtrong luſty maye enter campe ennemies ſame hertes courage late ye defended owne campe ¶ newe counſaile newe capitayn wel heard ſo moche ioyfully receiued howe moche acte ſemed bolde hardy wherfore prepared thynges redyneſſe departure reſted ſelues reſt day good part night martius cauſed called vp ſette theym ſecretely way forwarde aboute thre clocke mydnyght armye carthaginenſes ſeuen myles beyonde campe haſdruball ſonne gyſgon myddes waye holowe valeye therin lyttell woode woode martius ſent embuſhement romaine horſemen receyue ſuche fledde frome fyrſte campe wolde eſcape whan demed ſaid embuſhement come thither reſt company went next campe fynding watche reſiſtence entred tentes eaſily might haue done theyr owne ſodainly blew vp trum pettes made great clamour noyſe ſome ſlewe ennemies ſlepyng ſome ſet tentes fyre many kept entre gate campe none ſhulde iſſue thus ſodayne noyſe fyre ſlaughter ſo amaſed wyſt fledde gate receiued armed men ſlaine whan perceiued gate ſo hepte many ſaue liues lep touer dyches cloſures campe thynking flee next campe carthaginenſes alſo receiued romayn embuſhement ſlayne ſo none eſcaped eſcaped could haue brought word newes campe romaine came theym ſelues ſuche ſpede made go ſecōd campe ſo ſlaine oppreſſed firſt fielde thus breake day came ſecond campe found thinges vnready fyrſte ſome gone forthe woode ſome ragynge ſome vytailes many walked vp downe gate campe vnarmed many layed downe take theyr reſte romaynes beynge yet fyers theyr late victory ſlewe fyrſte ſuche made reſyſtence entre campe entred made great ſlaughter great noyſe many aroſe armed came defence fyelde thereby battayle ſeaſon cruel ſtronge ſone perceyued freſhe blodde romayns ſhyeldes whyche ſygne deathe companye ſtryken ſuche feare fledde many myght ſundry wayes ſo nyght morninge martius vanquyſhed ii hoſtes carthaginenſes flewe xxxvii men footemen ſtuffe daunger ¶ thus reaſonyng debatyng dyuerſe dayes employed tyll footemen cariage eſcaped great parte hoſt illuſion eſcaped began haſdruball ſtaye ſtyffe agreing couenauntes ſo muche began diſſent dyuers artycles whervnto aſſented feare leſſed faythe alſo decreſſed next morning appered great darke myſte vpon ground wel hilles valeys whiche ſerued wel haſdruball purpoſe thinking good houre come ſent nero conſull aduertyſing hym ſame day euer ben kepte bye holy ſacred amonge carthaginenſes ſo ſame lawfull hym trauayle buſyneſſe wherfore deſyred communication deferred tyll daie folowyng conſull yet thynkyng fraude deceite meſſage agreed thervnto haſdruball ſpede iſſued ſtrayte reſte hoſte horſemen eliphantes ſmall noiſe could make paſſed daunger daye waxed clere whē ſon began appere thē nero perceiuing campe carthaginenſes voyde knowyng many feſtly theyr departure theyr vntrueth mocke illuſion made muche ſpede coulde folowe ennemyes feruent deſyre fyght yf myght augment armie nero conſull ſende alſo ſame newe capitayne called proconſull theyr doubte ſhulde aſſygne office ſuccede place two ſo noble capitaynes late ſlayne ſpace xxx dayes daie appoynted commune amonge worthy rome office ſodeinly yonge p cornelius scipio ſonne ſlayne spaine xxiiii yeres old ſtode vp high place al mē myght well ſee beholde hym deſyred ſame offyce myght gyuen vnto hym declared mynde anon hole multitude eſtates gaue hym conſent criyng luckie empire spayne ¶ soone haſtie election ſodeyne ſylence amonge multitude men began ſecretly ſelues conſyder haſte nomination meruaylyng alſo forthinkyng fauoured perſon affection conſider youth theyr reaſon many miſlyked fortune happed ſtocke familie ſame countrei ſome ſorye ſende one ſame kyn name gouerne countreie father vncle ſlayne lay buryed ¶ yonge scipio perceyued ſilence repentaunce haſtie election deſired lyttell giue audience made ſuch oration excuſe age concerning rule affayres commytted ſuch herte courage onely enflamed hertes ardent deſyre loue towarde hym alſo fulfylled certeyne hope proſperous ſucceſſe empyre yonge man beſyde many marueylous vertues good quality wher naturally indewed alſo infancie wonderfull counning gifte noble auauncing ſettyng furth ſame somtime amonge commune people woulde ſhewe certayne dreames viſions nyght ſometime woulde declare vnto thinges commanded inwardly goddes
