ſodaynly glide vanyſhe away ¶ fayned inuention conception ſuperſtitious myndes people towarde hym woulde nother affyrme true nother ſaye falſe vntrewe couertly left dwell ſtyll theyr owne opinion wherby men ſuche admiration hym ſuffred hym enioy great roume el full vnmete yong age army ſhuld vnder hym spayne increaſed tenne thouſand fotemen one horſemen iulius sullanus appoynted helpe hym buſy affayres charge ¶ newe army nauy xxx ſhyppes departed italy makyng great ſpede tylle arryued spayne gathered togither power remained ſo ſobrely handled ſelf al men woordes iudged bothe royall maieſtie ſtedfaſt faythfulnes prayſed moch ſouldiours whiche founde fyrſt withſtanding theyr ii great loſſes men capitayns yet kept ſtill cuntrey defendyng manfully frendis many city ſame alſo ſuffred theyr ennemies enioy proſperous fortune whiche loſſe romayns one gyuen thyrdly driuen ennemies forſake theyr abode lide water iberus aboue lucius martius great honour veneration anon cōmyng beſtowed newe menne warre place ſhuld remaine winter ſeaſon hym ſelfe thinges ordinately diſpoſed went tarracon ¶ fame scipio leſſe among ennemies thā among frendes alſo certaine feare hym coniecturyng ſecrete diuination likely ſucceſſe thynges enſue feared hym hadde cauſe feared hym moche cauſe reaſon theyr feare hydde vnknowen perplexitie mynde departed army went dyuers partes wynter ſeaſon haſdruball ſonne gyſgon went ſea toward pyllars hercules mago kept myddell cuntrey haſdruball ſonne amilcar lay nigh riuer iberus farre sagunt ¶ oration scipio ſouldyours spayne commyng thyther cap xliiii ſpryng yere p scipio cōmanded ſhyppes furniſhed men vitailes munimentes warre mete hym mouthe ryuer iberus reſt hoſte cominge lande tarracon mette thinkyng neceſſary hym declare mynde olde ſouldyours lefte spayne laſte great loſſe ſlaughter romaynes called togyther made oration hereafter foloweth ¶ neuer newe capitayn cauſe gyue thankes vnto ſouldyours hadde tryed theyr hardines diligence bataile fortune hath boūd vnto louinge ſouldiours knewe countreye ſawe place campe fyrſte loue obedience ye haue borne father mine vncle bothe quycke deade ſecundarily whan hole countrey loſte reaſon greate diſtruction people yet noble vertue myghte haue obteyned poſſeſſion ſame agayne bothe romaynes alſo theyr deputie ſucceſſour ſayd father vncle ſens fauour goddis intende worke may dwell spayne ſtyll ſelues carthaginenſes ſhall haue dwellyng nother onely reſtraine ſhall come ſyde bankes water iberus intend paſſe ſame floode army gyue battayle feare leſt ſhall thoughte counſayle hardy ſpoken myne age wyſe conſyderynge late loſſe haue wherby tyme ſhuld ſerue v vndertake ſuche great enterpryſes noo manne hath cauſe remembre euyll fortune batayle spayne haue father myne vncle ſlayne within ſpace thyrty day ye wold ſay make heape corp family one vpon neuertheleſſe loſſe lacke frendes diſpleaſant mynde men euen ſo doth fortune noble vertuouſe courage forbyd man ſuche caſe diſpayre ſpecially ſens thorough fatall fortune chaunce hath heretofore bene haue bene beaten ſuſteined great loſſes beginning yet laſt haue euer ouercome ennemies ſuppreſſed v wyll reherſe olde hyſtories warres porſena frenchman samnite wyll onely remembre warres theſe ennemies carthaginenſes many nauies ſhyppes howe many capitaynes howe many army loſt fyrſt battayles theym tyme anniball nowe tyme trebia traſymenus canna thinges appere hole armyes theyr capitaynes romayne conſuls ſlayne furthermore howe great parte italy sardinia sicilia haue forſaken romaynes folowe amitie anniball nigh citie rome pytched campe ye hym ſelf ſene almoſt ride hard gate rome tyme great ruyne hard fortune hertes vertue courage romaynes remayned ſtyl ſtedfaſt hole vnmouable wherby haue ben euer ſuſteyned ſet vp agayne cruell batayle canna haſdruball great armye goynge ouer mountaynes italye helpe brother anniball ioyne theyr power together whych done accordynge intent hadde thys day ben almoſt memorye name romayns left ye hardy ſouldyours gouernaunce father withſtode theim good fortune ſo wel ſped therby euel chaunces hapned v wel releued nowe goodnes goddes dayly ioyfull proſperous sicilia great city syracuſa agrigentum wonne agayn hole ile brought vnto obedience romaine ennemies clene expulſed italy capua taken arpines brought vnder ſubiection rome anniball gret feare fleing frō rome nowe bryuen angle countrey brutians dayly prayer maketh goddes aboue al thinges may ſafe ſound eſcape without daunger countrey ennemies wherfore frendes nothyng vnmete contrary reaſon haue al aduerſitie lowe ebbe goddes ſelues almoſt annibals partie yet guyding father frendes haue ſuſteyned borne vp eſtate romaynes ye nowe al thynges ar mery proſperous ſhoulde ſhrynke ſuffre harte fayle nowe immortall goddes gouernours romayne empyre wylled people rome one aſſent elect vnto gret offyce dignitie ſame goddes ſundry preſages ſignes dreames nyght haue ſhewed thynges hereafter ſhal haue proſperous ſucceſſe ye moſt time regarde harte giueth ere long al spaine ſhalbe ſo many beare name carthaginenſe ſhall gladde feare flee hen lande ſea reaſon alſo gyueth ſame whiche herte conceyued muſt nedes trewe dyuers theyr frendes whyche haue theym ben euil intreted haue late ſent embaſſadours v ſocours agayne thre captaines whiche agree among ſelues whiche cauſe haue deuided theyr armye three partes departed farre ſundre wherfore ſame fortune ſkourged diſtroyed v doth nowe come theim felowes friendes truſt gone theim euen people called celtiberi departed forſoke • hadde moſte nede theim alſo haue deuided ſeuered theyr hoſtes cauſe deſtruction bothe father myne vncle diſcorde wyll ſuffer theim ioyne gether againe ye ſure one armie theim ſelfe able withſtande wherfore moſte hertely pray good ſouldiours loue fauour nowe name scipions whiche ſonne olde capitaine scipio impe growen ye woulde ſaye ſtocke cut downe grounde ye olde knightes ſo worke ye may brynge yonge capitaine newe armie ouer iberus countrey ye haue paſſed many great actes prowes ſhewed doubte ſhortly bringe paſſe ye nowe knowe ſimilitude reſemblaunce father vncle face countenaunce feature body euen ſo ſhall ye ſee alſo exaumple theyr witte faith vertue ſuche wyſe euery one ſhall ſaye scipio olde capitaine alyue agayne ¶ citie newe carthage hiſpayne romaynes great praye golde ſiluer neceſſaries warre pledge noble menne city spayne capi xlv vvhen theſe exhortation kendeled hertes men lefte behinde hym kepe countreye sillanus three thouſande fotemen thre hundred horſemen reſt armye xxv thouſande fotemen ii thouſande v c horſemen paſſed ryuer iberus paſſed ouer many counſailed hym ſeinge army carthaginenſes deuydedinto thre partes ſhulde aſſaile hoſt theim next vnto hym ſayenge peryll ioyned together leſt ſhulde able reſyſte theim imagined mynde woulde fyrſte aſſaulte carthago noua whiche onely ryche rycheſſe inhabitantes ſame alſo riche meanes carthaginenſes leyde theyr treaſure armour moche apparayll warre remayned alſo citie pledge noble men citees spayne beſyde citie ſituate vpon ſea whenſe eaſy paſſe ouer affrica hauen alſo therof able receyue eaſely greateſt nauye prynce ¶ purpoſe man priuye onely lelius gouernour ſhyppes armye ſea whome commaunded ſoo tempre courſe ſhyppes armye lande ſea myghte bothe ſodaynely appeere carthage one tyme whyche charge dewely putte execution ſeuenthe daye theyr departynge frome iberus mette newe carthage incontynente campe made tentes pytched northe ſyde citie ¶ nowe ſyte ſytuation carthage manier myddell spayne greatte boſome goulfe whyche ſea hath full courſe within lande lengthe fyue hundred paſſes breadthe ſea ſame place muche ſame quantitie inner parte furtheſt ende goulfe hylle whyche citie buylded two partes ſaye eaſte ſyde ſouthe ſyde encloſed ſea whyche frome ſayde goulfe boſome rounneth lande one ſyde citie vppon weaſte ſyde defended greatte brode poole rounneth vp alſo good part northe ſyde towne deepeneſſe poole noo certayntie ſea dothe aryſe heyghte ebbe lowe ſoo water thereof deepe ſhalowe ¶ thus cytie partes enuyronned water ylande oneles part northſyde mayne lande paſſeth ii hundred fyfty pace bredth wherfore ſens grounde broder scipio intended make trench part thought hym ſelfe ſtronge ynough keepe lyttell peece grounde ennemies alſo thintent myght tymes haue recourſe view walles ſtrength towne ¶ whan scipio ordered thinges ordinately vpon lande aſſaulte went hauen lyke maner ordered ſhippes men might appere citizen ſhoulde aſſaulted well water lande alſo commaunded watche kepte vpon water night ſeaſon euery ſhyppe thynges prudently appoynted retourned campe wyllyng dyd thing touching aſſault inſtruct admonyſhe people mynd concerning ſame comfort theym enterpryſe called togither made oration wyſe ¶ ſo euer beleueth good ſouldiours ye nowe brought hyther aſſault wynne one towne dothe conſyder labour peyne therin profyte ſhall enſue therof trewe ye ſhall aſſault ſkale walles one onely towne obteynyng one ye alſo ſhall wynne whole cuntrey spayne towne pledge noble men kynges people spayne one taken full ſhortly ſhall cauſe euer carthaginenſes doo nowe poſſede yelded vnto v vnder dominon alſo al money treſure ennemies whiche taken ſhall able longer maynteyne warres ſeinge haue many hyred ſtraungers theyr army ſame treaſure ſhall meruaylouſly profyte v therby wynne hertes loue theſe barbarous people beſyde remaineth theyr ordināce armour al abilimentes neceſſary warre whiche beynge one wonne ſhall ſerue well pourpoſe therof make ennemies bare theyr vtter diſtruction furthermore ſhall lordes fayre ryche citie whervnto lyeth goodly hauen whereby ſhall ſerued ſea lande thinges ſhall tyme lacke hauing theſe thynges ſhal pleſant profitable v alſo lacke ſame ſhal muche greatter hyndrance loſſe ennemies citie hath theyr greatteſt ſtrength theyr ſtore houſes corn̄e theyr treaſaurye theyr armory theyr houſes ſtuffed thynges neceſſarye theyr ſhyppes warre generally citie onely receptacle haue hyther lyeth ryght courſe ſea affrica spayn nowe ſens perceyue ye ſufficiently inſtructed haue thinges good ordre mete purpoſe lette v good hertes ſtrength make haſte aſſaultyng newe carthage ¶ therwithall euery man loude voice aſſented therto thinkyng ſlacke buſynes went furthe towarde carthage cauſing aſſauted water lande ¶ ſyde mago capitain cartha ginenſes perceiuing aſſault ordeined giuen ſea land diſpoſed men within towne maner two towneſmen cauſed armed put aray part towne romain tētes campe fiue c men appoynted kepe caſtell v c aſſigned remayne vppon hylle within citie towarde eaſte reſt people commanded redy helpe ſuccour company place towne ſo euer ſawe moſt nede reſiſt whan ſo euer herde crye made parte violent force aſſauting ſodainly gate open wherat cauſed ii ſouldiours towne iſſue vpon romains whoſe fyrſt cōming scipio cauſed men recule backe thintent might draw towne nere reſte romayne army fyrſt battayle ſtyf • e well maynteined partes whan carthaginēſes per ceiued ſo great numbre cominge tentes romains ſuccour felowes fledde greate feare towarde citie chaſed ſlayne harde theyr gate cauſed leſſe tremblyng citie battayle ſo moche diuers place walles lefte bare naked without men defende ſame euery man lept appoynted place ſo great ſodayne theyr feare perceiued well scipio ſtandyng hyll without towne wherefore commaunded ſouldiours come tentes ſpedyly aſſaulte towne bring theim ſcalyng ladder commaundement fulfylled fyght ſtrong bothe partes encourage people scipio hym ſelfe came thyther vnder couert ſhyldes paueſſes withſtande ſhotte came walles arowes dartes ingynnes whiche greate ſomtyme exhorted coumforted men ſomtime counſayled beſt attayning theyr purpoſe preſence awytneſſe bothe ofmens valyant courage alſo theyr cowardyſe wherby euery man enforced hym ſelfe clymmevp neyther regardynge heyghte walles fearyng men armes fierſely defended walles ſyde towne lyke aſſault gyuen ſhyppes part laye towarde water ſmall purpoſe mago ſo furnyſhed walles armed men euer bryngynge theym plenty dartes ordinance roman loſt wāne aboue al thinges ſauing town height walles wherby fewe ladder able reche toppe ſame thoſe ladder wer longeſt wer therto moſt weake ſo whan one aſcended vp wolde alſo clyme theron ſo heauy burden loded many brake great hurt climers whervpon scipio cō ſidering vaine labour cauſed wery company withdraw reſt wherby carthaginēſes wer eaſed releued preſent feare danger alſo therby toke hardy courage opinion citie danger taking aſſault wer ſtrong inough defend tyll capitaines carthaginenſes army might haue time inough come reſcous reiſe ſiege drewthen towarde middel day certain fyſſhermen tarracon ben fiſhing botes ſaid great large poole lay northweſt part towne certified scipio water therof low ebbe alſo northwind quicke driuing waues tide cauſed lower vale lightly ſeen ſo men might well wade ouer walles citie water moſt place paſt middell man ſome partes paſt knee ſtrange fortune vnſeen lowe ebbe water scipio tourned myracle ſayinge wille pleaſure goddis withdraw time water great pole make romains paſſage open way neuer man paſſed theſe ſtronge perſuaſions cauſed reſt army reſted thē tentes time firſt aſſault take ladder engine gyue newe aſſault ſame place beaten back began fierſe cruel bickering neuertheleſſe height walles ſo beneficiall citezens neuer ſo valiante hardy yet vp could get ouerthrowen ſmall peyne townes men ¶ buſy attentife defende citie well ſea coſt scipio good numbre ſtronge men ſecretely withdrewe hym ſayd ponde bad companye folowe god neptunus ſhulde theyr guide way ſhalowe water whervpon ſmall labour went ouer ſet vp ladder walles found eaſy ſcaled kept men warre hauinge ſure hope naturall ſtrengthe parte reaſon water made munimentes defence yet lefte watch euery man gone defence partes thaſſault ſemed moſt fierſe dangerouſe ſo without reſiſtence entred towne incontinent made haſt come gate battaile moſt buſy ſtrong whā wer com found al townſmen ſo erneſt defēce cōforting felowes neither herd ſaw roman tyl perceiued backes throwing dartes ſleynge partes nother tyl time knewe town thā anon wer gate broken gret nū bre armed mē entred gate many time goten ouer walles ſom went incontinent towne ſleyng met company wente araye market place myddel citie perceyued theyr ennemies fleyng ſome hyl within towne kepte v c men warre mago great numbre fledde caſtel scipio ſent parte hoſt ſayd hyll whiche anone wonne people ſlayne el taken reſt wente aſſaulte caſtel whiche mago ſeaſon valyantly defended ſeyng towne full ennemies lyke haue ſocours yelded vp ſelfe caſtell romaynes ceaſſed make ſlaughter citie euery man wente ſpoile towne praye whereof greate well golde ſyluer ordinaunce artyllary corne ſhyppes iron laten many thinges mete apparel ſhippes certayntie wherof wyll reherſe writars vary moch therin alſo x pryſoners taken wherof many citizen scipio let go libertie ſuffered dwel ſtyl towne enioy moche goodes ſpoyled amonge priſoners two craftes men cauſed bōd men worke common profytte citie rome puttyng comfort ſhould within ſhorte ſpace made free wolde labour worke earneſtely ſuche neceſſaryes ſhoulde haue nede warre greate noumber reſt ſeruauntes luſty yonge men ſent rower ſhyppes galeys place ſuche lacked alſo encreaſed nauy eyght ſhyppes wel furniſhed beſide al theſe priſoners alſo pledge noble men city greate noumbre whome cauſed well kepte gently entreated reſt daye scipio gaue lycence wery men reſt theym ſelues fewe al daye ben ſore trauayled fyghtyng one place cuſtody towne gaue cn lelius company ſee men ſelfe wente tentes ¶ gentylnes scipio reſtoryng fayre yonge virgin vndefiled luceius vnto ſhe fyaunced cap xlvi morowe aſſembled hoſte togyther fyrſt gaue humble thankes praiſe goddis gyuen handes one day ſo great ſo noble ſo riche citie lyke wherof found spain ennemies gathered togither treaſure bothe affrica alſo spayne ſuch abundance lyttell nothyng left thē romayns hauyng great plenty thinges nexte muche prayſed noble courage valyantnes men warre nother ſodayne excurſation theyr ennemies towne nother hygh walles water ſame coulde make afrayde let theyr enterpryſe nother yet theyr caſtels ſtrong towres coulde reſiſt theyr power aboue praiſed muche twayn firſt ſcaled walles entred towne eche gaue crowne good value ſouldiours rewarded euery man vertue merites ſpecially cn lelius gouernour nauye prayſed muche loued whome gaue rewarde crowne golde xxx ox ¶ cauſed pledge brought willyng good comforte ſhuld conſider wer power romayns whoſe naturall propretie deſire bynde men throughe theyr benefytes ſhewinge loue rather compulſion kepe men feare leauer ioyne ſtrange nation amitie faithfull felowſhyp ſorowfully kepe myſerable ſeruitude toke name city pledge ambaſſadours chaunce hym preſent ſayde city incontinent delyuered pledge vnto theim city ſent meſſangers wyllynge theim ſend vnto theim ſhulde haue theyr pledge frely delyuered alſo taken many noble matrones honeſt maydens committed ſobre honeſt men kept without force diſhonour done vnto among captiues one virgin brought vnto hym ſo excellent beautie ſo euer ſhe went men delyted beholde scipio enquired cuntrey ſhe kynred ſhe deſcended perceyned ſhe betrouthed made ſure yong prince celtiberiās whoſe name luceius wherevppon incontinent ſent ſaid yonge man alſo parentes whoſe coming knowyng yonge man ſoore enamoured thus ſayd vnto hym yonge man haue ſente alſo yong man come cauſe whan yong maiden fianced enſured brought ſoldiors herd ſay entierly loued beautie witneſſeth haue good cauſe ſo might laufully enioy pleaſaunt loue otherwyſe occupied mynde affayres commune welthe coulde perchaunce beare loue deſyre enioy ſame nowe wyll beare fauour loue ryght ought haue hath bene well honourably kept virginite preſerued though ſhe dwelled ſtyl owne parentes thintent might make preſent moſt acceptable conſeruation mine honor gift require one reward hēsforth becom louing frēd romās ye eſteme good honorable man father vncle reputed thinke noble citie rome many like vnto v truſt neuer people daye founde earth wyll gladder haue loue frend ſhyppe ye wolde ſory haue diſpleaſure yong man gret thankes gyuen hym praide goddes rewarde goodnes power ſuffiſed parentes mayden called forthe broughte great ſumme golde redemption theyr chyld perceiued giuen frely huſband deſired take parte therof theyr gyfte declaration theyr good hertes towardes hym affirminge receyuinge therof ſhulde ioyfull vnto reſtitution theyr dowghter vndefiled ¶ scipio beinge ouercome theyr longe vehement interceſſion cauſed ſayde ſumme layde grounde fete callinge luceius againe hym ſayde beſyde dowere ye ſhal receyue father lawe mariage doughter ye ſhall alſo take gyfte dower hande whiche great gift alſo moch honour hym done beſyde retourned home houſe countrey declaring euery man honour magnifycence scipio ſayinge yonge man come moſt lyke vnto god bothe power warre alſo gentilneſſe liberalitie peace ouercome countrey yonge gentilman leauing houſe familye good ordre ſhortely retourned scipio bringynge hym cccc good horſemen ayde ſocour romaynes ¶ scipio ſent c lelius rome beare tidynges victory hym ſent mago xv ſenatours newe carthage whiche wer takynge ſame citie taken alſo priſoners repaired broken walles citie ſet therin ſufficient numbre ſouldiours defence ſame remoued tarracon whyther apoynted legate olde friendes alſo newe gotten acqueintaunce reſorte communication theyr aliaunce procedynge theyr affaire ¶ anniball ſleith cn fuluius xiii romaynes beſide herdonea marcellus conſull chaſith anniball apulia makyng many ſhirmiſhes hym ca xlvii eſtate warres spayne durynge whiche tyme conſull marcellus toke salapia treaſon ii townes samnite force ſlewe iii men warre whiche anniball lefte kepyng ſame townes cn fuluius proconſull truſting wynne herdonea anniball ſtronge ſelfe neither garnyſon left ſufficient defence therof remoued thyther army hauyng hope comfort atteyne ſame knew wel annibal loſſe salapia departed cuntrey brutians ſuche ſure frendes anniball towne herdonea ſent hym priuyly worde meſſangers deſyrous kepe ſtyl old frendes haſted ſo horſemen lyghteſt footemen makyng ſo great iourneys alredy com nere herdonea fame comīg wer well knowen put romayns feare appered good aray battaile ſodainly baners diſplaied whiche fuluius perceiuynge lyke hardynes made ſpede put folke aray ioyned battayle hym anniball cōmanded horſemen ſigne token theim made while romains buſy battail againſt footemen euery man eye wer occupied buſyly ſhoulde ſecretelye cooſte fielde parte ſet vpon backes ennemies one parte inuade campe tentes greate noyſe ſlaughter ſaying truſted vanquyſhe fuluius ii yeres paſte ouercome fuluius name ſame cuntrey hope nothing deceyued ſo ſoone horſemen aſſailed romayns theyr backes great feare ſlaughter anon campe hearde great crye wherby romayns kept aray fought boldly ſo diſinayd ſome fledde many mo ſlayne among ſaid fuluius xii tribune xiii romayns ſlayne theyr campe ſtuffe taken ¶ anniball truſtyng nothyng ſtrengthe towne remoued inhabitantes therof metapontus thurines ſlew capitains therof ſecrete cōmunication conſull ſet town fyre ¶ marcellus conſulle baynge nothynge afrayde tydinges loſſe ſente letter ſenate rome byddynge whytte diſcomforted therwith doubted wolde cauſe anniball haue ſhort ioy victory whervpō immediately remoued toward annibal pitchyng campe playne fieldes euen ſyght ennemies ſoone valyantly came furthe order battayle redy fyght ſyde anniball leſſe quicke battayle betwene bothe horſemen footemen meruaylous fiers cruell neither ceaſſed tyll nyght departed thē indifferēt loſſe party night anniball ſecretly remoued went apulia marcellus mornyng perceyuynge departure ennemies folowed incontinent ouertoke theim nere vnto venuſia thus paſſed apulia without notable battaile one folowinge euer anniball wolde remoue nyght ſekyng place deceiue ennemies conſull always folowed day tyme ſendynge hym eſpies ſure crafty trayne anniball ¶ ſummer almoſt ended tyme choſynge conſuls drewe nere whiche chuſyng marcellus ſhulde haue hym ſelfe ſent letter rome affyrmynge ſhulde ryght hurtfull common welth yf dyd depart one foote anniball abſence yea onely ceaſſyng aſſayle hym ſhulde gyue hym moche courage whervpon cōmaunded abyde ſtylle army conſul liuius ſent choſen conſuls q fabius maximus q fuluius flaccus beſyde determined claudius marcellus ſhulde kepe alſo army warres agaynſt anniball one yere longar ¶ touchynge warres spayne ordeyned publius scipio sullanus ſhoulde gouernours onely yere vnto tyme called ſame ſenate ¶ aboute tyme came ambaſſadours kynge syphax affrica rome ſhewynge proſperous battayles hadde fought carthaginenſes deſyrynge haue amitie romaynes agreed hym whole ſenate whyche moued betwene hym two bretherne cneius p scipio spayne whoſe ambaſſadours ſenatours gaue gentyl thankes louynge anſweres alſo ſent kyng ryche preſentes ¶ longe tidinges wer brought rome affrica maſſaniſſa ſonne kynge gala come carthage v numidian great numbre affricans wer hyred go ouer spayne aſdruball intent ſtrongly accompanied might depart ſhortly then italy brother annibal iudged hope theyr victory reſt ¶ ſame time came lelius spayne rome bryngynge hym great numbre priſoners reherſynge ſenate houſe happy wynnynge newe carthage one daye gettyng many newe friendes spaine theſe newes made theim ſo mery comming aſdruball italy made theim afrayde conſyderinge come theyr power ſkant able reſiſte onely power anniball neuertheleſſe good chere coulde diſcharged lelius ſendyng hym agayne spayne ſhyppes came hym ¶ marcellus gyueth battayle anniball whiche men put flyght wherupon maketh ſharpe oration reneweth battayll morowe putt • th anniball hoſt flight loſſe many men cap xlviii newe conſull leauynge thynges good order rome departed towardes warres q fuluius flaccus paſſed capua whome q fabius made inſtant requeſte departed wolde kepe ſtrayght quicke warres anniball whyles dyd beſiege citie tarent whiche citie myghte one take frome hym ſhulde haue place ſure go neyther knowe coſt myght ſafely tourne hym ſo ſhuld afterwarde haue ſmall cauſe abide italy ſame requeſt alſo made marcellus letter thynkynge man italy ſo able matche anniball hym ſelfe ſo kendeled ſtirred fabius letter ſo ſone wynter paſſed fode founde fieldes able ſuſteyne army cattel went canuſium annibal laye hadde moued ruler towne yelde vnto hym leauyng romayne amitie ſo ſone parceyued marcellus come remoued thenſe leauynge playne countrey ſought hylly woddy countrey whiche myght apte traynes deceipte ennemies ¶ marcellus euer folowed harde ioyning almoſt campe campe dyuers ſkyrmyſhes made betwene horſe men bothe partes anniball mynding ieoparde one fledde hym nyghte laſt ouertoke hym playne fielde anniball cauſed campe trenched fortified marcellus men let workes therof ſo whether wold enforced batayl thyng moſt eſchued wherefore ordered theyr army bothe party fought tyll nyght departed morowe marcellus early put men good aray anniball dydde ſame exhortyng men remembre noble conqueſtes traſymenus canna ſuffre theyr gredye vnreaſonable ennemy ſo vexe might haue tyme incampe ſelues ye ſcarſely loke aboute take breathe ſonne whan ryſeth romain army bothe one tyme appere fieldes caſe ſaythe ye ſo handle hym may one departe loſſe men fielde wil herafter eaſy intreate theſe exhortation alſo euyl contented tedious continuall purſuing theyr enemy fierſly went battaile fought cruelly ſpace ii longe houres laſt ryght wynge romayns gaue backe whoſe place fulfyll marcellus appoynted legion men armes company fyrſt reculed feare ſo came fayntly place laſt romayn hoſt fearefull ſhamefaſt began flee ſlayn day romains ii thouſand ſeuen hundred wherof iiii wer capitaines hundreders two tribune ¶ marcellus come campe made ſouldiours ſo ſoore cruell oration wordes angry capitayne ſemed diſpleaſaunt peynefull trauayle toke battaylle daie ¶ moche bounde ſayth immortall goddes ye ſo fearfully toumbled together tentes chaunced ennemy victory aſſayle campe alſo fayle loke feare ye left battayle lyke feare alſo ye forſaken campe ſodayne feare hath nowe inuaded thynge hath cauſed ſo ſone forget bothe eſtate ſelfe alſo ennemies ye remembre theſe ſame ennemies ye ouercame purſued laſt ſōmer theſe ſame whome fleinge bothe daye night ye chaſed cūtreis ye ſame yeſterday ye wold neither ſuffer flee yet gyue theim ſo moche time fortifye theyr fielde wil reherſe thynges wherein ye may glory nowe wyll declare thynges whereof ye ought moche aſhamed yeſter daye ye departed batayle euen hande nowe hath daye nyghte ben ſo greate lette vnto taken army therby whit leſſed theyr power whyt encreaſed truely thinketh nowe ſpeake mine owne company ſouldiours yet romains perceiue nothing theim body armour ye ſame hertes mīdes ennemies ſhuld neuer haue loked backes loſte none ſtandardes time could neuer glorie ſlaughter company yeſterdaie ye gaue honour death felowes ¶ euerie man cried aloude deſirynge pardon daie paſt one againe trie herte courage men ſo euer ſhulde pleaſe nowe ſaide truely wyl proue againe wil morowe morninge ſet forthe araie intent ye vanquiſhers may aſke forgiuenes rather people vanquiſhed ¶ morrowe men well eaten dronken made theim ſtronge ſhould put people order ſet v • warde thoſe fled firſt daye thoſe company loſte ſtandardes beſt lyked comaundinge theim earneſtely fyghte ouercome theyr ennemies ſo victorie preſent daie might fly come rome ſclaunder yeſterdaies flienge ¶ whan anniball herd fierſe courage marcellus ſayd haue nowe ſuche ennemye neyther ſuffre good fortune badde yf ouercom ennemies gredily ſtyl aſſaileth theim whan ouercome alſo fierſly renueth warres vpon theim theſe wordes incontinent brought hoſte furthe fielde battayle cruell daie carthaginenſes euer ſtryuynge kepe honour romaynes auenge ſhame gotten daie aduauntage battayle betweene theim abode longe ſuſpence marcellus preſent witneſſe euer redye comforte exhorte romayn • anniball ſeinge doubtefulneſſe fyght victory putte ennemies ſodayne feare cauſed elephantes ſette agaynſte forewarde whyche fyrſte comynge brought theim order didde theim muche trouble hurte wherby one parte thereof lefte bare voyde reſyſtence reſte fled alſo hadde decius flauius tribune taken ſtanderde one bandes horſemen commaundynge company belongynge ſame ſtanderde folowe hym boldely obeyde incontinent brought theim company elephantes dyd moſte diſpleaſure cauſynge mooſte trouble rumour badde theim couragiouſely throwe theyr dartes ſpeares thoſe beaſtes whyche dyd woundynge many theim feelynge theim ſelues hurt greatte rage runne away coulde ſtayed theim rode theim romaynes folowed theim ſtyll droue thiem vpon theyr owne company spanyardes carthaginenſes makynge greatter ſlaughter amonge theim hadde done romaynes whan ſawe carthaginenſes meane brought array romaine footemen order entred brake aray cleane puttynge theym flyght whō marcellus cauſed horſmen folow chaſe ceaſſed tyl wer driuen yates campe great loſſe bothe men elephantes ſlayne daye viii men fyue elephantes romaine ſlayne thre thouſande many ſore hurt whervpon annibal next nyght folowinge remoued vnto brutians marcellus abode ſeaſon cure hurt ſouldiours ¶ home q fabius maximus recouered anniball citie tarent cap xlix ſeaſon q fabius max conſul toke manduria force then remoued tarent pytchyng tentes hardeby mouth hauen founde certayne ſhyppes whyche liuius late conſull hadde left defence ſhyppes brought vytayle neceſſary prouiſion caſtell theſe ſhyppes alſo came vitayles prouiſion thyther charged ſome gunnes ſtones kynde weapon inuaſiue ſomme laded ſcalyng ladder engyns aſſaulte towne ſoo ſea al thinges wer ready aſſaulte land alſo ordered cōpany ſame help purpoſe acheued ther chaunced ſmall thing eſtimation yet proued meruailous happy ſucceſſe great enterpriſe anniball ſent tarent crue men warre countrey brutians capytayne company meruailouſly enamored yong womā citie whoſe brother ſouldiour hoſt fabius ſiſter ſent worde letter familiaritie new acquaintaunce earneſt louer greate ryches honour whervpon man imaginynge truſtyng alſo loue ſyſter myght leade louer ſo euer ſhe wolde diuiſe conceyued hope good therby touchynge wynnynge towne whervpon ſecretely opened mynde capitayne fabius deſyrynge hym woulde ly • ence hym departe frome armye goo citie whiche woulde vndertake dooe diſſemblynge hym ſelfe ſtolen away company loue ſiſter deſyrouſe cytezen conſull thynkyng proue effecte opynyon ſuffered hym departe thus came ſyſter meanes felle greate familiarite louer capytayne brutianes longe acquayntaunce beganne couertly proue mynde lyttell lyttell whan founde ſome towardneſſe hym ſette ſyſter hande hym fayre flatterynge woordes ſoo compaſſed hym haue loue conſented betraiynge parte citie wher rular capytayne ¶ whan agreed tyme maner circumſtaunce purpoſe ſouldyour ſecretly nyghte lette furthe towne came capitayn declarynge vnto hym hadde doone waye ſhoulde take achieue enterpryſe tyme houre appoynted whiche begynnynge nyght conſull hadde prepared ſea ſyde hauen ſhyppes menne warre thereto appoynted ſhoulde vyolentely aſſaulte towne parte romaynes caſtell theyr force alſo ſhulde aſſayle citizen good numbre hym pryuyly drewe hym eaſte parte towne abode longe ſeaſon withoute makynge noyſe greatte noyſe bruite made purpoſely hauen ſyde ſyde towardes caſtelle leaſte daungier soo democrates capytayne whyche nyghe vnto crew brutians fearynge leſte abſence romaynes myghte chaunce ſyde wynne towne whyche feare moued greatte rumour crye cytezens parte whan hearde thynges quiete reſte parte towne wherin people haſted towarde caſtell ſyde hearde greatteſt noyſe ¶ conſull heringe thenoyſe ceaſſed men armes whiche loude iudging kepers warde gone then commanded ſtreight ſcalynge ladder ſette walles ſyde brutians kepte warde whyche done without reſyſtence brutians onely made noo reſyſtence alſoo holpe theym vp thus entred towne ſtreyghte wente nexte gate whyche brake cauſed moche theyr companye entre theyr baners dyſplayed breake day came markette place tarentines parceyuinge theyr towne taken came theyr power frome caſtell ſide hauen ſuccour therof late battayle lyttell begonne felte ſelues farre vnable reſiſt romaynes wherfore anon fled euery man houſe friendes houſe wer nico democrates ſlayne battayle philomenes chiefe autour betraying towne anniball toke horſe fledde whither wente became hym knowen great ſlaughter made carthaginenſes tarentines many priſoners taken ryche ſpoyle wall whiche anniball made deuyde caſtell frome towne throwen downe ¶ anniball fyrſte hearde tarent beſieged haſt poſſible hyed thyther ſuccour therof came nere thervnto hearde newes takynge citie meanes ſayde nowe ryght well fynde romaynes haue alſo anniball amonge theim euen ſuche crafte wanne tarent ſuche haue loſt ſhulde appeere reculed feare pitched campe fyue mile citie taryed certayne dayes thenſe went metapontus cauſed letter written two chiefe ruler citie fabius contentes therof woulde pleaſe romaynes hym receyue theim theyr grace remitte theyr olde iniuries wronges doone woulde delyuer handes bothe towne alſo garniſon carthaginenſes wer within ſame fabius nothynge miſtruſtinge ſent agayne appoyntynge tyme wolde come metapontus ſpeake whiche letter ſtreyght brough anniball beinge ioyouſe trayne deceyue old wiſe fabius tyme appoynted layde great embuſſhemente vpon waye fabius ſhulde paſſe metapontus ¶ ſame tyme fabius ſhulde departe ſought diuinations augury howe ſhulde ſpede voiage kyllyng beaſte therwith ſacrifyce lucke byrdes deteſtable vſe longe ben amonge romaynes whiche augury ſo vnlucky vntowarde ſhewed hym ſome euyll aduenture wente forwarde appoynted iourney wherfore deuynours wyſe men aduyſed hym tary ſtyll tentes feare treaſon ¶ metapontans ſeing fabius came day aſſigned ſent agayne hym requyring hym come capitaynes whiche meſſangers incontinente taken examyned vpon caſe fearynge tourmentes wer prepared theim confeſſed deceyte treſon wherby fabius eſcaped death deſtruction many armye ¶ scipio fyghteth haſdruball beſyde betula dryueth hym hyll ſleith viii hoſt taketh xii pryſoners maſſus neuew maſſaniſſa great praye campe cap l ſame ſummer tyme whyles theſe thynges done italy p scipio beinge spayne ſo gotten loue ſpanyardes ediſco indibilis mandonius thre great prince spayne come amitie alliaunce indibilis deſired commynge myght diſhonorable vnto man ſhulde reproche theim ſtolen awaye theyr olde friendes carthage lyke lyght people runne romaynes ſayde doone worthely tymes whiche theyr kyndeneſſe euer recompenſed pryde auaryce many iniuries ſo onely theyr bodyes abode amitie carthage theyr hertes hadde longe beene towardes romaynes knewe euer kepers theyr truſe taken mainteinours right equitie wherfore deſyred scipio receyue theyr friendely commynge vnto hym accordynge theyr meanynge intente▪ founde dylygent theyr ſeruyce doynge vnto ſo eſteme scipio hertely thanked grauntynge theyr requeſtes thynges wheruppon theyr wyues chyldren reſtored vnto theim whiche captyues scipio ſtedfaſte aliaunce amitie knytte betwene theim ſone theyr hole power men war came theſe prynces ioyned campe romaynes departinge guided euer tyl brought nere campe theyr ennemies ¶ meane armye greatly increaced yet beſydes one waye scipio polytikely augmented hoſt ſawe nauy car • hage ſea ſo neded haue great noumbre men ſhyppes broughte hoole nauye tarracon takynge ſouldiours whiche theim alſoo parte maryners hym warres lande great hooſte wente forwardes made ſuche ſpede ſecretly came nere vnto towne betula haſdruball laye armye theyr fyrſte commynge thyther certeyne ſmalle ſkyrmyſſhes made betwene theim haſdruball ſeynge romaynes power dayly increaſed made leſſe thoughte woulde ieoparde fyghte without lenger prolongynge tyme determyned ſeeke place ſtrengthe myght fyghte aduauntage hurte ennemyes wherfore nyghte remoued armye hyghe hyll nere adioynynge toppe wherof fayre large playne backe ſyde hyll ranne ryuer whiche compaſſed good parte hyll furthermore aboute myddes hyll another playne fyelde moche lower playne vnto nether playne aſcendyng hard peinfull lower fyelde aſd • uball day folowyng ſent great numbre numidian horſemen light harneſſed fotemen affrica iles called baleares nowe named maiorque minorque ¶ scipio rydynge aboute hoſte ſhewed theim theyr ennemyes theyr hertes ſaythe wyll ſerue theym fyghte v euen grounde wherfore ſeeke hyghe mountaynes truſtynge ſtrengthe place theyr owne ſtrengthe armour newe carthage hadde hye walles whiche neuertheleſſe ſcaled romayne ſouldyours neyther coulde hyghehylles caſtell thereof yet ſea withſtande theyr power knowe ſaythe theſe hye place whiche ennemyes haue choſen thynke ſhall ſerue theym flye v leapynge runnyng downe ſtiepeneſſe therof wayes wyll alſo ſtoppe frome theim wherevpon incontinente scipio ſente two company menne warre commaundynge one kepe mouthe valley whiche ryuer ranne ſhulde abyde ſecretely waye laye bowinge mountayne betwene towne betula fyeldes hym ſelfe good noumbre nymble harneſſed men wente ſtreyghte towardes theſe numidian affricanes whiche lower playne hyll whoo ſuffered theim come almooſte vppe withoute let ſaue onely ſtyepeneſſe hylle vntyll came within caſtynge dartes thenne fyghte ſoore bothe partes ſpecially great plenty ſtoones inginnes throwen hyll romaine neuertheleſſe althoughe hylle verye tediouſe harde wonne alſo almooſte ouerwhelmed ſtones yet beinge nymble well harted men moche vſed approchynge ſcalynge walles ceaſſed goo ſtyll vppewarde tyll formooſte theym hadde gotten playne euen grounde anone putte numidyans flyghte greatte ſlaughter droue theym vppe theyr armye abode hygheſte parte hyll thenne scipio commaunded ſame companye go ſtreyghte vppe towarde myddle theyr ennemyes reſt hoſte deuyded two partes wherof cauſed lelius take one halfe go aboute ryght hande hyll eſpy myghte fynde eaſye place aſcende parte kept lefte hande ere euer fette farre compaſſe clambe vp ſayde mountayne ran ennemyes whoſe backes wer toward wherwith hoſt carthaginenſes ſore troubled great clamour made inforcynge tourne reſyſt scipio company chaunge theyr ordre whiche troublous bruite came lelius theym ſide whoſe coming cauſed foreward gyue backe feare inuaded behynde meane wherof myddell warde scipio gotte hylle whyche poſſible theim haue wonne army elephantes kepyng aray place ſo ſtiepe aſcend began carthaginenſes flee ſauegard great ſlaughter made among abode scipio company thoſe fledde many receyued ii company layde embuſſhement ſame purpoſe ſo ſlayne numbre viii men aſdruball ſeing beginning battaile nothing proſperous intent ſent money many elephantes away him▪ folowed many coulde ſaue ſelues flieng paſſyng ryuer tagus went ſtreight toward mountain pyreneis ¶ scipio comynge campe carthaginenſes gaue pray therof ſouldiours except priſoners wer numbre x thouſand fotemen ii horſemen whiche numbre ſoo many spanyardes let go lybertie freely without raunſome paying reſt cauſed ſold queſtor gaue large gyftes princis spayn ſpecially indibilis gaue iii c horſes beſte coulde chuſe taken whiche liberall diſtribution commune spayne called hym kyng whyche name scipio declared odious deteſtable roman wherfore deſyred abſteyne callyng hym name name gouernour capitayne well contented ¶ whan queſtor ſell pryſoners capitaynes commaundement among found goodly yonge chylde xv yeres olde whome ſente scipio herd deſcended lignage roial scipio enquired countrey greatter age happened campe amonge men warre aunſwered numidia named maſſus father ſayd deade wherfore mother ſent father sala kinge numidia frome time ben brought vp vncle maſſaniſſa vncle came ouer spaine ſocour carthaginenſes came alſo euer went batteil vncle wolde ſuffer hym go time ſayde neuer came fyelde nowe alſo vnware ſayde vncle euery man made hym redye pryuely alſo toke horſe harneies entered battayle chaunce ſo euyll nowe faule horſe wherby taken romaynes scipio demaunded hym whether deſyrous retourne maſſaniſſa aunſwered wepynge ioye wolde verye glad chaunce ſo good scipio gaue ringe golde cote ſenatours garmente ſpanyſſhe cloke goodly horſe well harneyſed buckle golde ſuffered hym departe vncle pleaſure appoyntynge horſemenne conducte hym waye ſo farre woulde haue theim ¶ theſe thynges done beſtowed reſte ſummer receyuynge many people city spayne amitie romaynes remayned tarracon ¶ sone battayle foughte betula aſdruball ſonne gyſgon mago theyr armyes came frome parte spayne helpe aſdruball late battayle paſte theyr comynge wherfore conſulted beſte doone laſte conſyderynge scipio gyftes lyberalytye hadde hertes hyther partes spayne onely people furtheſte parte co • ntreye towardes gades pyllers hercules knewe yet nothynge hym romaynes wherfore ſure frendes carthaginenſes determyned neceſſytie muſte remoue theyr ſouldiours spayne eyther furtheſte partes spayne elles fraunce elles ſhorte ſpace woulde turne frendſhip romaynes ¶ alſo agreed aſdruball takynge hym al spanyardes spayne farre name scipio ſhulde go ouer mountaynes towardes anniball italy heade chiefe grounde warres ¶ furthermore mago leauinge hoſt aſdruball ſonne gyſgon ſhuld paſſe ouer ſea iles called baleares nowe called maiorque minorque great ſumme money ſhulde alſo hire many mo ſouldiours theyr helpe purpoſe whoſe departyng aſdruball ſonne gyſgon hoſt appointed depart portugall ſhoulde wyſe fyght romayns maſſaniſſa iii beſt lighteſt horſes men appoynted hym whiche numbre aſſigned pervſe ryde abrode countreys helping city frendes carthaginenſes ſpoile diſtroy townes fieldes ennemies theſe intentes myndes euery one capitaines departed makyng greate ſpede achieue enterpryſe ¶ marcellus conſull ſlayn imbuſhement layde anniball criſpinus conſull marcellus ſonne ſoore hurte capi li fame scipio dayly encreaſed rome alſo q fabius maximus gotten greate honour wynnynge towne tarent marcellus meane ennemies runne great infamy reported anniball rouyng abrode countrey kept hoſt ſommer ſeaſon towne venuſia marcellus purge hym ſclaunderous name came rome againſte tyme chuſynge offycers thyther came alſoo q fuluius flaccus conſull cauſe marcellus openly debated c bibulus one tribune charged hym ſoore ſayeng negligence marcellus ſuche lyke cauſe anniballes ſo longe abode italy ſayd tenthe yere ſens came fyrſt countrey hath lyued almoſt long italy hath done carthage choſyng officer ye wylled claudius marcellus continue yere longar office nowe ye wyll knowe fruite hath brought forth yere meane therof ye ſhall vnderſtande hath hooſte two tymes beaten many ſlayne yere chiefe ſommer hath kepte reſydue men venuſia within ſure walles ſame ¶ accuſation marcellus ſo wyſely ſobrely aunſwered ſhewynge policy actes doone agaynſte anniball excuſe onely welle taken alſo well dooinge daye folowynge hole conſent people choſen conſull titus quintus criſpinus choſen felowe appoynted kepe italy agaynſte anniball marcellus wente olde army venuſia takyng hym dyuers ſupplye place thoſe ſlayne criſpinus ſeinge honour growen fabius wynnyng tarent thoughte beſyege citie locrus wherfore ſent maner ordynances sicilia ſhyppes alſo aſſault ſame ſea well land hearinge cominge anniball lacinium lefte pourpoſe ſeaſon ioyned hoſte fellowe marcellus come venuſia countrey apulia bothe incamped army iii myles one frome thyther came alſo anniball ſoone parceyued conſull criſpinus hadde lefte beſiegynge locrenſes ſame cuntrey pytched campe tentes yere aſſayed power herte marcellus ſometyme wynnyng ſometyme loſſe men wherefore fearynge power bothe conſulles ouermatched diuyſed howe policy craft deceiue conſulles made dyuers ſkyrmyſhes men thinkyng ſuche tryflynge frayes paſſe furthe ſommer kepe hym occupied yet neuertheleſſe truſted ſtronge ynough alſo beſiegynge locrus wherfore ſent sicilia cauſyng l cincius nauy army come beſiegynge locrus ſea furthermore aſſayle alſo lande commaunded part army whiche laye defence tarent brought thyther appoyntement ſo pryuyly done anniball hadde knowledge therof certayne thurines whervppon agaynſte tyme appoynted theyr comynge ſent embuſſhement two thouſande horſemen thre thouſande footemen lye ſecretely vnder hylle petillia vppon way wherby romayne tarentines ſhoulde paſſe romaynes vnaduyſedly paſſyng waye amonge great hurtes two thouſande theim ſlayne one two hundred taken pryſoners reſt eſcaped fledde dyuers way backe agayne tarent conſulles laye theyr ſeuerall campes farre frome campe anniball nowe myddell waye betwene romaynes campe hym greatte hylle full woodde taken viewed romayns feared viewe doubted maner grounde vttermooſte parte thereof towarde theyr enemy neither viewed anniball eſtemed ſame place mete deceiue ennemies pytche theron campe wherefore nyght ſent thither company numidian horſemen lye pryuily myddell wood without mouynge makynge noyſe daie tyme feare eſpied romaynes euer cryed theyr capytaynes ſhoulde take ſayde hylle pytche one theyr campes feare leſte anniball ſhoulde take theim ſaid marcellus felowe criſpinus lette v certaine horſemen v go viewe ſame hyll • yghte whereof maye diſpoſe thynges accordyngly beynge thus agreed takyng ii hundred xx horſemen wente bothe ſuruey ſayde hylle wood yonge marcellus conſuls ſonne aulus manlius beinge bothe tribune folowed couetous mynde marcellus ioyne battaile anniball thoughte coulde neuer ioyne campe nyghe ynough campe ennemye wherefore departynge cauſed people redyneſſe caſe place lyked theim myghte gather vp veſſelles theyr ſtuffe folowe theim frome theyr campes ¶ capytaynes paſſed thorough lyttell playne fielde frome thenſe entred fayre brode waye rydynge whyche wente vp woodes toppe rydynge numidian hadde ſette eſpy watche thynkynge ſoo greate praye happed theim come onely watche forrageours wood caryars ſhoulde happe roue abrode vytayles wood ſuche neceſſaries eſpye warned theym romaynes commynge numbre gaue theim ſygne whan euery man theim ſhoulde leape oute ſecrete denne whyche craftyly executed gaue theym ſygne iſſue oute tyll romaynes ſoo farre paſſed theyr wa • e hyndermoſte parte embuſſhement myght incloſe theim ſtoppe theyr waye behynde theim tyme formoſte embuſhement aſſayled theim partes iſſued layde romaynes conſulles ſeynge theim ſelues ſtopped bothe behynde foughte manfullye theym ſelues comforted theyr fellowes thynkynge prolonge battayle tylle ſuccours myghte come ſoo fierſe parte romaynes fledde neuer leſſe reſte foughte ſeaſon tylle ſawe criſpinus ſoore wounded felowe marcellus thruſte thorough ſpeare falle deade grounde thanne reſte left lyue fledde criſpinus conſull ſoore hurte two dartes yonge marcellus beynge alſo ſoore wounded aulus manlius ſlayne marcus aulius foure forty horſemen arenius fyue ſergeantes conſulles eyghtene horſemen taken priſoners ¶ anniball craftily ſendeth lettters salapia ſealed marcellus ſygnet aſdruball paſſeth mountayns army mete brother anniball cap lii anniball knowynge greatte feare woulde romayne hooſte deathe one conſulle alſo woundynge putte theym feare incontynent remoued hooſte ſame hylle battayle hadde beene pytched campe founde bodye marcellus whiche cauſed buryed criſpinus beinge ſore feared deathe fellowe alſo owne woundes nyght folowynge remoued ſecretelye armye higheſt nexte hyll ſuertie coulde fynde pitchinge campe tentes capitaines endeuoured ſelues vttermoſt one deceyue eſchewe deceite ¶ anniball bodye marcellus founde alſoo ringe ſygnet wherby truſted worke deceytfull concluſions criſpinus myſtruſtinge alſo ſame ſente ſpede worde city romaynes nere adioyninge warnynge theim felowe marcellus ſlayne anniball gotten ſignet wherfore commanded theim wyſe gyue credence letter ſhulde ſente vnto ſealed ſeale marcellus made name soone meſſanger came salapia anniball letter written ſealed name marcellus ſhewynge vnto nyght folowynge marcellus wolde priuely come thyther wherfore commaunded capitaynes garriſon redy commynge knowe pleaſure done salapiens fyndynge crafte wrytynge ſente backe meſſangers anniball gentyll anſwere nyghte prefyxed ſette ſure watche warde walles ſpecially parte towne gate demed theyr ennemyes wolde come lyttell daye came anniball great company hym firſt company cam yates roman wer departed cuntrey taken wage anniball romayne armour came gate ſpake laten dydde romaynes wakynge watchemen byddynge open gate conſull watche aroſe great leuers lyft vp port colyes ſoo hyghe men myghte entre vnder ſayde bande romaynes runawayes entered ſo faſt myght entred numbre vi c rope whiche dyd holde vp portcolyes let ſlyp fell downe great noyſe makynge salapiens ſmalle reſyſtence ſlewe entred towne myſtruſtinge ſuche thyng bare harneys hanginge theyr ſhulders thynkyng haue entred peace many towne ſpeares dartes chaſed theyr ennemyes gate walles ¶ thus anniball beinge taken owne trappe deceyued thenſe departed rayſe ſyege friendes locrenūs cincius ſouldiours ordynaunce came sicilia kept harde ſtrayghte ¶ mago citie herynge death marcellus toke ſome comforte vnto hym harde tydynges anniball ſente numidian horſemen coming hym ſelfe fotemen ſpedely myght withoute feare wherfore eſpyed afarre numidian approchyng cauſed gate opened arraye folke iſſued vpon romaynes ſodeyne comyng ſtrengthe cauſed battayle endure ſeaſon doubtefull numidian alſo come romaynes ſo ſtryken feare withoute ordre ranne towarde theyr ſhyppes leauynge behynde theym theyr ordynaunce wherwith beaten walles meane ſyege locrenſis rayſed ¶ criſpinus conſull ſente letter rome bothe felowes deathe alſo ſore hurtes letted ſo could come rome choſyng conſuls ſenatours penſyfe ſe two conſuls army deſtitute capitaynes wherfore day election loked fynd two wiſd circumſpect perſons offyce ben acqueynted deceites anniball fyrſte aboue lyked c claudius nero knewe valyaunt man good capytayne eſtemed hym quicke tyme warres matche ſoobre capytayne anniball wherfore deuyſed match quickenes ſobre felowe great temperance one liuius man great ſobreneſſe late come agayne citie ben conſull viii yeres paſſed conſulſhyppe condempned comons without fault put offyce ſhame hym done toke ſo diſpleaſauntly leauynge citie wente forthe countrey dwell company men viii yeres condempnation marcellus valerius leuinus conſulles brought hym home agayne citie founde hym foule euyll apparellyd heare bearde longe token ſhame receiued time cenſors cauſed hym rounde heare puttynge cleane garmentes come ſenate houſe brought thyther father examyned theyr opinion liuius touchyng offyce conſull agreed ſenatours common mete couple hym claudius nero alone refuſed office accuſyng citezens vnkynde lyghtneſſe ſayinge ¶ meruayle moche ye laye nowe burthen office ye late thruſte oute ſame offyce thynkyng vnworthy therof ye accompt good honeſte man dyd ye condempne euyll man offender ſyns ye iudged euill gouerned conſulſhyp wherin laſte truſte ye nowe agayne ſame roume ¶ ſuch wordes accuſed father alſo common ſenatours rebuked hym wordes ſhewinge example furius camillus though banyſhed citie rome yet reſtored agayne ſayd lyke childe ought ſuffer ſharpe puniſhement father ſo ought euery man ſuffer puniſhement countrey pacience gentilnes ¶ theſe wordes appeaſed hym cauſed hym take hym ſayde office ¶ one conſull appoynted kepe warre againſte anniball italy leſte ſhulde drawe nere aſdruball cominge mountaynes ſuccour aſſygned mete aſdruball fame whome beganne approche mountaynes thintent come ouer ioyne power brother anniball opynion anniball dyd alſo mo • helpe romaynes purpoſe althoughe knewe brother woulde ſommer paſſe mountaynes come ouer hym yet whan remembred manyfold lettes ſelfe paſſynge ryuer rhodanus dangerus mountaynes ſtryuinge bothe men peryllous place wherin ſpent fyue monethes loked ſo ſpedye quicke coming brother whiche cauſed hym ſo long er euer remoued frō place wintred army moche deceiued aſdruball better ſpede paſſage loked ſelfe frenchemen alſo mountaynoys dyd onely receiue ſuffered hym army paſſe countreys alſo folowed warres leadinge many ſure wayes whiche anniball brother vnable paſſed agayne wayes ouer mountaynes continuall vſe goinge ouer made moche eaſy people gentyll intreate annibals comynge vſed company ſtraungers neyther ſene countrey wherfore wylde ſauage people thoughte alſo fyrſte tyme carthaginenſes come take theyr caſtelles cattell nowe fame warre holden italy betwene romaynes carthaginenſes taught made know hole contention betwen thoſe noble head city worlde beinge ſo farre diſtant ſundre onely honour rich ſo wolde trye whether ſhulde poſſede dominion hole ¶ theſe cauſes knowen made mountaynes open eaſy aſdruball paſſe ſpeede ſo good paſſynge ſame let great beſieginge placentia whan come ouer thought citie beinge faire plaine countrey ben eaſy wynne fame wynnynge therof thoughte city adioyninge ſhulde haue trembled feare ſtrength therof moche deceyued knewe anniball full wel came ouer riuer trebia vayne aſſayed ſtrength therof aſdrubals aſſieginge placentia onely lette owne iourneye alſo ſtayed anniball moche longer harde therof ere euer ſette forthe place wyntered hoſte ¶ conſulles theyr armyes went prouinces liuius towardes placentia whome ere departed q fabius warned exhorted ſhulde ouer haſtyly fyght ennemies knewe maners condition theim liuius remaynynge yet dyſpleaſure towarde citezens banyſhement anſwered wolde fyght theim ſo ſoone might haue fyght whan cauſe demaunded hym wolde make therm ſuche haſte truely ſayd eyther wyll quyckely haue great honour ſubduinge myne ennemyes el greatte ioye ſleynge myne owne vnkynde cytezens whyche ioye althoughe honeſte yet ſhall accordyng theyr deſeruynges ¶ quintus claudius nero made haſte tyll approched nere vnto anniball gone countrey lucanes lay towne grument claudius hadde army forty thouſande fotemen two thouſand fyue hundred horſemen anniball gatherynge togyther moche power coulde amonge brutians ſuche fortreſſes helde lay inc • mped nigh vnto walles grument within halfe myle campe romaynes betwene bothe campes goodly playne valey hauynge oone ſyde fayre playne hylles without wooddes couerte hyde embuſſhement cauſe deceyte wherfore leſſe ſuſpecte bothe party theſe hylles laye adioynyng lefte ſyde carthaginenſes ryghte ſyde romaynes playne medowe many lyght eſkyrmyſſhes made betweene hoſtes many excurſyons romayne conſull cauſed made onely kepe ennemyes frome goynge towarde aſdruball ¶ ſyde anniball deſyrous remoue place power intended gyue hym battaile wherfore putte whole hoſte array claudius nero perceyuynge intent cauſed ſecretely nyght folowynge titus aſſellus p claudius two tribune good noumbre men theim paſſe ouer ſayde hylle adioynynge abyde valeye behynde hylles appoyntynge theim tyme whan ſhoulde deſcende mountayne backe theyr ennemies hym ſelfe breake daye reſte footemen horſemen came fielde good araye anniball lykewyſe commaunded men arme theim greate noyſe made campe euery man runnynge harneys whan armed ranne oute campe yates bothe horſemen footemen without array anniball knowledge therof ſoone campe playne ranne ennemyes fyghtynge bothe horſebacke foote chaunce gaue theym meete theyr ennemies kepynge none order ¶ whan conſull ſawe theym thus rounnynge abrode fyelde without order commaunded c arunculeus horſemen legyon inuade carthaginenſes moche vyolence myght wherby myght ſlea theym beinge without order lyke beaſtes coulde brought array whyche dydde dilygentely execute makynge greate ſlaughter battayle ſtrong ſeaſon reaſon contynuall reſorte freſhe ſouldiours runnyng ſuccours theyr felowes ¶ anniball yet campe hearyng noyſe men fyghtyng came furthe reſte power ſo dilygently applyed ſelfe euen menne fyghtynge put many theym araye whiche thynge hath bene lyghtly ſeene therein ſhewed hym ſelfe experte capytayne hauyng olde well acquaynted warryours vnder hym thus brought wholle hoſte order ſtyll fyghtyng c aſſellus bandes romaynes ſodainely deſcended hylles backe carthaginenſes greate clamour meanes wherof beyng aferde leſt ſhuld ſtopped campe began flee partes horſemen ſlewe many chaſe many mo ſlayne campe ſo nere hande yet loſt anniball men battayle viii ſlayne vii c taken aliue next day diuers day romains array kept fielde deſyrous fight carthaginenſes abode ſtyll theyr tentes ¶ soone nyght anniball army remoued towardes apulia makinge great fyres campe towardes romaynes leauynge entree campe certayne numydian horſemen ſhewe tyl hooſte myght farre gone frome ennemyes whan day lyght ſayd numidian ſhewed theim ſelues gate campe ſeaſon purpoſely deceyue romaine whan ſawe theyr tyme ſpedily rode theyr companie ¶ conſull hearynge noo noyſe tentes ennemyes ſent two light horſmen viewe theyr campe fyndynge voyde theyr ennemies retourned claudius certifiynge hym theyr departyng whervpon hoſte wente thyther toke ſpoyle ſuche baggage leſte morowe early folowed carthaginenſes fame hearde waie whiche gone anniball willynge fyght toke waie euer nyght ouer mountaynes tyl came metapontus toke hanno ſoudiours whyche lefte ioyned theim armye ſendynge hym ſmalle numbre hym countrey brutians aſſemble moo men warre ſuccour ¶ great battayle betwene aſdruball conſulles whyche aſdruball ſlayne ſyx fyfty thouſand men beſyde many taken great ſpoyle cap liiii asdruball leauing aſſiegyng placentia ſent foure frenchemen two numidian brother anniball letter paſſyng italy heryng anniball ſhoulde metapontus folowed thither er ware loſt way came fieldes tarent taken ſent claudius nero letter whan redde knewe contentes therof aſdruball intended mete brother vmbria thynkyng tyme mete common welth tary determination ſenate imagyned would enterpryſe ſome ſtrange thing wherby ſhulde put citezens rome alſo ennemies great feare lengthe whan achieued ſhulde tourne wholle citie greate feare meruailous gladneſſe wherfore ſent ſayde letter rome owne letter intended enterpryſe incontinent ſente meſſangers hym townes countreys whych army ſhoulde paſſe commaundyng theim brynge furthe fieldes agaynſt commynge vitayles horſes neceſſaries ſouldyours wholle armye choſe vi thouſande footemen one horſmen ſayinge publyſhyng intended aſſault next towne lucans take carthaginenſes whiche left keping therof company nyght departed makyng great haſte myghte iourney come healpe felowe liuius ſhulde haue aſdruball leauynge quintus tatius campe rule gouerne reſt hoſte rome conſulles letter made men leſſe aferde two yeres paſt whan carthaginenſes hadde pytched theyr tentes walles rome doubted whether myght allowe diſallowe bolde enterpryſe conſull whyche dyd appere hange vpon chaunce knewe campe left nere anniball army diſpurueyed capitayne ye flowre ſtrengthe ſame armye taken awaye capytayne leauynge campe ſure nothynge onely ignoraunce ennemies priuy conſulles abſence yf happed knowen chaunced anniball wholle army folowe nero hauyng vi thouſand fotemen armed one horſemen wold aſſaile reſte left campe without ſtrength good gouernance euil chance ſuſteined warres late dethe ii conſuls one yere increaſed feare whyche happed theim whan one capytayne one army ennemies italy nowe knewe ii myghty army ii valyant capitaines ye almoſt ii anniballes countrey aſdruball ſonne alſo amilcar hadde many yeres spayne made warre agaynſte romayns hadde two noble victory ſleynge two greate army alſo ii scipions noble capitayns ſame furthermore myghte glory aboue anniball bothe ſpedy paſſage ouer mountaynes alſo drawyng hym frenchemen battayle euen one almoſte loſte greatter parte menne hungre colde whiche two greatteſt myſeries warre euen gathered together gret puiſſance rekened alſo claudius nero ſhuld haue witty capitayn knewe mocked illuded hym spayne lyke child deceiteful intretyng condition peace wherby eſcaped ſtraytes wherein indaungered thus throughe feare whiche thinterpretour thynges worſte eſtemed power theyr ennemyes great owne ſmall ¶ meane tyme nero conſull ſo farre traueyled frome daunger ennemies iudged myght ſafely diſcouer ſecrete enterpriſe called together ſouldiours ſpake vnto ſayinge neuer enterpryſe taken hande capitayne whiche apparence bolde effect ſure wyll nowe brynge ſayde certayne ſure victorye goo battayle whiche felowe liuius many fotemenne horſemen appoynted hym ſenate wolde deſyre ye ſuche numbre wolde haue deſyred greatter ſhulde haue ben appoynted fyght anniball hym ſelfe nowe fame comynge conſull armye beinge ioyned ſhall fayle haue vndoubted victory fame thynge gyueth victory battayle yea ſmall thinges oft tymes driue hertes myndes men eyther feare good hope hole glorye honour good ſpede ſhall gyuen v euer whiche cometh laſt draweth honour ¶ comforte conſull ſhulde departed brother anniball could deuyſe thing brother ſo illuded departinge capitayne campe whiche farre part power iudged ſuſteined ſome gret loſſe wherby durſt followe conſull wherfore feared greatly leaſt whan loſt come late brother ſocours alſo miſtruſted letter neuer came anniballes handes meſſangers taken vp waye vpon ſyghte wherof conſull come haſt vanquiſhe alſo beinge great perplexitie cauſed fire put oute euery man truſſe vp ſtuffe baggage begynninge nyghte hole hoſt departed ſecretely folowinge two guide whoo farre gone partly feare partely beinge troubled rumour armye toke good hede waye wherfore ſecretely ſlypped awaye leauyng theim without guide wandered abrode fieldes ſome beinge wery ouerwatched laide bowne ſlepe reſt leauynge theyr ſtandardes daye appered aſdruball cauſed ſtandardes go hoſte alonge ſyde ryuer metaurus ſekynge fordes myght paſſe ouer went vp riuer hyer bankes thus wanderynge ſtyll crokes tourninges banke ſekyng place paſſage ſpente parte ſhulde euer aſſaulte towne reſted wherfore commaunded thoſe whiche fyrſt aſſaulte withdrawe tentes reſt incontinent two partes freſhe ſouldiours gaue newe aſſaulte two partes towne ſo defondours chaungynge parte therof battayle betwene horſemen endured longe whan hoſt fotemen within half myle together scipio cauſed horſemen withdrawe ſelues deuided two partes cauſed ſtande behynde two wynges
