agaynſt anniball ¶ thynges putte good order departed citie wente countrey lucanes ſhorte tyme brought countrey ſubiection anniball lyttell doone offered hym ſelfe gyue battayle ſo diſcouraged loſſe brother frendes ſouldiours parte conſulles thought beſt prouoke hym battayle ſe • founde hym noo ſturrynge moche feared eſtemed valour noble capytayne whome prayſe gyuen noo man coulde iudge hym whether commended tyme proſperitie tyme aduerſitie woulde wonder ſe maynteyned warre ſo farre frome countrey full ſpace thyrtene yeres lande ennemies hauynge armye owne citie countreye gathered togyther many nation whyche lyued vnder one maner lawe neyther hadde one cuſtome language moche different apparayle armour cuſtomes ceremony ye hadde ſeuerall goddis yet dydde ſo gouerne theim knytte theim gyther ſuche amitie man coulde iudge knowe dyſſention betweene theym inſurrection agaynſte theyr capytaynes althoughe dyuerſe tymes lacked paye theyr wage alſo vitayles ſuſtenaunce lacke whereof warres moche inconuenience hathe enſewed agayne deathe aſdruball armye whome truſt whan italy taken frome hym ſaue onely countrey corner brutians woulde wonder ſee noo rebellyon amongeſt owne menne conſyderynge vyttayles hadde lyttell angle brutians whyche yf hadde beene wholly tylled ſowed hadde beene able ſuſteyne ſoo greate armye neuer leſſe greatte parte therof vntylled parte feare romaynes theyr friendes partely mooſte parte yonge menne countreye taken warres whyche wonte tylle man • grounde huſbandrye theſe thinges ſay conferred togither wyll make al men muſe howe coulde ſo quietly gouerne greate hooſt prayſe greatly wyſe conduict therin ¶ scipio aſdruball arriue one daie affrica lodged bothe togyther palays kynge syphax cap lvi departynge p scipio tarracon carthaginenſes beinge dryuen spayne maſſaniſſa ſeinge great falle frendes carthaginenſes ſecretely communication sillanus wōne ſure frende romayns whervppon haue frendes affrica obedyent redy hym neceſſities appoynted ſayle ouer countrey make hym ſelfe ſtronge myght ayde ſuccour romaynes whan neede requyred sillanus ſoone retourned scipio tarracon ¶ p scipio wylling certifie ſenate great victory happie chaunces ſente brother l scipio rome reherſed ledde hym many noble men priſoners whome hadde taken warres whervppon meruaylouſely honoured prayſed men yet alone hadde deſerued ſayde honour eſtemed feates done spayne nothyng compariſon thoſe thynges whyche conceyued mynde looked conqueſte greate carthage affrica ende warre conſummation honour glory wherfore worke tyme thinges afterwardes ſhoulde ſerue pourpoſe determyned wynne vnto hym harte princis whyche borderars vnto countrey fyrſte mynded attempt kynge syphax ¶ syphax kyng people affrica called maſeſuli adioynyng moore lying ſide ſea mediterrane ouer againſt new carthage spain tyme great friende carthaginenſes hym ſent c lelius goodly preſent wherwith kynge verye gladde well pleaſed conſyderynge mynde good fortune whyche romaynes hadde partes ſeynge power olde friendes carthaginenſes ſoo greately decayed italy hadde nowe lyttell doo spayne nothynge agreed lelius become friende romaynes ſayde woulde procede confirmation amitie betweene tyll myghte perſonally ſpeake scipio chief capitayn romaynes whervppon lelius takynge aſſuraunce hym ſafe goynge commynge capitayne retourned scipio declared vnto hym howe ſpedde declared scipio indgynge frendſhyppe great helpe furtheraunce purpoſe touchynge deſyrous affayres affrica bothe greatte ſtrengthe rycheſſe alſo countrey adioynyng carthage directly ouer agaynſte spayne leauynge lucius martius tarracon sillanus newe carthage power ſufficient defence spayne lelius two galeys rowbarges fyue oores piece paſſed ouer affrica ¶ nowe happened euen ſame tyme aſdruball late ben dryuen spayne newely arryued ſame hauen ſeuen galeys caſtyng ankers drewe neere ſhore coulde aſdruball perceyuinge two galeys rowbarges scipio comynge towardes ſame hauen knewe full welle veſſelles ennemyes wherefore doubtynge beynge ſoo fewe numbre myght eaſyly oppreſſed vanquyſ • hed ſhoulde gette hauen commaunded folkes wey vp ankers make theim redy ſette furthe ſpeede hauynge good wynde theyr furtherance entred hauen galeys aſdruball myght gette ſuche ruffelinge noiſe littell ſhifte made men wherefore romaynes one gotten kinges hauen man durſte ſo bolde meddell theym thus wente two capyteynes lande fyrſte aſdruball scipio lelius bothe wente kynges palayes whoſe comynge dydde vnto syphax greatte honour neuer ſeene gouernoures ii moſt noble ſeignories thoſe dayes world came euer palayce vpon one day deſire amitie peace kynge ryght gentylly receyued theim bothe ſens theyr chaunces mete one time howſe dydde myght brynge communication truſtynge therby appeaſe ſtryfe diſcorde mattier hadde beene betweene theym scipio refuſed doo affyrmynge pryuate matter diſpleaſure betweene hym aſdruball whyche communication hearynge friendes neded determined neyther thynge touchynge common welthe countrey wherin might trauayle intreate oneleſſe ſpeciall auctoritie commaundement wholle ſenate kynge made great inſtance scipio ſeinge bothe gueſtes one wolde contented ſo ordered myghte haue cauſe expelle theim bothe frome table scipio kynges requeſte onely contented ſytte aſdruball oone table alſo kynges pleaſure laye ſame bedde dyd scipio naturally ſuche dexteritie ſo conformable reaſon thereby onely wanne herte syphax alſoo broughte mooſte mortall ennemye aſdruball admyration hym hadde ſeene conuerſation euer dydde acte euer dydde wherevppon beganne coniecture iudge syphax myghte become friende romaynes suche polycie deemed scipio haue wynnynge hertes men beganne dyuiſe neceſſary carthaginenſes conſult among theim ſelues spayne loſte myghte recouered rather howe myghte keepe domynion affrica specyally moued thus doubte iudged ſoo greatte capytayne romaynes woulde leaue countrey lately hadde conquered wander abrode ſtraunge domynyon onely two galeys leauynge behynde hym greatte power committyng hym vnto daungier vnknowen kynge onely vppon ſome truſte therby wynne affrica ¶ scipio concludinge peace amitie kynge departed hym leauynge aſdruball wrapped manyfolde trouble within foure dayes ſuſteynynge many ſtormes ſeas arriued ſafegard newe carthage ¶ maſſaniſſa ſpeaketh ſecretely scipio entreth leage romaynes mago ſayleth italy ioyne anniball cap lvii declared howe sillanus ſecrete communication maſſaniſſa wonne hym friende romaynes concluſyon communication deferred tyll maſſaniſſa myghte ſpeake scipio perſonallye ſure faythfull aſſurance theyr alliaunce whiche cauſed p scipio enterpryſe longe peynfull iourney come nere ſea ſide mete hym whoſe approchynge maſſaniſſa yle called gades aduertiſed l martius fained mago horſes loſt ſpylt ſo longe kepte within yle without exerciſe men alſo empayred throughe idlenes puttynge ſelues vre feates armes furthermore ſaide longe lienge ilande cauſed derth ſcarſitie thynges wherfore deſired licence mighte horſemen paſſe ouer spayne ſpoyle waſt countrey nere ſea ſyde ¶ perſwaſyon obteyned lycence came ouer spayne fyrſte arryuaile ſente thre noble men numidie scipio wherof wylled reteyne hym two pledge ſende againe third theim acertayne hym tyme place theyr metynge whoſe conducte myght broughte place appoynted daye came met gether ſmalle numbre companye maſſaniſſa fyrſte ſyghte althoughe greate admyration scipio throughe noble fame actes yet vppon ſyght hym preſence hym moche veneration beſydes nature indowed goodlye large ſtature wherein ſhewed marueylouſe magnifycence yet ſame ſet forthe reaſon goodly long heare comly apparell manly warrelyke faſhion alſo myddle age full ſtrength become ſo beautyfull ſickenes whiche late recouered luſty youthe ſemed renewed wherby pleaſaunt beholde theyr firſt metyng maſſaniſſa half aſtonied gaue hym humble thankes goodneſſe ſhewed ſendynge home brother ſonne priſoner tyme ſayde ceaſſed ſeke occaſion friendſhyp amitie whiche nowe obteyned gaue thankes goddes truſtynge wold ſo apply himſelfe affayres romaynes cauſes theyr common welthe neuer aduaunced one man beinge ſtraunger vnto harty beneuolence good wyll bare coulde neuer althoughe wolde haue ſhewed hym spayne beinge hym ſtraunge vnknowen countrey caſe romaynes wolde ſende scipio theyr capitayne affrica bred brought vp doubted ſuch hie ſeruice honour carthage ſhuld longe endure ¶ scipio gladly behelde hym alſo heard hym knowinge ſurely chiefe al horſemen army ennemies luſty yonge man nobleherte courage wherfore entreated theyr buſines giuynge faythe one faythfull loue amity departed scipio tarracon maſſaniſſa ile gades bycauſe myghte appere mago done ſome feate spayne scipio ſuffered ſpoile certayne goodes groundes ſea coſt take praye hym ¶ mago beinge deſperate good ſpede hadde spayne mynde ſayle affrica ſodeynlye letter came hym carthage commaundyng hym nauy ſhyppes gades ſhulde ſayle ouer italy hyringe moche people myghte frenchemen liguriens ſhoulde ſpede ioyn ſelfe annibal purpoſe great ſummes money ſent carthage beſydes leuied exacted moch money coulde gaditanes compellinge euery man brynge money beſydes ſpoyled temple rich arryued ile minorque gathered together ii yonge men beginnynge ſommer toke hym fayled ouer italy xxx great ſhippes warre many ſhyppes loden prouiſyon hoſte tyme xii fotemen two horſemen numbre ſodeynlye arriued geene whiche towne toke ſmall reſyſtence beinge vnprouyded men warre thenſe ſayled alonge coſtes liguria nexte mountaynes called alpes hering people countreye called ingawni helde warre certayne mountanoys called epanterii landed makynge leage amitie iagawnes graunted inuade mountanoys certayne people reſt ſent carthage defende coſtes ſea bruted abrode scipio mynded lande nauy affrica ¶ longe ſeaſon taryed armye ſtil encreaſed frenchemen dayly reſorted vnto hym hering fame glory name arriuaile liguria geene sp lucretius ſent letter rome ſenate aduertiſynge aſdruball ii yeres paſte ſlayne armye frontier italy great comfort citie great ioye vaine paſſed lyke ſhadowe onleſſe prouyded nowe ſpedye remedy newe armye come mago carthage begynne newe warre lyke onelye capytayne therof chaunged theſe newes moued moch ſenatours wherfore ſente letter liuius proconſull commaundynge hym brynge hoſt hetruria arminius cn seruilius pretour hadde alſo commaundement bringe thyther rome two newe legion thus laye bothe hoſtes romaynes army carthaginenſes theyr friendes oone farre longe ſeaſon without thynge doinge worthy memory ¶ scipio ſayleth italy cometh rome treate one conſulies deſpreth haue licence ſaile affrica army cap lviii sone departyng mago ile gades gaditanes yelded ſelues romaynes p scipio committing rule gouernaunce army l lentulus l manlius takyng x ſhippes men ſufficient went ſelfe rome againſt whoſe coming counſaile ſatte without citie houſe bellona ſoberly declared ſenatours thinges done spayne howe often foughte banner diſplayed againſt ennemies howe many cyties taken ſtrength people brought theyr obeyſaunce ſhewed alſo hadde fought iiii ſundry capitaines noble men vanquiſhed army whiche neuer vanquiſhed nowe carthaginenſes lefte spayne al noble actes admitted entre citie triumph bicauſe neuer borne office citie counſayle aroſe entred citie preſented brought treſory great plenty money rich gaynes prayes soone tyme came choſyng conſuls whiche daye p cornelius scipio choſen conſull p licinius craſſus fellowe yere great reſort came behold scipio ſo euer went common conceiued mindes opinion hym manne appoynted goddes finiſhe warres italy delyuered spayne carthaginenſes whiche warres italy ended appoynted theyr owne hertes alſo ſpake openly ſhulde haue affrica appoynted prouynce prouynces allotted appoynted sicilia l craſſus brutians againſt anniball fame amonge common ranne ſtyll scipio ſhoulde haue affrica prouynce euer deſyrouſe great glory ſayde onely choſen conſull meynteyne warre fynyſſhe make ende therof whiche wiſe myght achieued oneles myght paſſe army affrica deſyre caſe ſenatours woulde graunte wolde referre voyce commune ¶ oration made q fabius maximus diſſwading scipio deſired iourney affrica willyng mayntein warres againſt anniball italy cap lix purpoſe scipio ſenatours conſulted togyther amonge deſyred q fabius maximus declare opinyon aunſwered making oration maner fourme folowynge ¶ well aſſured father conſcript yf diſſent agree haſty paſſage affrica two thynges wyll iudged ſpoken one ſlownes ſlacke tractynge mattier whiche naturally gyuen yongemen calle fearefulnes ſlouthe greueth lyttell thoughe haue ſuche opinion ſens men councelles heretofore haue appered gloryous fyrſte face lengthe counſaile hath euer proued beſte moſte common welthe ſeconde thynge ſhoulde euyll wyl go aboute hynder glory valyaunt conſull daily groweth encreaſeth frome whyche ſuſpition yf neyther faſcion lyuynge maners offyce dictatour whiche haue borne roume conſull whiche haue fyue time enioyed neyther greate glorye haue wonne tyme peace warre wyl delyuer pourge lette myne age leaſt deliuer therefro indifferent contention betwene hym yeres may matche ſonne dictatour mayſter horſes laboured ſo ſenate made equall auctoritye rule whyche thynge neuer ſeene yet neuer manne herde eyther priuyly openly refuſe theyr ordre therin hadde leauer gette deedes woordes whyche mennes iudgement compared ſhoulde ſhortely owne confeſſyon gyue preferrement moche leſſe nowe whan haue ſo oft borne theſe honourable office dooe intende ſtryue flouryſſhynge younge manne letted anniball vyctory intent myghte nowe vanquyſſhed luſty ſtronge reaſon woulde pub cornelius ye ſhoulde contented ſens dy dde neuer ſette myne owne fame honour fame people dyd common welth although preferre honour laudis common welth neuer leſſe caſe warre italy elles ſuche ennemy whoſe vanquyſhing ſmall honour gotten would kepe italy although commune welthe therby ſomewhat anaunced myght ſeeme go aboute take thy glory ſens anniball ennemy hath hooſte theſe xiiii yeeres vexed italy ſhouldeſt thou p cornelius thynke loſe honour thy proweſſe beynge conſull thou canſte expelle driue hym cuntrey hath cauſe ſo many men ſlaughter ſo great diſtruction wherby luctatius bare away honourable title fynyſhyng firſte warre carthaginenſes euen ſoo nowe thou mayſte obteyne prayſe fynyſhing warre oneleſſe thou doeſt thynke amilcar capitayn preferred anniball warre victory noble gloryous ſhall thy chaunce conſull ouercome thinkeſt thou honour deliuer spayne frome ennemies delyuer italy anniball ſuche man ſo euer wyll choſe warre place muſte reckened rather feare hym diſpyſe hym make redy therfore thynke fetche compaſſe aboute buſſhe goo affrica intente anniball ſhoulde folowe goo nexte waye woorke ſo euer anniball thyther dyrecte thy warre nature gyueth manne ſhould fyrſt defend owne countrey inuade aſſaile lande lette firſte peace italy warre affrica lette feare fyrſte expelled v driuen vpon yf thou canſte thy gouernaunce bothe fyrſte ouercome anniball aſſayle carthage treaſorye able finde ii greate armyes one affrica ſufficient fynde p licinius one hoſt italy p scipio alſo affrica yf ſhuld chance god forbyd yet ſuche happes haue happed maie dooe agayne anniball dyd ouercome licinius comynge towardes rome myght call frome affrica dydde call quintus fuluius frome capua ſuccours ye affrica alſo fortune warre doubtfull variable lette thyne owne howſe famylie warnyng thy father thyn vncle ſlayne theyr hooſtes within thyrty dayes ſpace yet hadde amonge ſtraunge nation ſea lande gotten greatte renoume cytie rome theyr poſterytie daye woulde fayle made ende yf ſhoulde reaken vp name kynges capyteynes whyche raſſhelye haue inuaded landes theyr ennemyes vtter vndooynge theym theyr armyes athenienſes leauynge warre home ſente noble yongeman capyteyne huge nauye sicilia beynge ouerthrowen oone battaile hadde ſuche loſſe common welthe cleane ſubuerted euer outwarde exaumple auncient let ſame • frica loſſe owne conſulle attilius taken carthaginenſes frendes v document comparyſon affrica publius scipio countreyes spayne play game eſtates theym nothynge lyke thy paſſynge spayne thou dyddeſte ſayle coſtes italye fraunce dyddeſt arryue thy nauye citie oure friendes ſettynge thy men lande thou ſure wayes conueyed tarracon friendes alſo romaynes frome tarracon thou cameſt ryuer iberus thou foundeſte noble capytayne l martius many fyers romain ſouldiours left army thy father thyne vncle ſone newe carthage wonne bicauſe none iii hoſtes carthagynenſes came ſuccour defence citie fellowes theſe thynges cannot ſo greatly praiſe touchynge warres affrica ſhall founde farre vnlyke ſhalte thou fynde hauen open army nauie grounde peaſyble citye oure fryendeſhyppe kynge frende alſo place mete v eyther abyde vppon goo forewardes wherefore whereſoeuer thou looke thou ſhalte ſee full thyne ennemyes wylte thou beleeue syphax numidian lette ſuffyſe thou dyddeſt one beleue hym folyſſhe hardyneſſe doothe neuer proſpere deceyte doothe ſoo order ſelfe ſmalle thynges faythe may geuen intent great thynges may deceiue gret aduauntage thy father vncle oppreſſed armour ennemies til firſt deceiued owne felowes fals friendes celtiberiens ye thy ſelfe neuer ſo great ieopardy mago aſdrubal capiteines thyne ennemies thou indibilis mandonius princis spaine whome thou diddeſt take thy frendes thyne owne romain ſouldiors haue late rebelled agaynſt wilt thou nowe truſt numydians bothe syphax maſſaniſſa touchyng dominion rule affrica wil preferre theim ſelues carthaginenſes yet wyl gladlier ſuffer carthaginē ſes beare rule ſtranger nowe contention debate betwene bicauſe fraied forein power ſo ſone romain army ſhal appere theim wil ſtraight ioyne ſelfes together towne fier houſe people wyll aſſemble together quenchyng thereof feare common hurt danger ye ſhal ſee carthaginenſes defend theyr walles town cuntrey tēples owne houſes wiues yong thildren ſort defē ded spayne carthaginenſes makyng peace kynges theyr neyghbours truſtynge ſtrength townes perceyuing italy made bare men warre thy coming thither ſuch power wil ſende newe army affrica italy wyll commande mago already come coſtes liguriens ioyne anniball power ſhall ſame caſe wherein aſdruball paſſed mounteynes deſcended italy ſtronger valyant capytaine thou arte moore oughte italy reioyce keepe ſtyll amonge v thou canſt deny thy ſelf anniball head ſtrength warre thou ſayſt thy goinge affrica ſhall drawe anniball thyther ſoo whether ann • bal thou muſt chefly haue praye aunſwere shalt thou ſure affrica beinge alone italye hauinge conſull thy felowe hoſt ioyned thou wilte ſeke experience therof let claudius liuius late conſulles exaumple lernynge agayne whether ſhall anniball ſtronger lyttle angle brutiens wherunto dryuen hole hoſte ſhall come carthago hauynge al friendes affrica hym deuiſe choſe rather fyghte trye thyne ennemie thy power ſhall ſmaller halfe thine ennemies power doubled fyght place thou ſhalte haue two army againſt one ye one worne weried longe greuous warre conſydre thy ſelfe howe moche thy counſayle varieth frome mynde thy father beinge fully appoynted spayne prouynce fearynge comynge anniball italy intent mete hym deſcendinge mountaynes lefte owne prouynce came italy nowe thou annibal al redy italy intendeſt leaue italy common welthe ſo therby purchaſe noble glorious name ye noble father conſcripte thinke p corn scipio made conſull owne priuate welthe pleaſure common welthe ſafegarde v neyther army men warre appoynted hym thintent lyke prynce mighte ſayle part world wyll aſſigned predeceſſours ſafegarde defence citie italy ¶ oration fabius beinge man great authoritie wiſedome experience fame part auncient ſenatours perſwaded mo men allowed ſobre counſayle olde man fyerſe mynde scipio yongemanne wherfore scipio made vnto hym aunſwere ¶ aunſwere p cornelius scipio oration q fabius maximus ſaylynge sicilia armye cap lx qvintus fabius beginning oratiō father conſcript ſaid declaration opinyon mighte ſuſpected ſpeke euill wylle enuy accuſe ſo great ſo noble man therof although doo perceyue ſame ſuſpition yet ſufficiētly auoyded whether defaulte therof deformitie oration lacke good matter knowe well perceiue auoyde crime ſuſpition enuy hath ſo extolled owne honour fame noble actes though ſhuld becom ſtand honor contende ſelfe childe vnder age ſonne conſiderynge great office hath borne citie wherby ſemeth meanynge deſyre glory ſhulde meaſured onely length lyfe man extende perpetuall memory poſteritie knowe well euery noble herte hathe couetous deſyre equiualent famouſe vertue age preſent alſo people al age paſt yet come onles wold diſſemble truly q fabius wyll equall vnto renowme alſo paſſe prayſes yf may atteyne thervnto lette neyther v bothe thynke none ſhall come v ſhall lyke vnto v deſyre greate hurt hynderaunce bothe poſteritie alſo common welth generally mankynde furthermore fabius hath remembred ieoperdies peryls ſhulde entre goynge affrica though carefull bothe myne army meruaile greatly whens louing care thought ſo ſodeinly ſpronge whan father myn vncle wer bothe ſlayne bothe theyr army almoſte diſtroied ſlayne cleane loſte affricanes ouerrounnynge countrey iiii ſeuerall hooſtes capytaines woulde man offre hym ſelfe capitayne romaine spayne onely atwhychetyme whan people citie made gouernor thā xxiiii yeres old man founde whiche would remembre tendre age neyther power ennemies daungerouſnes battayle yet late death deſtruction frendes spayne nowe affrica greatter army better capitaines spayne mine age tyme mete warre thanne nowe greater matter fight enemy affrica spayn affrica nowe eaſy auaunce ſelfe iiii army carthage diſtroied ſo many city taken force ſo many prince wylde nation ſubdued spaine vnto occean ſea ſo none apparence lefte warre likewiſe victorious returne affrica ſhalbe eaſie ſet forthe ouercominge thinges whiche nowe laide terryble dangerdus intent kepe ſtil home fabius demeth ſhal haue hauens porte open enter alſo remembreth taking attilius regulus affrica though attilius fall firſte arriuall countreye trueth hadde hauens open entre pleaſure ye ſpace hole yere many noble actes whome carthaginenſes neuer able owne power ſubdue till ſeconde yere coming many hoſt ſlaine ſent xantippus capitayne lacedemonians power whome lengthe ouercome taken battayle exaumple nothing feare ſhoulde feare ſayle affrica bycauſe taking attilius afrayd ſaile spaine deathe bothe scipions truſte xantippus lacedemonien born fortunate carthaginenſes ſhalbe romayns mine owne countrey tale muſte recited athenienſes howe fondely leauynge warre home entred affrica doeſt thou reherſe hiſtorie agathocles king syracuſanes countrey sicilia ben long troubled warre carthaginenſes hoſt failed ouer affrica whereby delyuered owne countrey warre tourned defence power affrica ſhewe commoditie inuadinge foreyne countreye thereby auoyde ieopardyes home better example man reherſe anniball greate difference betwene ſyght bournynge ſpoylyng mennes countreyes ſyght deſtruction thine owne city regyons courage manne offrethe battayle defendethe lyttell thoughte anniball fyrſt comyng italye ſo many city people wolde haue yelded vnto battail canna moch leſſe cauſe ſhal carthaginenſes haue truſte hoope affrica conſideringe vntruthes neyghbours owne proud cruel dominion ouer ſubiectes beynge forſaken neyghbours haue ſtil endured al danger owne power ſtrength carthaginenſes haue great ſtrength owne power hyred ſouldiours affrica numidia whoſe lyghte wyttes cauſe lyghte faythe ſe cauſe chaunge yf ye ſuffer depart hence ſpede ye ſhall ſhortely heare paſſage thither warre wherewith ſhal vexe theim ſhal ye ſee anniball make ſpede departe countreye ye ſhall heare ſhortely ſyege carthage doubtynge ye ſhal receiue gladder tydynges affrica euer ye fro spayne theſe hope conceyue fyrſte fortune citie people rome secondely throughe truſte goddes whiche witneſſes truſe broken theim thyrdely occaſyon offered syphax maſſaniſſa whoſe promyſe faythe wyll ſoo truſte wyll alſo well ware theyr falſehode dyſceipte parte manne good capyteyne ſhrynke forſake fortune offered knowe well quintus fabius ſhall find anniball matche wyll rather drawe hym ſhall retire wyll cauſe fyght owne cuntrey carthage ſhall rather pray rewarde victory countrey caſtelles brutians whyche almoſt dyſtroyed already nowe ye ſay italye ſhalbe daungier departynge hen praye may p licinius conſull whyles ſay lynge thyther ſtaye hoſte anniball nowe ſmall power aſwell thou q fabius dyddeſt ſlaye conquerour ouerranne italy yt ſhall greate honour romayns eternal ſame among kinges ſtrange nation haue courage defend italy alſo enter make warre affrica ſhame ſhal ſhall ſayde anniball enterpriſed act romayne capiteyn euer durſte enterpriſe contention betwene v carthaginenſes sicilia nauies army oftentimes inuaded affrica howe contention italy betwene v affrica remaineth quiet peace nowe let italy take reſt peace whiche long tyme hath ben vexed let affrica ſeaſon ſuffer bournynge ſpoylynge waſtyng let puiſſaunt romayne army approche walles carthage rather ſhould bulwarkes fortifycations defende ennemies owne walles let affrica henſeforthe place warre let feare flieng ſleing waſtynge fyeldes dyſtructions belongynge warre nowe tourned thyther whiche ſpace xiiii yeres hath inuaded countrey ¶ aunſwere scipio greate ſtryfe altercacion ſenate houſe laſte decreed sicipo thyrty ſhyppes ſhulde go sicilia thence pleaſure yf thoughte moſt conueniente common welthe ſayle ouer affrica cō ſul kepe warre countrey brutians againſt anniball beſydes theſe ſhyppes romayne legyons whiche appoynted scipio many city cuntreys adioyning rome willingly ayded ſhyppes vii thouſande ſouldiours thinges neceſſarye owne coſtes charge whiche noumbre arriued sicilia deuyded theim companyes appointynge euery company hundred men amonge al whiche nomber choſe oute thre hunderd mooſt valyant actife yonge men withoute armour kept euer aboute hym knewe pourpoſe mente daie choſe named iii c moſt noble rycheſt yonge gentylmen sicilia whome ſayde ſhould ſayle affrica aſſygninge theym day whiche ſhuld appere theyr horſe armour commaundement troubled theim ſore ſo farre frō home labour land ſea ſemed painful onely theim alſo frendes kinſefolkes daye appointed retorne came bringing theim horſes harneis althinges neceſſary ſaid scipio ſhewed certaine men armes sicilia grudge ſore go inthis iourneye wherefore anye mynd pray ſpeake nowe wil gladly heare moche leauer ye vttered nowe betymes ye ſhuld agaynſt hertes go forth become vnprofitable ſouldiors cōmon welth wherevnto one iii c anſwered truely ſyr yf choyſe election ſhulde woulde go forthe warres well ſayde scipio sence ye haue playnely declared mynde without diſſimulation wyll appoynte one place whome ye ſhall delyuer youre horſe harneyes neceſſarye inſtrumentes warre whome ye ſhall take home youre howſe teache inſtruct exercyſe hym feates warre tyll ſende hym agayne bargaine yong gentylman verie ioyefull delyuerynge appareyll warre toke home reſte three hundred men armes sicilia perceiued companion meane diſmyſſed warre good loue fauour capytayne euery one theym alſo beganne make excuſe deſyred haue scipio appoynte theyre roumes whyche gladdelye dydde meane horſed harneyſed inſtructed three hundred wyllynge romaynes vnarmed horſes harneys knyghtes sicilia withoute anye charge ſtocke cytie rome whyche proued valiaunte menne armes dydde manye noble actes aduauncemente common welth scipio ſerched ſuche ſouldiours warred vnder marcellus conſull wynnyng syracuſa choſe chiefly iudged theim expert aſſaultyng ſcalyng townes caſtelles euen imagined wynnyng great carthage sone ſette menne worke make ſhyppes ſpeede amende repayre olde ſhyppes done ſent c lelius good numbre men affrica ſpoyle robbe waſt ſea coſtes landed nyghte dawnynge daye ſettynge men good order ſpoyled fieldes diſtroyed ſlewe manye affricans whiche loked lyttell ſuche ſodeyn inuaſion ſo longe continued pleaſure eaſe fame deſtruction came anone carthage meſſangers noyſed abrode scipio arriued hadde herde alredy come sicilia ſo ſodeinly taken feare coulde tell certayntie nothynge neyther numbre romaynes theyr ſhyppes feare cauſed theim make moche therof dede citezens carthage meruaylous feare penſifeneſſe beholdynge ſodeyne chaunge fortune late ſo aduaunced theyr army lay gate rome capytaines almoſt ſubdued al italy nowe contrary wiſe loked none ſpoyling theyr countrey beſieginge carthage romaynes conſidered helpe founde theyr citezens menne theyr owne countrey weake nothyng mete warre theyr ſtrength hyred ſouldiours frō partes affrica wauerynge people vntrewe vnſtedfaſt alſo rekened syphax turned ſecrete cōmunication scipio hym maſſaniſſa apparently become theyr ennemye mago tidinges remouing gene goinge italy ioyne hoſte annibals hoſte fame alſo ſtrengthe anniball waxed faynte ¶ hole conſydered theyr wofull ſtate condition began ſenatours counſayle prouide helpe theyr preſent neceſſitie muſtered theyr men citie without hyred many ſouldiours affricans vytayled theyr citie amended theyr ſhippes prouided harneſſe thynges nedefull ¶ thus buſy true tidinges came capitayne scipio arryued lelius certayne ſhyppes menne come robbe ſpoyle countrey onely great reſt army yet sicilia theſe newes ſomewhat comforted deuyſed ſende embaſſadours syphax prince aboute theim ſure aliance frendſhyp ſent alſo phillip kyng macedonia promyſynge hym great ſummes money inuade eyther italy sicilia great hoſt italy alſo meſſangers ſent cauſe capitayns annibal mago ſtay scipio italy mago ſente xxv longe ſhyppes vi fotemen viii c horſemen vii elephantes greate plenty money hyre mo men thoſe party willyng ſtrengthe remoue towardes citie rome ioyne hoſt annibals preparation made carthaginenſes ¶ ſhippes carthage arriued gene founde mago army nauy ſhyppes knowyng mynde carthaginenſes called great numbre frenchemen liguriens vnto whome ſhewed ſent thoſe party purchaſe theim lybertie delyuer bondage wherin hadde longe ben holden declared alſo liuius sp lucretius laye theyr two romayne army farre one hetruria fraunce whoſe power reſyſt neded haue great aſſemble people frenchemen aunſwered theyr hertes myndes holly ſerue hym therin ſayd hoſt romaynes redy theyr countrey whiche dyd perceyue mago ayded theym wolde incontinent waſt deſtroy theyr countrey wherfore deſyred liguriens might helpe hym nothynge ſo nere daunger wolde priuely helpe hym vittayles thynges neceſſarye beſte theyr power wherunto liguriens agreed deſyred two monthes ſpace aſſemble take muſters theyr beſte ſoudiours ¶ marcus liuius herynge mago gathered gether ſo great numbre people remoued hoſte fraunce ioyned hym ſelfe sp lucretius lyinge euer awayte mete mago ſo ſone remouynge liguriens wolde offer entre italye take iourney towardes rome caſe mago wolde reſt angle mounteynes without procedynge lyke wyſe wold abyde arminius euer redy defence italy ¶ complaynt lortenſes ſenatours cruell gouernaunce pleminius cap lxi maſſaniſſa hearynge arriuaile romayne army affrica ſmall numbre horſemen cam lelius complayned moche ſlowenes scipio hadde tyme ben affrica great power conſyderinge lowe ebbe carthaginenſes broughte vnto alſo ſeynge syphax buſyed warre prynces adioynynge vnto hym ſayde knew ſuerly brought owne purpoſe good effecte leiſer ſettle owne buſynes wolde obſerue promiſe bonde made romains lyttle good faythe knewe hym wherfore deſyred lelius moue ſtyrre scipio make haſt thyther wolde fayle although dryuen owne realme mete hym ſoone landinge good numbre bothe horſemen fotemen ¶ morowe lelius departed ſhippes loded theyr pray landed sicilia found scipio declared mynde meſſage maſſaniſſa wherupon ſhortly ſet forwardes affrica hearde comforte wynnynge locres citie vttermoſt parte italy holden carthaginenſes whiche citie ſhorte tyme obteyned partly treaſon certayne carpenter wrought caſtell partly fauour citezens therof beinge greuouſly opreſſed amylcar capitayne carthaginenſes garriſon ceaſſed vſe kyndes oppreſſion ouer laſt conſented receyue romaynes towne whiche brought paſſe scipio returned sicilia leauynge behynde hym q pleminius capitayne towne garryſon ſufficient kepinge ſame whoſe departynge pleminius ſouldyours farre paſſed amylcar carthaginenſes pride auaryce vyces ſeemed ſtroue ſhuld ouercome feates armes ſhuld excede vice ſpared nother men wiues maiden doughters exercyſed cruell rapine men goodes ſpoilyng temple wherof citizen beynge wery ſent meſſage complaint scipio conſul whervpon eftſones came locrus al matter debated length punyſhed certayne theim empryſonmente departed leauynge ſtyll q pleminius capitayne leſſe auctority fore departed pleminius wyllinge execute malice ouer ennemies put certayne theym cruell deathe whiche complayned conſull ſouldiours alſo afterwarde cruell vnrulye therfore ſent legate rome greuous complaynte ſenate manyfolde iniuries hurtes cruell paynes ſuffered moche romaynes euer hadde carthaginenſes whoſe complaynte beynge well delyberately herd ſenate quintus fabius replete olde malyce agaynſt scipio ſet forthe neglygence inquired legate whether neuer time ſhewed cauſe conſul scipio aunſwered firſt complaynt herd matter putting tribune pryſon let pleminius go libertie put auctority although worthy puniſhement ſecond complaynt made legate ſo buſied aboute ſetting forewardes ſhippes men affrica could attend examine matter gret reproch ſpoken scipio many prince ſenate ſpecially q fabius alleged born corrupt diſtroy al warlike policy lernyng ouermoche ſufferāce giuing libertie would haue pleminius brought rome bound scipio called frō prouince laſte ſentence q metellus toke place whiche good ſend pleminius according mynde fabius touching scipio whole citie fyrſte choſen youth capitaine spayn according theyr expectation delyuered hole countrey handes ennemies whervpon alſo late choſen hym conſull ſubdue affrica deliuer italy anniball thought meete ſuche noble man ſodainly condemned cauſe duly herd debated haue called frome iourney without greatter cauſe conſideringe locrenſes could lay defaut scipio ouermuch ſufferance pleminius wherfore thought beſt pomponius ii tribune ſhuld ſent locrus frō then sicilia examyne trie whether wronges done locrēſes wer done cōmandement aſſent p scipio caſe conſentyng therto ſhuld cōmand returne rome legate occupy place el ſhoulde continue purpoſe iourney affrica appoynted ¶ according ſentence pomponius ii tribune legate came locrus makyng proclamation yf man wold accuſe pleminius scipio mā ſhulde come theim ſhuld well herde locrenſes gyuyng great thankes romaine goodnes therin ſhewed anſwered wold accuſe pleminius chief doer miſchief certain touching scipio nothynge charge hym withal eyther gaue ouermoch credēce pleminius litell faith wordes ſayd knewe wery well wronges theim done neither wyll commaundement scipio thought hym nature many men ſory wronge offence ſhulde committed yet whan iniuries done haue hertes willes reuenge puniſhe offender ſame ¶ aunſwere pomponius moch eaſed inquirie scipio matter wher fore toke pleminius xxx complices founde gyltie dyuers greatte offence ſente bound rome pleminius dyed priſon sone wer put condigne execution thought go scipio ſee whether ſclaunder ſpoken ſlouthe gouernaunce myſorder hooſte true myght therof make true reporte whan returned rome ¶ scipio hearyng coming cauſed army repayre syracuſa lay alſo cauſed nauy ſhyppes ſette furthe ordered poyntes though ſhulde ſame day haue fought carthaginenſes bothe water lande whan pomponius embaſſadours come gentilly louingly receiued ſhewed army land array redy fight nauy alſo ſea ſhewed onely redy battaile makyng ſhew fight hauen ledde garner corne armory ſtore houſes ordinance artillary inſtrumentes warre ſeing al prouiſion order ſtriken great admiration hym conduict iudgyng gouernance army carthaginenſes ſhoulde ouercome elles neuer poſſyble theim ſubdewed wherfore deſyrynge goddis proſpere welle iourneye departed frome hym takynge theyr waye rome greatte ioye though goinge brynge tydynges rome victory rather report meruaylouſe preparation towarde battayle whiche hadde ſeene sicilia whanne came ſenate howſe extolled fame actes scipio ſuche ſorte ſent hym worde incontinent departe towardes carthage takynge wolde leauynge behynd hym defence sicilia certaine pleaſure ¶ king syphax marieth daughter aſdruball ſendeth letter scipio willing abſtein warre affrica aunſwere dyſſimulation scipio vnto ſame scipio arryueth affrica hooſt cometh maſſaniſſa ca lxii vvhyles romaynes made great ordynance warre carthaginenſes fearing greatly coming scipio prepared moche coulde theyr defence ſtrengthe wherfore plucke syphax amitie romaynes aſdrubal ſonne giſgon made haſt fyniſhe maryage betwene syphax daughter fayre mayden kynge inflamed loue made haſt alſo maried aſdrubal beſides particular aliance made newe general bonde amitie betwene hym carthaginenſes greate ſolempnitie othes takynge promiſynge faythfully friendes ennemies one ſhulde alſo friendes ennemies neuer leſſe aſdruball remembringe promyſe amytie kynge one made scipio lodged palais knowynge mutabilitie vnſtedfaſtnes thoſe barbarous nation fearynge leſte scipio one arryued affrica bande mariage wolde lyttel worthe therfore whyles loue feruent betwene kyng daughter greate deſyre daughter alſo fayre entreatynge cauſed kynge ſende embaſſadours scipio sicilia letter gyuynge hym warnynge ſhulde vpon truſte promiſe hym made kynge ſayle ouer affrica aduertiſynge hym maryed daughter one aſdruball carthage scipio mette palaice arriued affrica furthermore ſayde greate leage amitie people carthage wherfore deſyred hym romaynes wolde warre carthaginenſes farre carthage haue done heretofore ſhulde nede preſent theyr battailes caſe scipio wold forbeare affrica lay ſiege carthage coulde leſſe fighte defence countrey affrica gotten borne brought vp defence countrey wyfe father family ¶ theſe letter came meſſangers citie syracuſa scipio parceiued contentes ſame ſhuld haue great lacke kynges helpe buſines affrica yet ſet forth countenaunce kepynge ſecrete cauſe theyr coming tyll ſent home agayne kynge letter wherin moued neuer breake promiſe one made ſwarue faith amitie made romains wherof goddes witneſſes meſſangers wer departed letter scipio fearing leſt ſoudiours wold muſe moch deuiſe alſo cauſe comynge ſayd meſſangers hyde ſayd cauſe put courage diſſembled matter callinge men gether ſayde ¶ sir nowe ful tyme v depart henſe affrica without tarieng kinges friendes haue ſent vnto v inſtantly deſiring v make ſpede fyrſt maſſaniſſa came lelius complaining greatly tractynge tyme nowe syphax hath alſo ſent vnto v marueylynge tary ſo longe deſiringe wyll eyther ſhortlye come ouer el caſe otherwiſe minded certifie hym writing therupon maye prouyde hymſelfe countrey wherfore ſens althinges redy matter requireth haſt intende leade mine army nauy partes lilibeus ſoone wether ſerueth depart fauour god towardes affrica ¶ theſe wordes ſpoken ordered al thynges departynge ſoone came ſayde porte hoſt ſhyppes alſo met nomber whereof ſo greatte hauen ſuffyſed conteine theym citie coulde receyue men certainte nombre wrytars agre wherefore wyll let paſſe ſemeth nomber men greatte achyeued ſo greatte enterpryſe ſo gret prouiſiō made iiii c ſhippes charged men vitailes ordinance neceſſary cariage beſides xx great long ſhippes wherof scipio ſelfe l scipio brother toke gouernance xx like ſhippes vnder rule c lelius admyrall ſea whiche xl great ſhippes thus deuided ſailed euer ſydes iiii c wafters defence theyr vitayles cariage euery ſhyppe alſo cauſed vittailes freſhe water xlv dayes wherof meate wolde ſerue xv dayes redye ſodden rawe gaue commaundement al ſouldiours kepe peace ſylence theyr ſhyps troublynge ſhipmen ſhulde redy al ſayd ſhypmen deſyred nede requyred great numbre ſhippes mē departed day folowyng euery one xl long ſhyppes beinge appointed haue nyght ſeaſon one lyght euery one iiii c laden ſhyppes u lyghtes capitaynes chiefe ſhips ſpeciall marke knowlege thre fayre lightes mornynge ſoundinge trumpet veſſelles ſet forth good order scipio hym ſelfe departynge made praier openly audience many peple maner ¶oye goddes goddeſſes whiche inhabite rule gouerne ſea lande humbly beſeche ye graūt thynges haue done ſhall may turne honour welthe citizen rome ye wyll aydynge aſſiſtinge procedinges ennemies beinge ouer come maye ſafe ſounde returne home houſes laden pray gotten ſpoyle ennemies graunt ye alſo may haue power ſo vnto people citie carthage haue intended citie rome ¶after theſe wordes ſacrifice cuſtome vſed departed wynde good ſhorte ſpace toke fyght lande within foure dayes brought vpon coſt affrica scipio ſeinge great mounteyne rocke lienge vpon ſea inquired mayſter ſhyppe name mountain anſwered named mount beaute ſayde scipio lyke name lucke therof well nexte hauen therto ſet v lande armye landed get nexte hylles whervpon pitched theyr tentes encamped ſelues inhabitantes ſea coſtes coū trey great feare trouble perceyuynge arriuaile ſo great nauy euery man fled thoſe party takynge theyr wynes theyr chyldren ſubſtance driuinge cattell nexte ſtrong townes great feare countrey newes therof brought specially carthage ſuch feare ſorowe trouble inuaded people though theyr citie ben redy taken theyr ennemies vnprouyded bothe men warre alſo good capitayne gouernour beſt capitayne aſdrubal ſonne byſgon scipio diuers battelles spayne put flyghte laſt droue cleane oute spayne helper ſoo eſtemed capitaynes farre vnlyke armye carthage vnlyke romayne hoſte greate feare gate citie ſhutte walles kepte watche warde thoughe theyr ennemies ben already come walles towne fyue hundred horſemen alſo ſente forthe eſpye conduite romaynes chaunce mette manye romayne horſemen ſent robbe ſpoyle fieldes adioynynge put flyghte greate loſſe many carthaginenſes ¶sone arriuaile romaynes came maſſaniſſa scipio bryngynge hym ii c good men well horſed power greate ben driuen chaſed owne realme baniſhed ſtrengthe owne countrey whoſe comynge verye ioyfull comfortable romaynes carthaginenſes loſſe theyr horſemen aſſembled againe newe winge horſmen wherof made gouernor hanno ſon amilcar ſent letter legate aſdruball come ſuccour citie pointe beſyeged ſent alſo kyng syphax deſyring come ſocour defence carthage alſo affrica lay romaine nere vnto citie vtica hanno hauyng iiii horſemen came towne salera xv mile romain campe scipio knowlege therof ſent maſſaniſſa certayn horſemen hym ſhirmiſhe gate commaunding ſo ſone multitude ennemies one come forth coulde longer endure theyr ſtrength ſhuld ſoftly withdrawe ſelfe towardes hylles ſhuld fynde hym hoſt redy ſuccour inſtructiō maſſaniſſa departed rode gate citie ſkirmiſhing ſuch ſaid gate ny came forth battayl without good order maſſaniſſa faining ſelfe afraide ſomewhat reculed ſometime turned fought folowed thus played baſe tyll whole multitude horſemenne come furthe yates ſobrely withdrewe ſelfe tyll came hylles hilles romayne horſemen couertely come maſſaniſſa fierſely retourned aſſayled ennemies romaine beinge freſſhe ſelues hauyng freſſhe horſes compaſſed aſſailed almoſte weery chaſing maſſaniſſa ſo fyrſt brunt hanno ſelfe • horſemen hym ſlayne reſt fledde wherof romaynes chaſe ſlewe toke ii amonge wer many noble men citie carthage pray victory greatte towne taken capytains men armes welle rewarded scipio aboue gaue maſſaniſſa great gyftes leauynge ſufficient garriſon towne hoſte remoued thenſe ſendynge moche pray whiche taken bothe men beaſtes rycheſſe certayne ſhippes sicilia intendyng hym ſelfe aſſayle citie vtica power whiche yf myght one wynne reckened reſtyng place tyl reſt voiage acheued ¶ thus town vtica beſieged round hope haue ſuccours aſdruball aſſembled togyther xxx fotemen iii horſmen neuer leſſe numbre aſdruball durſte ſette furthe carthage tyll kyng syphax alſo come hym fyfty thouſande footemen x horſemen ſet forewardes came nere vnto vtica pytchinge tentes campe farre romayn army came aboute tyme sicilia sardinia great plenty wheate vitaile romaine ſo therof great plenty alſo brought thither xii c gownes xii cote ſouldiours prouiſion made thynges lacked theſe actes scipio affrica ſommer ¶ duryng whych ſommer p sempronius conſull italy fought anniball romayns worſt loſte xii c theyr men ſoone sempronius ſent p licinius proconſull come hym armye whoſe cōmyng theyr power beinge ioyned together went towardes anniball beynge ioyefull laſte victory foughte theim agayne greate loſſe aboue iiii men ſlayne iii c taken anniball beynge greately dyſcomforted loſſe retourned thence croton sone tyme choſyng conſulles come whiche cn seruilius cepio cn seruilius geminus create conſulles officer choſen according olde cuſtome diuers city alſo brutiens conſentia pandoſia ſubmytted theym ſelues retourned agayne romaynes ¶ scipio wiſely eſpieng maner ennemies campes nyght burneth bothe putteth syphax aſdruball flyght great loſſe theyr men make agayn newe fylde eftſones diſcomfyted put flyghte cap lxiii winter drewe nere gret hoſtes lay encamped farre vtica yet scipio neuer ceaſſed beſiegynge towne campe ſyghte ennemyes mynd ſtyll vpon buſynes touching warre amonge care deuiſed greatly meanes myght wynne king syphax carthaginenſes iudgyng heate loue yonge wyfe tyme ſomewhat aſſwaged werye pleaſure loue beinge thoughte ſatisfyed therin contentation legate aſſaied mynde kynge made aunſwere wolde intreate peace betwene romains carthaginenſes vpon condition romaynes ſhulde departe cleane affrica carthaginenſes lykewyſe italy without trouble orelles wolde fayle purſue warre partie carthaginenſes theſe condition scipio nothynge pleaſed neuertheleſſe truſtinge communication matter haue aduauntage ſerche trewe knowledge ſtate ennemyes throughe common entercourſe eyther partie others campe fayntly refuſed thoſe condition wherby ennemies myght take ſome hope achieuinge theyr purpoſe wynter houſes campes carthaginenſes made wodde bowes ſuche coulde get together numidiens lodginges couered flagges redes laye within theyr campe without order many alſo choſynge theyr owne place without aſſignemente laye withoute campe dyches whiche beinge ſhewed scipio gaue hym comfort hope lodginges ennemies pollicie myghte ſet fyre wherfore euerye tyme ſente embaſſadours kynge syphax entreate peace parfectly aſſured • rewe ſtate thynges euer ſent certayne witty fellowes army diſguyſed habite fourme ſlaues commaundinge while embaſſadours buſy theyr communication ſhulde ſtraye abrode partes campe ennemies marke well entree iſſues campes ſyte faſcion ſtacion lodginges well carthaginenſes numidiens quarter ſette howe farre kynges campe diſtante campe aſdruball maner theyr watche warde bothe nyghte daye ¶ matter thus dyuerſe tymes debated betwen two counſayles romaynes parfecte ſtate theyr ennemies theyr order legate scipio ſayde vnto kynge commaunded neuer returne vntyll brought determynate aunſwere eyther peace warre deſyrynge hym eyther gyue aunſwere therof hym ſelfe take counſayle aduyſe aſdruball carthaginenſes therupon make theyr aunſwere nowe hye tyme knowe eyther oone withoute tryfelynge forthe tyme thus syphax toke aduyſe aſdruball aſdruball noble menne carthage eſpyes leyſar viewe ſerche thynges charged scipio hadde tyme prepare mete ſerue purpoſe numidiens alſo carthaginenſes truſtynge euer peace neglygente foreſeinge aduoydynge daungiers warre prepared theyr myſchiefe laſte aunſwere made romaynes woulde haue peace theyr condition indifferente whiche deſyred wheruppon scipio hauynge good occaſion honeſtlye breake truſe betwene theim taken morrowe ſente worde kynge ſyns perceyued man wyllynge haue peace hym ſelfe therefore kynge then forthe ſhulde truſte haue noo peace romaynes onleſſe wolde leaue amitie carthaginenſes tyme truſe expyred ſprynge yere come wherefore scipio brynge pourpoſe aboute aſſembled gether ſhippes furniſhed theim ordynaunce artyllery though woulde aſſayle vtica ſea coſte alſo ſente two thouſande men warre kepe hyll vtica whiche laye vnkepte dydde two purpoſes fyrſte drawe myndes ennemies ſuſpection whiche deuyſed occupy contrary worke secondly power defende campe excurſions citezens caſe wolde iſſue whyles power gone syphax aſdruball dydde open vnto maſſaniſſa certayne mynde doo nyghte folowynge commaunded tribune euenynge folowynge ſhulde brynge forthe hoſte fyeldes accordynge commaundement aboute ſonne ſettynge ſette forthe ſtandardes banner begynnynge nyghte hoſte ſet forwarde arraye ſo mydnyghte hadde gone vii myles come nere campe theyr ennemyes scipio deuyded army ii partes one parte numidiens appoynted lelius maſſaniſſa wyllynge inuade campe kynge syphax ſet fire lodginges made bowes flagges hartely prayinge bothe nyght apply theyr buſineſſe great dilygence ſayde ſo ſone myghte perceyue fyre kynges campe wolde alſo aſſayle campe aſdruball ¶ accordyng commaundement purpoſe achieued incontinent fyre put vttermoſt partes houſes fyre anon toke drye ſtyckes flagges ranne one houſe ſo ſhorte ſpace abrode euery parte campe numidiens kynges hoſte parceyuinge fyre ſtryken ſodeyne great feare bycauſe chaunced nyght ſeaſon yet nothynge miſtruſtinge cauſe therof aryſe throughe ennemies iudginge come throughe ſome negligence euyll fortune ranne partes helpe ceaſſe quenche fyre without armour weapon nowe maſſaniſſa whiche knewe wayes entree kinges campe ſoo laide numidiens embuſhmētes people ran abrode quenche fyre fel company theyr ennemies er knew meanes many ſlaine many alſo wer burned theyr beddes fyre watche carthaginenſes campe aſdruball parceyuinge great fire kynges campe awaked reſt hoſte alſo deceyued thought fyre hapned negligence deuiſe theyr ennemies herynge greate crye theyr companye kynges hoſte ſlayne whiche thought came onely throughe ſodeyne feare fyre happened nyghte ranne together companyes vnarmed gate theyr campes next way takyng onely ſuche thynges wherwith myght quenche fyre romaynes receyued came flewe euery one none eſcaped beare tydynges therof scipio incontinent inuaded campe fyudynge gate ther vnwarded entred armye ſet fyre lodginges diuerſe partes whiche ſpreadyng abrode ſhort ſpace burned therin bothe man beaſte ſtuffe ſuche wold haue fledde daunger fyre ſlayne ſwerde romaynes ¶ thus one tyme bothe campes wonne neuertheleſſe bothe capitaines eſcaped xx fotemen v c horſemen wherof manye wounded hurte fyre ſlayn burned night xl beſydes taken aboue vi thouſand many noble men carthage whereof xl ſenatours greate ryche praye horſes armure thynges moche valure whiche diſtributed amonges ſouldiours kynge certayne hym fledde owne countrey ¶ aſdruball great ſpeede mightcame carthage founde citie ſoore troubled greate feare iudged scipio leauynge aſſault vtica wolde incontinent victory come aſſault ouercome carthage determined haſt aſſemble newe hoſt citie countrey theim alſo ſent meſſangers kynge syphax require hym would gather power healpe defende bothe countrey theyrs whervnto yonge wyfe muche moued hym pyteouſly wepyng deſyred hym ſuffre father countrey diſtroyed citie carthage bourned romaynes late bourned kynges tentes father legate carthage alſo ſhewed hym good fortune comminge towardes arryued late iiii men warre celtiberia countrey spayne whyche hyred comme ſuccours aſdruball woulde fayle ioyne hym full noble armye whome kyng gaue gentyll aunſwere ſayinge woulde aſſemble put armour luſty yonge men realme ſayde knewe well ouercome fyre battayle wherefore woulde neuer accompte hym ſelfe vanquyſhed oneles ouercome ſubdued fielde ſtrength power anſwere meſſangers departed ¶ ſhortly accordyng theyr appoyntement aſdruball kynge mette togyther army betweene bothe xxx men scipio herynge theyr newe comming agayne hym power lefte ſayde vtica ſmalle numbre people bothe ſea lande hym ſelfe greatte power went mete ennemies pitched campe playn fielde farre kynges campe lyghte ſkyrmyſſhes made betweene horſemen bothe partes ſpace iii dayes fourthe day capitaynes prepared theyr hoſtes battayle ¶ scipio ſet ſpearemen front battayle behynde whome beſt aſſured ſouldiours footemen ſet theyr ayde ſuccours ryghte wynge horſemen italy lefte wynge maſſaniſſa numidian horſemen ¶ ſide aſdruball againſt wynge italyan horſmen ſet numidian againſt maſſaniſſa ſet carthaginenſes middes newe ſouldiours celtiberia thus beinge ordered battailles ioyned fyrſt encountre winges carthaginenſes numidian driuen backe numidian rude vntaught men armes noothinge able reſyſte romain horſmen neither carthaginenſes alſo vnexpert feates warre able withſtande maſſaniſſa fierſe terrible ioy late victory wherfore wynges beinge thus put flight poore army celtiberians remained alone naked deſtitute helpe refuge flie durſte beinge vnknowen cuntrey knewe place whither flie ſaued taken looked grace scipio hand ſeinge came owne cuntrey affrica fight againſt hym ofte tymes good frende wherfore compaſſed ennemies ſlayne one vppon without pitie while al men buſy theim syphax aſdrubal tyme eſcape night beinge ſo nere moche ſafegarde ¶ feare carthaginenſes great ouerthrowe friendes ſeing scipio army ouer ryding countrey rounde aboute theim winning city townes vnder ſubiection penne write tunge expreſſe loked euery houre whan theyr citie ſhoulde enuyronned ennemies fortifyed walles broughte vytayles endure lenger ſpace prepared thynges neceſſarye conſulted beſt theym agreed meſſangers ſhoulde ſent letter anniball commaundyng come carthage power ſocours ¶ certayn ſenatours gaue counſel good nombre ſhippes furnyſhed men ordenance ſhuld ſodeinly inuade romayne hoſte nauy lay reſt vtica myſtruſtynge ſhulde fynde ſhyppes neglygently kept wherby ſmall peyne myghte oppreſſe theim theſe two pointes ſenators agreed ſhippes ſette furthe letter alſo ſent anniball scipio retournynge battayle leadynge cariyng hym ſpoile pray many townes wanne ſent ſayde praye priſoners campe vtica hym ſelfe came tunnes whyche found void men warre fled battayle left town without garriſon takyng towne scipio gladde well naturally ſtronge reaſon ſyte therof beſyde ſurely fortifyed induſtry man alſo place ſo commodyouſe pourpoſe dyſtaunt carthage twelue myles yet frome thenſe myghte welle ſee citie carthage alſo ſea bette walles towne ¶ whyles romaynes caſtynge trenche fortifiynge towne tunnes perceyued nauy carthaginenſes ſaylynge towardes vtica scipio leauyng woorkes made haſte men towardes vtica come healpe ſhippes lay ſiege therof came arryuing carthaginenſes trifled tyme ſea beinge feare ſet enterpryſe ſo scipio prouyded well defence ſhyppes coming neuer leſſe moche trouble fyght ſea toke vi romayn ſhyppes returned carthage ſmall ioy made ſmall gayne ¶ syphax maketh new fialde lelius maſſaniſſa taken priſoner men put flighte maſſaniſſa taketh citie cirtha haſt marieth sophonisba wyfe kinge spphax cap lxiiii morowe battaile fought kyng syphax eſcaped declared scipio ſent lelius maſſaniſſa romayn horſmen lyghteſt harneiſſed footemen alſo numidian folowe kyng aſdruball while went wynne townes countrey adiacent carthage within xv dayes came numidia whoſe coming people therof called maſeſuli receiued gladly maſſaniſſa deliuered hym whole realme theyr ryghtfull kynge whoſe cominge ſo longe deſyred expellynge cleane city fortreſſes therof garnyſons syphax ſoo glad kepe hym within bondes owne realme harte ſwelled diſpleaſure wyllynge reuenged whervnto wyfe father moche intyced hym prycked hym forwardes hadde great plentie men alſo horſes whyche moche encouraged hym make newe fielde wherefore aſſembled many thoughtable gyuyng theim horſes harneys diuydynge horſemen footemenne companyes appoyntynge theim capitaines accordynge learned romaynes thus hauyng thinges redyneſſe marched towardes ennemies great hooſte almoſte newe ſouldiours yonge men warre whan came nere hoſt romains fortified campe anone certayne horſemen iſſued badde baſe nother numbre romayne horſemen ſoo beaten retourned agayne company anon reſcued numbre company thus diuers iſſuynges helpynge euery part theyr company beyng either aſhamed angrye theyr driuynge backe battayle beganne quicke bothe partes ſo laſt hole companyes horſemen bothe partes come fieldes noumbre kynge syphax hoſte come ſo thicke bataile romaynes fayne recule put worſe romain legyons fotemen come theyr ſuccours whoſe comynge kynges people muſynge theyr order maner fyghtyng began ſtay laſte dryuen backe began flee syphax wyllynge withholde people flyght beganne exhort abyde manfully fyght ſhewynge vnto theim bothe ſhame alſo ieoperdye woulde enſue theyr flyinge ¶ whyles rode fielde comfortyng people hapned come nere company romaynes horſe ſtryken downe ſlayne vnder hym taken alyue brought lelius people fledde faſte myght came citie cirtha whyche chiefe citie realme menne ſlayne battayle v aboute ii v c taken ſayd maſſaniſſa lelius nothynge pleaſant hauyng nowe victory viſite father kyngdom long exyle haue recouered time ſuffre v ceſſe enterpriſe wherfore ye wil ſuffre take hors men kyng alſo nowe priſoner goo cirtha ſhall fynde euery man ſoo ſuppriſed feare ſhall ſoone wynne ſmal reſiſtence ye fotemen may come ſmall iourneys eaſe ¶ diuyſe lelius aſſented maſſaniſſa horſemen haſted tyll came walles citie cirtha called certaine towne deſired haue certain noble mē citie come furth ſpeake hym done moued gentylly yelde vp citie knowing takinge king wiſe wold perſwaded ſubmit ſelfes romains cauſed maſſaniſſa king syphax brought bound priſoner pitifull ſyght citezens partly feare partly truſtyng therby obteine fauor maſſaniſſa romains opened yates citie maſſaniſſa leauyng fyrſt gate wals furniſhed people thintent none citie ſhuld eſcape great ſpede rode kinges palaice fyrſt entre found sophoniſba wife syphax daughter aſdruball carthage abode coming gate palaice whan ſhe eſpied coming amonge great route men armes ſhe iudging partly goodly armure partly riche apparaile kyng ſhe fell knee hym ſayd goddis thy ſtrength thy good fortune 〈…〉 full power v ſo euer ſhall • pleaſure neuer leſſe praier poore woman •• take place lord hath power lyfe deth humbly beſeche royall maieſtie wherin late alſo wer loue name people cuntrey numidia appertained syphax loue alſo goddis place whō deſire ſend better proſperus coming hither thā gaue syphax departing hen thou wilt graunt thy priſoner ſo euer thy pleſure ſhal refuſe ſo thou ſuffre come cruell proude dominion romayne leauer auenture yelde power numidian one borne myne owne countrey affrica handes ſtranger vnknowen howe moche daughter aſdruball carthaginenſe borne hath cauſe feare hande romayne caſe thou canſte none otherwiſe helpe deſire mooſte hartily require ſteame thus deathe delyuer daunger romaynes ¶ quene excellent beautie luſty flouriſhyng age humble behauiour fayre ſpeche ſo perſuaded king maſſaniſſa toke mercy alſo hauyng victory hole citie becam ſo captiue loue takig right hand promiſed requeſt thervpon mounted kinges palaice began dyuiſe
