ſpecially battayle caſe thou vanquiſhe v battayle thou ſhalte wynne ſo moche glory profyte aboue thou mayſt haue v peace thou ſhalte loſe caſe fortune turne agaynſte one houre fortune maye ouerthrow longe ſpace hath ben gotten alſo loked whiche ye truſte haue nowe thy power ioyne thynges gether peace p cornelius come tryall muſte bothe take ſuche fortune goddes wyll ſende amonge exaumples felicitie marcus attilius may well remembred one arryued ſame countrey affrica wynning victorye vppon forefathes carthaginenſes denyed graunt peace inſtantly required hym laſt coulde meaſure felicitie moderate fortune ſo hyghly aduaunced hym therfore fall fowler howe moch hygher eleuate proſperitie belōgeth aſketh peace hym gyueth peace appoynte condition peace knowlegyng defaulte wyl appoynt ourſelues condigne puniſhemente ſame refuſynge leaue vnto poſſeſſion ſuche countreys whiche warre beganne sicilia sardinia spayne iles within ſea betwene italye affrica carthage beinge contented affrica onelye ſenſe hath ſoo pleaſed goddes wyll ſuffer enioye empyre dyuerſe ſtraunge countreys dominion gotten bothe ſea lande paraduenture aſkynge peace heretofore ye haue bene playnelye iuſtely delte withall whiche cauſeth myſtruſte faythe promyſe carthaginenſes therin touchyng obſeruynge peace taken moche conſydered perſons peace required haue harde tolde scipio father heretofore denyed carthaginenſes peace perſones came intreate therfore ſmall dignitie eſtimation nowe doo anniball requyre peace whiche woulde deſyre onleſſe thoughte profytable ſame profyt demande ſame wyll alſo ſtyll kepe conſerue haue endeuoured ſelfe man ſhoulde forethynke hym warre begunne thorough mine occaſion like maner ſhal nowe enforce ſelfe none ſhal repent peace ſhall take oration finiſhed scipio made thervnto aunſwere ¶ anſwere scipio oration anniball battaile thervpon betwene wherin anniball vanquiſhed put flyght ca lxx knewe ryght well anniball truſte thy comyng home made carthaginenſes breake truſe betwene v taken alſo let hope peace thou doeſt denye thy ſelfe thou nowe withdraweſt v thynges requyre alſo graunted treatiſe peace ſaue onely thoſe countreys wherof haue alredy poſſeſſion wherfore thou doeſt labour thy citezens may feele burthen diſcharged ſo muſt trauayle noo parte whyche haue promyſed ſhall nowe withdrawen remayne vnto theim rewarde vntrouth conſyderyng ſame theyr vntrouthe hathe made theim vnwoorthye haue condition peace theim offered neyther dyd father fyrſte make warre sicilia nowe spayn dangier wherin mamertines frendes fellowes put nowe diſtruction sagunt cauſed v iuſtly make warre hath bene prouocation thou haſt cō feſſed thy ſelfe goddis alſo witneſſes gaue ſuche ende firſt warre right behoued haue warre haue gyuen doubt wil giue like end part conſyder well bothe infirmitie man power fortune know actes ſubiect chance knowlage caſe thou woldiſt haue come deſire peace toke ſo grettrauaile come affrica thou haddeſt thy good wil departed thine army italy denied thy requeſte might well haue iudged haue wrought proudely ſtubburnely euen ſo haue drawē thy power home affrica thou arte redy make v reſiſtence ſeinge peace truce one taken whiche ye haue broken taking ſhippes force tyme truce violatinge embaſſadours may ryghte well honour byd prepare warre ſens could hold contented peace whan ye thus without agrement peace ii capytaines brake communication departed euery one company determining try matter battail take ſuche fortune goddis wolde gyue theim ¶ ſoone come campes openly bothe partes gaue commaundement ſouldiours make redy fyght theyr laſt battaile wherby ca dyd ouercome ſhulde haue felicitie one day euer next nyght ſhuld know whether rome carthage ſhuld haue ſuperioritie onely italye affrica worlde whiche ſhulde rewarde nowe hym ſhuld haue victory contrary part peryll ieoperdye leſſe declared part whiche ſhulde haue worſe battayle romaynes hadde place whether flye beinge ſtraunge countrey carthage muſte nedes come vtter diſtruction caſe laſt army refuge vanquiſhed ouerthrowen ¶ great ieopardy next day ii valyant capitaynes two moſt noble rycheſt people ſette furthe ii myghty army intendynge day eyther increaſe honour whiche gotten el ouerthrowen loſe hoope feare myngled bothe togyther theyr myndes whan ſawe theyr owne battaile battayle ennemies conceiued myndes ioye ſorowe ſouldiours fayled remembre theyr capitaines declared vnto theim greate warnynges exhortation anniball reherſed people theyr actes done italy many romayne capytaynes howe many armyes hadde ſlayne scipio ſhewed conqueſtes spayne alſo late affrica confeſſyon ennemyes feare conſtrayned requyre peace although theyr vntrouth wold ſuffre theim kepe ſame whan wherfore geſſed goddis appointed theim fyght bataile lyke ſucceſſe lucke whā fought yle egates ſayd warre trauayle end ſpoyle carthage euen hande whyche ye ſhall retourne home countreye youre parentes wyues chylderne owne goodes theſe comfortable woordes ſette furthe ſuche geſture bodye merye countenaunce though hadde al redy hadde vyctory ennemies afterward putte men order firſt ſpearemen chiefe mooſte aſſured footemen greate multitude togyther ſtandarde ſmalle bandes whyche ſhoulde certayne ſpace diſtaunt one intent elephantes theyr ennemyes myghte come betweene ſayde bandes receyued theim without breakynge arraye theſe voyde ſpaces betweene ſayde bandes appoynted dyuers lyghteſt harneyſed ſouldiours ſtande fulfyll voyde place commaundynge theim whan elephantes preſſed theim ſhuld recule behynde ſayd bandes whyche array el ſteppe among thoſe went ſtanderdes right hande left hand giuing way vnruly beaſtis entre amonge men weapon myght wounded ouerthrowen lefte wynge ledde lelius italyan horſemen ryghte wynge ledde maſſaniſſa numidian ¶ anniball part forefront battaile ſette elephantes whyche numbre lxxx whome put ordre ſuche nation hyred came ſuccour liguriens frenchemen men iles named baleares called maiorque minorque myngled amonge great numbre moore ſeconde battaile ſette carthaginenſes affricanes legion lacedemonians ſent thither ſuccours carthaginenſes philip kyng macedome within lyttell ſpace theim placed italian cam whan left cuntrey winges wer horſemen left winge helde numidian horſemen right wynge carthaginenſes hoſte annibal wer men diuers nation cuntreis diuers tunges langages alſo different lawes armour aparaile euery one theſe gaue ſundry diuers exhortation either feare comfort ſuche come ſuccours promyſed great rewarde pray whiche ſhulde wonne induſtry trauaile liguriens promiſed plentiful reward fertile pleaſaunt fieldes italy moore numidian exhorted well feare leſte ſhulde el greuous ſeruitude maſſaniſſa frenchemenne wer ſet naturall hatred bare romaynes carthaginenſes put remembrance fight walles naturall cuntrey propre goodes ſepulchres elder child parentes trembling wiues meane way ſayde put betwene hope feare either muſt ſuffre miſerable ſeruitude diſtruction citie cuntrey orels obteine empire worlde ¶ tyme noble capitayn finyſhed wordes romaynes blewe vp theyr trumpettes horne makynge ſo terrible noyſe clamour greate numbre elephantes beinge furyouſe tourned backe vppon theyr companye ſpecially vppon lefte wynge moore numidian whiche perceyued well maſſaniſſa wherefore alſo inuaded ſame wing horſemen putting theim ſuche feare fledde leauynge ſyde hoſte bare ſuccour dyuers elephantes force wer conſtrained entre myddle battaile whome anone lyght armed ſouldiours gaue place ſuffryng theim entre among theim thruſt ſpeares innelyns ſo many ſlain lelius horſmen aſſailed right wing horſmē carthage puttig thē alſo ſlight ſo body hoſt ſides left without defence horſmē winges chaſed away thā began battel fotemen ſtrōg partes great wer cry wer made roman wer better corage ſtronger hope ſtrēgth wherfore ſhort ſpace cauſed enmies giue back certain ſpace groūd whā thei ons gotē ſome grounde theyr ſhyeldes targettes came ſtill thruſting theyr ennemies bearing backe tyl ſome ſone fyrſte battayle tourninge theyr backes began flie came ſecond battayle carthaginenſes moore wolde ſuffer entre leſte ſhulde cauſe theyr arraye broken wherfore betwene theyr owne fellowes began great debate ſlaughter ſoo carthaginenſes conſtrayned fyghte bothe theyr owne vnruly felowes alſo romaynes theyr ennemies neuertheleſſe wolde wyſe receyue theyr felowes fledde amonge leſte ſhulde mengle fearefull ſorte whiche flyghte hurte wounded amonge earneſtly bent fight whiche myght haue turned moche theyr dyſpleaſure dryuing away heapes compelled go gether ſome one ſide theym ſome abrode fieldes great occiſion made ſo moche romaynes coulde come fyghte carthaginenſes fyrſte muſte peyne go ouer dead body ſlayne scipio cauſed troumpet blowen withdrawe men firſt battayle ben ſore traueyled many ſore wounded theſe cauſed ſtand behinde rereward made ſame rerewarde beſt men auaunce forewarde vpon carthaginenſes beganne battayle newe agayne whiche ſore fierſe came romaynes moſt aſſured ſtrongeſt men moſt expert warres beinge vanquiſhed twyſe nowe lothe aſhamed vanquiſhed romaynes farre moin noumbre taken great courage dryuinge awaye bothe wynges alſo forewarde theyr ennemies ¶ whyles thus foughte ſeconde battayle lelius maſſaniſſa returned theyr horſemen chaſe wynges carthaginenſes power violence came backes ſeconde battayle carthaginenſes whiche buſy valiauntly fought able endure theyr violence force put flyght ſlayne partes day ſlayne taken carthaginenſes aboute xl men many elephantes many ſtandardes noble men taken battayll great alſo praye ſpoyle founde campe romanes toke brought ſhippes romaynes alſo loſt battayle aboue x men anniball fewe fledde adrument neuer departed field til bothe battayle aſſayed aſmoche poſſyble done ſafegard people wherin day prayſe bothe scipio al expert men warre romains ſpecially ordering battayl fyrſt ſet forefront great nomber elephantes whoſe gret ſtrength intollerable violence ſhuld breke arraye romaine putting order whyche halfe wynnynge battail ſet foremoſt hyred ſouldiours diuers nation intent ſuch confuſed nombre ſtrangers fought great faith loue onely money ſholde haue place tyme flee battayle alſo intent ſuche ſtrangers ſhuld endure fyrſt violence ennemies makyng wery weake chiefe men moſt truſt ſhould haue thyng theim carthaginenſes affricans moſt truſtie ſouldiours laſt al good ſpace behinde theim placed italiens people whome knew wel whether ſhuld friendes foe thus pollicie wolde ſerue hym yet ſtrengthe coulde helpe fledde ſayd adrument thenſe ſent come carthage whyther came xxxvi yere departynge thenſe beinge chylde open aſſemble noble men citie confeſſed hym ſelfe vanquiſhed none hope ſafegarde obteyninge peace ¶ condition peace graūted carthaginenſes scipio ratyfyeng ſame ſenate ca lxxi scipio hoſte comynge ſhippes laden ryche praie worde brought hym p lentulus arriued vtica l ſhippes warre c hulkes laden maner prouiſion wherfore scipio thynkinge put citie carthage feare al partes fyrſt ſent lelius rome beare newes victory ſent cn octauius lande towarde carthage army horſemen fotemen while takyng hym bothe newe nauy ſhyppes brought hym lentulus alſo olde nauye wente ſea vtica towardes hauen carthage whyle ſailed ſea ſhippe carthage met hym couered white lynnen clothe full bowes oliue token peace whiche ſhippe x embaſſadours prynces carthage ſente mynde anniball deſyre peace ſhyppe come fore parte scipiosſhip coueringe taken awaye legate ryght humbly required hym extende mercy pitie vpon aunſwere none giuen ſhoulde come hym tune place ſayde wolde remoue campe aunſwere departed wente nauy ſhippes carthage partely viewe ſituation towne partely make inhabitantes ther afraide ſmal ſoiourninge departed frome thenſe returned vtica thenſe goinge tune ſodeine newes wer brought vermina ſonne syphax great numbre horſemen fotemen comyng ſuccours carthaginenſes encountre theſe people scipio incontinent ſente good parte fotemen hoſt horſemen metynge theim theyr fyrſte reencountre put flyght ſtoppinge paſſages wherby myght fleinge eſcape ſlewe numidiens xv toke aboue xii c many horſes countrey numbre xv c peyne capitayne hym ſelfe eſcaped hauynge ſmall numbre hym thenſe campe pytched tune olde place ſet thyther came xxx noble men carthage embaſſadours ſent vnto scipio moche lamentation done required peace scipio conſtrained therunto contrarietie fortune late ouerthrow friende vermina lykewiſe herde leſſe pitie bicauſe theyr late vntruthe rebellion ſo moche thought moſte men citie carthage myghte iuſtely worthely deſtroyed theim ſo ben dede one thynge ſpecially moued scipio contrarye whiche newe conſull comynge thyther whoſe deſyre haue honour fame victory fyniſhinge warre whiche achieued scipio traueile great daungier cauſe scipio counſaylours wer fully minded take peace carthaginenſes wherefore nexte day called legate carthage greatly rebukinge vntrewth diuers time ſhewed wyllynge theim nowe laſt beinge taughte good experience regarde bothe theyr goddes theyr othes ſhewinge hauing pitie deſtruction theim theyr ſoo noble citie contented graunte peace vpon theſe condition fyrſte ſhoulde lyue free theyr owne lawes cuſtomes enioyinge ſuche city townes affrica hadde poſſeſſion warre betwene theim taken frome daye forthe romaynes ſhulde deſtroye ſpoyle parte therof agayne carthaginenſes ſhulde reſtore romaynes ſuche perſons fled runne away romayns priſoners romains theyr friendes captiuite alſo ſhoulde delyuer theim theyr ſhyppes warre ſhyppes excepte onely galeys hauynge thre order oores piece ſhoulde alſo delyuer vp theyr elephantes whiche alredye tamed made apte warre neyther ſhulde tame moo agayne ſhoulde moue warre affrica withoute affrica lycence commaundemente romaynes furthermore ſhulde reſtore vnto maſſaniſſa ſuche thynges hadde taken makynge peace agrement hym alſo yelde vnto romayne hoſte wheate wage vnto return legate rome beſydes ſhulde paye x talentes ſyluer fyftye yeres durynge whiche tyme ſhulde yerely paye ſumme deuyded euen portion paymente wherof perfourmaunce theſe condytions ſhoulde delyuer hym c pledge owne election wherof none ſhuld vnder thage xiiii yeres neither aboue thage xxx vpon theſe condition agreed giue truce ſo wolde delyuer hand ſuche hulkes ſhyppes burthen fraught implementes carthaginenſes toke theim duringe laſte tyme truſe graunted theim elles ſhulde neither loke truſe peace ¶ whan legate come carthage cō maunded declare ſame condition peace openly congregation people therevnto aſſembled againſt condition one gyſgo noble man carthage ſpake ſore wold haue diſſuaded people taking peace whoſe ſayinges many vnruly multitude gaue good audience annibal therwith greatly moued went force drewe downe place violent facion bene vſed citie thought dyuers contrary libertie citie people free libertie ſpeake opinion annibal vſed facion warres peaſible vſe citie remembrynge liberty therof excuſed rudeneſſe maner whan departed citie ix yeres olde whiche nowe xxxvi yeres agone time haue ſufficiently knowen inſtructed feates warre beinge taught chaunces fortune euen frome chyldehoode wherfore beynge diſvſed ſoo longe ſpace frome lawes maners cuſtomes citie although doo forgette liberty vſes therof leſſe blamed thus hadde excuſed folye perſwaded people takynge peace howe neceſſary nowe theim alſo howe reaſonable condition conſyderynge theyr preſente eſtate whiche perſwaſions greatteſt parte multiude agreed reſiſters agaynſte greately blamed greateſt doubte howe myghte make reſtitution taken frome romaynes tyme truce ſpoyled goone neyther knewe badde theym onely ſhyppes hulkes remaygned concluſyon worde ſent agayne scipio ſame legate wold receyue condition peace coulde knowe goodes wer hulkes wold pay therfore owne iudgement veſſels men ſhulde reſtored ¶ thus truce gyuen citie carthage thre monethes commaundement duryng time truce ſhulde ſende embaſſadours place rome caſe embaſſadours ſent frome place carthage ſhuld wyſe depart then vntyll romayne capitayne aſcertayned cauſe theyr comming ¶ soone went legate carthage rome ſent c veturius philo martius valla lucius scipio brother p scipio romayn capytayn ¶ come thyther l veturius philo declared howe scipio hadde foughten anniball ouercome carthaginenſes theyr vtter confuſyon makynge nowe ende dolefull longe warre betwene romaynes theim alſo vermina ſonne syphax power beaten ouercome whyche newes ſenatours beinge meruaylous ioyfull commaunded hym publyſſhe ſame gladde tydynges whole multitude citezens makynge greatte ioye gaue thankes vyctory goddis wer legate carthage broughte ſenate whan ſenatours behelde age dignitie grauitie ambaſſadours mooſte noble menne citie carthage iudged intended playnely ſyncerely intreate peace amonge theſe noble carthage one aſdruball called hedus one chiefe theim bothe auctoritie nobilitie euer deſyrous peace held moche agaynſte anniball affinitie aſdruball ſayde fewe couetous perſonnes citie culpable warre comminaltie faultes whyche layde theym excuſed ſome confeſſed leſte denying myght worſe hearde ſenate perſwaded senatours vſe theyr proſperous fortune gentylly due temperance profeſſynge euer caſe carthaginenſes would haue folowed myndes hym hanno takynge tyme whan offered beene gyuers peace vppon ſuche condition nowe gladde take others handes ſayde ſeldome ſene good fortune good mynd gyuen one men cauſe conqueſtes romains euer chiefly hath proſperitie ye haue remembrance conſulte thynges come empyre hath bene encreaſed gentylnes fauour ſhewed nation ye haue vanquyſhed hath bene victory gotten theim ¶ aſdruball finyſſhed oration ambaſſadours made moche lamentable propoſitions bewayling miſerable fall ſtate carthaginenſes greatteſt lordes honour worlde nowe conſtrayned abyde encloſed within walles citie hauyng nothing el myghte clayme propretie ye ſame citie helde vpon goodnes forbearyng romaynes while theyr pleaſure forbere vtter diſtruction therof theſe humble gentyll woordes ſenatours vniuerſally fully inclyned peace one ſenatours ſpake loude voyce peace graunted carthaginenſes goddis ſhall ſweare make peace whan haue broken promiſe deceiued goddis ſware whan laſte toke peace v ſayd aſdruball anſwered euen ſame goddis wyll ſweare ſo angry reuenged v brake oure laſte truſe leage herevpon ſenatours comons inclyned peace determined thaduiſe x legate rome p scipio ſhulde make theim peace vpon ſuche condition ſemed beſt legate wer named made theim redy depart carthaginenſes whiche ambaſſadours gaue greate thankes ſenate theyr goodnes theim ſhewed deſyryng departyng licence theim entre citie viſite certayne frendes kynneſmen kepte citie priſoners whiche requeſte graunted theim deſyred alſo myght redeme diuers theim vpon reaſonable raunſom cōmaunded write name ſuche wolde haue redeemed named ii c theim incontinent delyuered x legate take theim affrica scipio wyllyng caſe peace went forwardes carthaginenſes ſhoulde rendre theſe ii c pryſoners carthaginenſes free without payinge raunſome theſe thynges beynge ſo concluded carthaginenſes romayne legate departed towardes affrica whan cam scipio concluded peace hym vppon condition ſpecified ſhyppes carthage elephantes fugitiues priſoners numbre iiii delyuered scipio among whome one terentius culleo notable ſenator rome ſhyppes vpon deliuerie theim furth ſea numbre v c al ſortes commaundement scipio ſet fyre bourninge ſorowfull ſyght carthaginenſes ſene whole citie carthage fyre ¶ scipio teturneth rome greate triumphe ioye people cap lxxii thus ended warres betwene romaynes carthaginenſes gentylly thoughte ſhulde haue done scipio dyuers tymes reported conctouſe hyghe mynde fyrſt claudius nero cu cornelius deſyrynge honoure vyctorye carthage cauſe citie carthage vtterly diſtroyed waſted ſayde peace thus taken money whyche ſhulde preſently payde romaynes greuous carthaginenſes whoſe ſtocke common ſubſtaunce greatly waſted reaſon longe contynuall warres wherefore leuyinge ſayde ſumme theyr pryuate ſubſtaunce greate lamentation wepinge made citie whiche anniball beholdynge coulde forbeare laugh wherat aſdruball hedus toke great indignation rebukynge hym beynge verye origynall cauſe al theyr ſorowe common mournyng citie ſhulde ſo laugh thervnto anniball aunſwered ye myghte beholde inwarde thoughte mynde ye maye outwarde apparent countenaunce face ye ſhulde parceiue laughter come ioy herte madneſſe freneſie neuer leſſe laughter ſo inordinate cometh ſo time teares ſhuld haue wept armour taken frō ſhippes burned eies libertie makinge warres ſtraunger onely lycence romaynes taken frome wherin reſted chiefe vndoinge greatteſt falle ye fele hurte oneleſſe touche priuate welthe great hurte common welthe ye neyther fele regarde ennemies greate ſpoyle vyctorie carthage remayned alone naked without armour defence among ſo many armed men affrica man wepte mourned nowe ye muſt pay tribute owne priuate goodes euery man wepeth ye wolde burienge friendes feare ſore ye ſhall ſhortly perceyue ye wepte leaſte harmes worſt behinde ¶ peace thus cōcluded betwen romains carthaginenſes scipio calling people together beſides reſtored vnto maſſaniſſa father kyngedome alſo gaue citie cyrtha townes groundes wonne syphax afterwarde cauſed cn octauius delyuer cn cornelius newe conſull nauy brought sicilia cauſed embaſſadours carthage go towardes rome haue thinges confirmed auctoritie senate whiche auctoritie romayne legate concluded ¶ thus thynges beinge peace ſea lande army toke ſhippynge ſayled ouer sicilia thenſe italye met men countrey great honour ioye ſo gladde euery man bothe peace victorye poore men townes city waye went towarde rome ran forthe ſe hym prayſe hym thus greate honour came rome receiued citie mooſte noble triumphe enryched citie greate ſ • mmes golde ſyluer prayes taken beſyde diſtributed amonge ſouldiours xl li conqueſt whiche made affrica called scipio affricanus euer great honour familie ſucceſſion ¶ anniball fleith ſea antiochus kynge siria antiochus moueth warre romaynes l cornelius scipio ſayleth aſia fyghteth antiochus vanquiſheth hym graunteth hym peace vpon condition returneth rome cap lxxiii warres thus ended affrica carthaginenſes continued peace certayne ſeaſon laſt ennemies annibal worke diſpleaſure ſent worde rome ſenate anniball pryuely ſente meſſangers letter antiochus kynge siria mouynge hym warre romaynes alſo meſſangers ſente letter ſecretely antiochus anniball certifieng mynde annibal ſuche coulde neuer contented till harde ſounde harneis vpon mennes backes romaynes beinge angry therat ſent legate thither c seruilius claudius marcellus terentius culleo try whether information made true commanding publiſhe abrode cauſe theyr coming determine certaine matter controuerſie wer betwene carthaginēſes king maſſaniſſa none ¶ tale publiſhed beleued true common people anniball therwith could blinded knewe full well onely cauſe theyr comminge wherfore thynkinge ſeaſon gyue place till time might better ſerue hym ii departed oute citie begynninge night ſtraungers apparaile came place apointed horſes mete thenſe ſpede wente caſtell owne ſea ſyde ſhip italy awaited hym apoynted ſame purpoſe whiche ſhyp ſayled affrica arriued ſame day ile circyna makynge dole way harde chaunces happed countreye dydde owne euyll fortune hauen circyna founde many ſhyppes laden marchaundyſe landinge greate reſorte people ile came vnto hym ſalutynge hym makynge comynge great ioye anniball fearynge leſte ſome thoſe ſhippes nyght ſhuld departe hauen ſhewe affrica ſene hym circyna deuiſed make ſolemne ſacrifice great feaſt badde al maiſters ſhyppes hauen marchauntes ſame wether hot middes ſommer cauſed al ſailes ſhips croſſe maſtes wherunto ſayles faſtened broughte lande w • erwith made pauilions bowres defende theym vehement heate ſonne whyle ſouped ſhore feaſt ſumptuous tyme might ſerue therto kept ſolempnely wine great plenty wherwith many drunken heuy headed bankette alſo purpoſely prolonged tyll farre nyght fell marchauntes ſlepe maryners alſo whiche anniball eſpienge thoughte good tyme mocke takynge ſhyppe ſecretly departed leauynge faſte ſlepe morowe maryners aroſe heuy heades caryed theyr ſayles tackelinges agayne ſhyppes preparynge thynges redy myght bryng al paſſe ſpent good parte nexte daye ¶ morowe departyng anniball carthage friendes vſually reſorted company coulde fynde hym hym gathered great multitude citie together market place inquiringe newes coulde ſhewed chiefe ruler theyr citie coniectured fledde away feare conſpiracie againſte romaynes ſayde romaynes ſome crafty traine conſpired deathe thus dyuerſe tale accordynge diuerſitie ſectes citie tydynges ſone brought thyther ſene circyna romayne legate openly ſenate carthage founde greate lacke blamed greately citezens ruler ſuffryng hym departe conſyderynge priuie letter meſſages ſente betwene antiochus ſaying wolde neuer ſatiſfyed tyll hadde moued warre throughe worlde carthaginenſes excuſed theym ſelues affyrmynge nothyng priuie conſentynge departynge ¶ annibal arriued tyrus receyued honorably great ioy ſoiourned certaine day thenſe ſayled antioche epheſus founde king antiochus great doubte comynge maner ſhulde mainteygne warres againſt romayns kyng greatly comforted meane coming alſo beinge embaſſadours etholiens whoo ſame tyme wer departed amitie romaine determined moue warre agree wolde certaine condition peace romaine preſcribed vnto whiche thought ſhuld greatly loſſe honour alſo dominion wold haue cauſed hym leaue poſſeſſion certayne city alſo ſhuld medle grece ſhulde moue warre determyned anniball greatly fauour chieifly thought expert man mete counſaylour affayres agaynſt romaynes anniball euer opinion ſhulde make warre italy countrey italy able furnyſhe army vitayles thynges neceſſary alſo ſouldiours ſhulde haue nede men armes tyme ſayde warre moued italy ſoo romaynes maye haue hole power therof make warre region italy prynce nation worlde able withſtande romaynes wherfore ye wyll delyuer vnto one c ſhyppes warre xvi thouſande fotemenne one thouſande horſemen wyll power ſayle affrica truſting cauſe carthaginenſes rebel agaynſte romaynes caſe wyll folowe requeſt yet wyll inuade ſome part italy moue warre romaynes maye ſayde kyng reſt power ſayle europe kepynge armye grece redy ſet forwardes ye ſe cauſe ¶ counſeyle well allowed kinge wherevppon one ariſton epheſien wyſe truſtie manne choſen ſayle carthage friendes anniball priuie ſpeciall token mouthe whiche knewe wer true feyned ſhewe vnto theim purpoſe writinge durſte ſende none feare takynge meſſangers meſſage onely declared vppon credence ¶ whyle aryſton went meſſage therin hadde good ſpede ambaſſadours rome come epheſus knowe antiochus cauſe intended ſuche warre agaynſt romaynes among whiche ambaſſadours ſayd p scipio called affricanus one whiche ambaſſadours hauyng knowledge kyng antiochus lyttell gone agaynſte piſidians fyndyng annibal diuers time reſorted vnto familyar communication onely intent make haue good opinion romaynes myſtruſte thyng intended theym agaynſte among communication betwen ambaſſadours annibal remembred scipio demaunded whome iudged moſt noble capitayne euer knewe hearde whome anniball aunſwered alexander macedony ſmal power ouercame ſo many nation vanquiſhed ſo many greate army battayle traueylynge ſo many ſtraunge farre cuntreis whiche paſſed power witte mannes cumpaſſe scipio demaunded hym iudged ſeconde moſt noble capytayn aunſwered pyrrbus moſt wyſe expert man placinge campes fortifieng fortreſſes watche ward getting hertes men vnto obeyſaunce ſoo muche warred italye italyens gladder vnder gouernaunce beynge ſtraungyer vnder dominion power romaynes demaunded scipio whome thoughte thyrde withoute fayle ſayde ſelfe whych aunſwere scipio laughed ſayde wouldeſt thou haue ſayd caſe thou haddeſt ouercome battayle haue done treuly ſayde anniball woulde haue putte myſelfe bothe alexander pyrrhus alſo aunſwere ſeemed scipio ſtraunge proude whereby mynded take scipio al glory ¶ durynge longe taryenge romayne legate epheſus nothynge el wrought often metynge communication theym anniball made kynge ſuſpecte myſtruſt whervpon called councel ¶ agayn one thoas etholien deſirous haue kyng power arryue grece withoute partynge ſame ſtrengthe ſayde vnto hym syr greatte citie demetrias part city grece loke daylye commynge thyther agaynſte arryuayle ye ſhall ſee countreye aſſemble ſeaſyde ſo ſone may watch perceyue nauy comynge ſea touchyng parting ſhyppes power wyſe allowe caſe ye mynded ſo anniball men moſt vnmete haue rule gouernance therof ¶ fyrſt ye muſt conſyder ſaid thoas annibal carthaginens outlaw baniſhed man frō cuntrey whoſe crafty witte wyl imagyne dayly newe deuyſes euen fortune dothe varye ſhall fall brayne agayne yf ſhoulde chaunce annibal looſe nauie men vanquyſhed loſſe wil leſſe capitayne loſte theym caſe ſhoulde happen hym haue vyctorye honour therof ſhall wholly abyde anniball antiochus furthermore fortune ſo well ſerue anniball vtterly ſubdue romaynes ye thynke continue ſubiection whiche cuntrey culd ſuffre ſelf obedience nay ſaid youth hath euer coueted minde emperour hole world age neuer contented vnder rule may choſe wherfore coūſayl ye haue nede make annibal capitain pleaſe ye may vſe cōpany frēd iourney takīg aduiſe affayrs prudēt counſailour none otherwiſe ¶ crafty vntrew coūſail thoas turned kīges mynde cleane frome ſendynge anniball army affrica thoughte moſt mete neceſſary wherfore prepared ſayl grece help etholiens wanne certayn citi • laſt conſul atulius army romains came ſocors frendes great mounteyne whiche paſſethe throughe myddle grece fought antiochus put flyght ſleyngal hoſt except onely v c fled kyng ¶ whiche diſcomfiture antiochus annibal ſmalle nomber men lefte hym battaylle cam ſee toke ſhipping came epheſus remayned thynkyng ſelfe ſure oute daunger romayns perſwaded beleue many gladde pleaſe mynd many ſuche diſſemblers haue beene ſhall dayly greatte prynces onely anniball aduyſed kynge prepare commynge romaynes ſayenge meruayled already arryued rather commynge myghte loked shewynge alſo romayns ſtronge valiant vpon ſee land doubtyng ſhortely wold ſtriue dominion aſia eyther muſte take theim empire el ſhuld dangier loſe kyngdome knewe deſire ruler ouer worlde counſelynge loke none thyng handes caſe ſhuld deceiue ſelf vayne falſe hope ¶ long beginnynge warres grece l cornelius scipio c lelius chooſen conſulles whiche election p scipio affricanus offered ſenate caſe would grant brother l scipio countrey grece prouynce would gladly take payne go iourney wherunto ſenate agreed geuynge alſo auctoritie go aſia thought expedient sayenge woulde nowe proue whether antio • hus ſhould holpen counſayl anniball vanquyſhed romain conſull army help scipio made great conqueſt affrica army ſhippes made ready conſull arriued grece ſone receyuing many rebell city handes thenſe ſayled aſia licence kynge philyp paſſage throughe macedony trace kyngdome antiochus ¶ dyuers battaylles foughte vppon ſea betweene romayne nauy polixenidas capitayne kynges ſhyppes euer romaynes victory help kyng eumenes alſo rhodiens laſte chaunced ſoonne scipio affricanus taken priſoner brought antiochus kepte honorably gentelly afterward truſtyng haue frendſhyp p scipio healpe peace made betwene romaynes ſente home ſonne withoute payeng raunſome perceyued romaynes approche ſo nere vnto thought better common peace battayle truſtyng haue eaſy condition peace moued tyme matter came communication betwene conſulle kynges embaſſadours condition peace ſo ſore antiochus refuſed take theim althoughe thervnto perſwaded letter p scipio affricane wherevpon bothe partyes prepared theim fyghte battayle cruel laſt kyng antiochus put fiyght liiii footemen ſlayne horſemen iiii beſydes iiii c taken pryſoners ſmall loſſe romayns ſent antiochus eftſones embaſſadours conſull peace lengthe meanes p scipio affricanus graunted vpon theſe condition ¶ fyrſte ſhoulde frome thenſe foorthe make warre europe alſoo ſhoulde leaue poſſeſſyons city landes countreyes whyche ſyde greatte mountayne called taurus agayne ſhoulde paye romaynes fyftene thouſande talentes xii yeres pay vnto king eumenes iii hundred talentes great quantitie wheate vpon theſe condytions ſhoulde haue peace prouyded anniball authour warre thoas dyuerſe capytaynes counſaylloures myghte bee delyuered vnto hym kynge beynge extreeme myſchyeffe receyued peace vppon ſayde condytyons putte perfourmance ther pledge ſame peace alſo confirmed ſenate rome ¶ ſo thynges thus proſperouſly brought paſſe l scipio conſull returned rome receyued citie great honour triumphe brother victory affrica named affricanus ſo conqueſtes aſia called aſiaticus honour ſucceſſion euer ¶ anniball fleith pruſias kyng bithynia howe ended lyfe cap lxxiiii anniball battayle begon betwene romains antiochus wherin vanquiſhed fledde miſtruſtinge folowed kynge neceſſitie muſt dryuen take peace whiche feared leſte romaynes bearyng hym mortall malyce wold require delyuerie thoughte prouyde hym ſelfe tyme wherfore incontinent fledde pruſias kyng bithynia longe taryed quintius flaminius ſent rome kynge ſhewinge hym ſenatours thought delte friendly kepe realme theyr great capitall ennemy annibal man made fyrſte owne countrey make warre vtter vndoinge ſame thenſe came antiochus autour alſo warre romaynes nowe repayred vnto hym thought woulde tourne vndoinge pruſias wyllynge gratyfy romaynes deuyſed eyther ſlee hym el take delyuer hym flaminius wheruppon incontinente ſeruauntes kynge alſo flaminius beſette houſe anniball rounde ſo coulde waye iſſue anniball foreſeinge hatred romaynes bare hym ſmall fayth prynces ſpecially lyghtnes pruſias therfore thynkynge haue ſome waye flie daungier nede required deuyſed vii wayes entree houſe wherof certayne ſecrete priuie numbre ſo great men armes whiche houſe watche ſo ſtraightly kept kynges commaundement ſo euer offered iſſue eſpyed embuſhementes harney ••• men 〈…〉 tyme death drawe nere called poyſon whiche longe tyme 〈…〉 hym euer redy ſuche chaunces ſayde nowe wyll delyuer romaynes great thought haue longe tyme taken bringe confuſion althoughe nowe olde yet thynke longe dye deathe bothe flaminius theyr legate ſhal haue ſmall victory blaming deteſtable falſhede pruſias ſo cruelly wolde ſuffer murther friend receyued keping drunke empoyſoned drinke ſone dyed ¶ lamentable ende ryght wyſe noble valyaunte capytayne anniball ſtraunge region exiled banyſhed owne natiue countrey aboute time longe worthye romayne scipio affricanus alſo dyed romaynes manyfold benefites ſhewed recompenced deteſtable ingratitude certayne citie beinge ennemies man authoritie eſcape enuye charged hym olde matier betwene pleminius locrenſes wherin ſayde conſul corrupted money therfore miniſtred iuſtice agayne layde agaynſt hym delyuerye ſonne beinge priſoner antiochus withoute raunſome whiche thoughte ſuſpecious theſe ſmalle cauſes called senate though ben meane perſone put aunſwere extremitie without fauour hauynge reſpecte noble actes done common weale whiche ingratitude toke ſo diſpleſantly departynge court went countreye towne lytarne dwelled long lyued exilynge hym ſelfe rome euer deathe commaunded body buried alſo bone myght reſt vnkynde countrey ¶ thus ii worthyeſt city worlde found vnkynde theyr noble ruler capytaynes one tyme carthage banyſhed anniball vanquiſhed rome exiled scipio vanquiſhed ennemies wherin ſhe twayne blamed ingratitude ☞ finis ☜ ❧ londini ❧ aedibus thomae
